Chapter 6 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Businesses, ch. 18; equipment used in investigations of case of driving under the influence, § 70-2. 
State Law reference- Municipal regulation of alcoholic beverages, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-112; power of city to abate nuisances, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-117 et seq.; intoxicating liquor, malt beverages and wine, Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-1-1 et seq.; local license taxes, Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3A-21; approval of retail license applications by council, Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3A-23. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 6-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Alcoholic beverages; association; beer, or malt or brewed beverages; club; corporation; fortified wine; liquor; liquor store; meal; minor; person; state liquor store; table wine; and wine shall have the meanings respectively assigned to them in Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3-1 et seq. 
    Licensee means any person licensed by the city council to sell liquor, wines or malt and brewed beverages under the terms of this chapter. 
    Lounge means any place or premises operated by a responsible person of good reputation in which alcoholic beverages of any types may be offered for sale but does not meet the requirement for a restaurant-lounge, restaurant-pub, or club as these establishments are defined in this section, and which meets the following additional requirements: 
(1)  A lounge area of at least 1,000 square feet on one floor in one room; such area to be equipped with tables and chairs and capable of seating at least 50 persons. 
(2)  A minimum of five off-street parking spaces shall be provided for each 100 square feet of lounge area, provided that this requirement shall be in addition to the parking requirements for any other uses in the same building. 
No person under the age of 19 shall be admitted on the premises of any lounge as a patron or employee, and it shall be unlawful for any lounge licensee to admit any minor to the premises as a patron or employee. 
    Public place means any place or gathering which the public generally attends, or is admitted to, either by invitation, common consent or right, or by the payment of an admission or other charge, and, without limiting the generality of the foregoing, shall include any theatre or other place of amusement and any athletic contest; provided, however, that such term shall not mean or include premises which have been duly licensed by the city for sale thereon of such beverages. 
    Restaurant lounge means any place or premises in which foods, refreshments and liquor are offered for consumption within the building in which the establishment is located, which is operated by a responsible person of good reputation and which meets the following additional requirements: 
(1)  A dining area of at least 1,000 square feet on one floor in one room; such dining room to be equipped with tables and chairs accommodating at least 50 persons at one time; 
(2)  A kitchen separate and apart from the dining area, but adjoining the dining area, in which food is prepared for consumption by the public and in which the food or meals served in the dining area are prepared; 
(3)  At least one meal per day shall be served at least six days a week, with the exception of holidays, vacations, and periods of redecorating; 
(4)  Such place shall be duly licensed by the ABC board of the state for the sale of liquor for on-premises consumption; and 
(5)  The serving of such food or meals shall constitute the principal business of such establishment, with the serving of liquor, malt or brewed beverages, wines, or other alcoholic beverages being only an incidental part of the business. During any 90-day period, the gross receipts from the serving of meals and food shall constitute more than 50 percent of the gross receipts of the business. 
    Restaurant-pub means any place or premises in which foods, refreshments, and malt or brewed beverages and/or table wines (but not liquor) are offered for sale for consumption within the building in which the establishment is located, which is operated by a person of good reputation and which meets the following additional requirements: 
(1)  A dining area of at least 1,000 square feet on one floor in one room; such dining room to be equipped with tables and chairs accommodating at least 50 persons at one time; 
(2)  A kitchen separate and apart from the dining area, but adjoining the dining area, in which food is prepared for consumption by the public and in which the food or meals served in the dining area are prepared; 
(3)  At least one meal per day shall be served at least six days a week, with the exception of holidays, vacations, and periods of redecorating; 
(4)  Such place shall be duly licensed by the ABC board of the state for the sale of malt or brewed beverages and/or table wines for on-premises consumption; and 
(5)  The serving of such food or meals shall constitute the principal business of such establishment, with the serving of malt or brewed beverages and/or table wines being only an incidental part of the business. During any 90-day period, the gross receipts from the serving of meals and food shall constitute more than 50 percent of the gross receipts of the business. 
    Retail, off-premises, package liquor store means a place at which alcoholic beverages are offered for off-premises consumption which is operated by a responsible person of good reputation and which meets the following additional requirements: 
(1)  Such place shall be duly licensed by the ABC board of the state for the sale of liquor for off-premises consumption. 
(2)  Such place shall meet the following building requirements: 
a.  The building must be separated from any other building by a wall or firewall with no way of entrance to adjoining building. 
b.  There shall be no windows except plate glass windows in the front of building which must be protected by burglar bars or burglar alarm. No drive-through windows will be allowed. 
c.  There shall be no public seating in the building. 
d.  The doors to the building must be metal with dead bolt locks. 
e.  There shall be complete day/night lighting in front and rear of the building. 
f.  All stock must be kept in the same building in which it is offered for sale; it cannot be stored off the premises. 
g.  The front door of the building must be at least 350 feet from a church or school. Except as otherwise provided in Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3-17, this shall not apply to schools or colleges wherein only specialized subjects such as law, stenography, business, art, medicine, dentistry, vocational occupations or other specialized subjects are taught. The distance set out shall be measured by a straight line from the door of the business to the front door of the church or school. State liquor stores and sales of alcoholic beverages shall also be requirements of Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3-17. 
(3)  Cocktail mixes may be sold under this license, but no other license such as for selling snacks, crackers, cakes, etc., shall be combined with this license. 
    Tavern means any place or premises operated by a responsible person of good reputation in which malt or brewed beverages and/or table wines (but not liquor) are offered for sale for on-premises consumption, but which does not meet the requirements for a restaurant-lounge, restaurant-pub, or club. 
(Ord. No. 80-18, § 1, 12-22-1980; Ord. No. 82-04, § 1, 1-12-1982; Ord. No. 94-12, § 1(a), (b), (d)-(o), 4-25-1994) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 6-2. - Prohibited acts. 
(a)  Public consumption. It shall be unlawful for any person to drink, sell, serve, dispense or have in any open or unconcealed possession or custody for drinking any alcoholic beverage in any public place other than a place licensed to sell alcoholic beverages for consumption on premises. Public place shall include but not limited to any motor vehicle on public streets or at public places as well as any "public place" defined by Code of Ala. 1975, § 13A-11-1(2). Public place shall not mean any area in which a city permit or exception has been obtained hereunder and compliance has been obtained with all applicable state and local laws and licenses, specifically allowing alcoholic beverages to be sold, served or consumed. 
(b)  Permitted public consumption. The city council shall be authorized by resolution to temporarily suspend the operation of this section with regard to the controlled dispensing and consumption of beer and table wine upon any public property during any special event conditions as may be prescribed by the council, with the provisions of this ordinance remaining in effect in all other areas of the city. 
    Special events shall be limited to those events of broad public interest which may benefit the city and city's economy by attracting large numbers of visitors, by generating favorable publicity, and by enhancing a marketable image for the city. The definition shall also the private rental of public properties. 
(Ord. No. 80-18, § 1, 12-22-1980; Ord. No. 2009-14, §§ 1, 2, 5-11-2009 ) 
Sec. 6-3. - Penalty for violation of chapter. 
    Any person who shall be convicted of a violation of this chapter shall be punished as provided in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 80-18, § 2, 12-22-1980) 
Secs. 6-4-6-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - OFF-PREMISES RETAIL SALES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Alabama, 1975, § 28-1-5. 

Sec. 6-31. - Application of article provisions. 
    The provisions of this article shall apply to the retail sale of alcoholic beverages for off-premises consumption only and shall not apply to the establishments regulated by article III of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 82-04, § 2, 1-12-1982) 
Sec. 6-32. - Regulation of sale. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the off-premises, retail sale of alcoholic beverages within the city limits or police jurisdiction without first obtaining a license as provided in this article. No person shall be granted a license for the off-premises sale of alcoholic beverages within the city unless such person operates a retail, off-premises, package liquor store, and unless such person is duly licensed by the state alcoholic beverage control board, and unless such person is licensed to do so by the city and conforms to all the regulations provided in this article, and to all regulations promulgated by the state alcoholic beverage control board, and unless such person shall file written application on the form provided by the state with the city clerk prior to consideration of the application by the city council. Licenses shall be granted and issued by the city only to reputable individuals or to associations whose members are reputable individuals or to reputable corporations duly qualified under the laws of the state to do business in the state, and then only when it appears that all officers and directors of the corporation are reputable individuals. 
(Ord. No. 82-04, § 3, 1-12-1982) 
Sec. 6-33. - Levy of license fee. 
(a)  In addition to all other taxes now imposed by law, any person prior to the sale of any alcoholic beverages within the city limits or police jurisdiction and prior to the receiving of a license from the city for such purpose shall pay to the city an annual license tax. Such license tax is fixed and levied and shall be in amounts computed as follows: 
(1)  A basic license fee of $1,000.00 for businesses and $2,500.00 for package liquor stores located in the city limits is fixed and levied, which shall be due and payable on or before January 2 of each year, except that for the first year in which any licensee engages in business, such basic license fee shall be paid prior to the commencement of the licensee's business, and shall be paid annually thereafter. 
(2)  The basic license fee of $500.00 and $1,250.00 for package liquor stores is fixed and levied for a business located without the city limits, but within the police jurisdiction of the city. The time of payment shall be the same as set forth in subsection (a)(1) of this section. 
(3)  Licenses issued after July 1. In any instance where a license provided for in this article is issued to a person not previously licensed under the provisions of this article, on or after July 1 in any calendar year, the license taxes for the remainder of that year shall be in amounts equal to one-half the amounts provided for under subsections (a)(1) and (a)(2) of this section. 
(b)  No license issued under this article shall be issued for more than one premises, nor for separate types of operation on the same premises. 
(c)  This section shall not apply to any state liquor store. 
(Ord. No. 82-04, § 4, 1-12-1982; Ord. No. 2004-02, §§ 1, 2, 1-26-2004; Ord. No. 2006-08, § 1, 4-24-2006) 
Sec. 6-34. - Limitation on sources of supply. 
    No licensees shall sell, offer for sale, give away, or have in possession or custody for any purpose, any liquor which has not been sold by the state alcoholic beverage control board, except that possession or custody, for consumption only, of not more than one quart of liquor purchased pursuant to the laws of a foreign state shall not be unlawful. 
(Ord. No. 82-04, § 5, 1-12-1982) 
Sec. 6-35. - Disposition of seized liquor or wine. 
    Whenever any person shall have been convicted of possession or custody of any liquor or wine contrary to the provisions of this article, and it shall appear that the police department has seized such liquor or wine and has the same in custody as evidence or otherwise, such seized liquor or wine shall be disposed of as provided in Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3-242 et seq. 
(Ord. No. 82-04, § 6, 1-12-1982) 
Sec. 6-36. - Hours and days of sale. 
    It shall be unlawful for the proprietor, keeper, or operator, or the servants, agents or employees of the same, of any café, lunchroom, restaurant, hotel, motel, lounge, pub, bar, or other public place to knowingly permit any person to give away, sell, serve or distribute for consumption on or off premises, or drink or consume any alcoholic beverages on the premises of such café, lunchroom, restaurant, hotel, motel, lounge, pub, bar, or other public place between the hours of 2:00 a.m. Eastern time and 6:00 a.m. Eastern time on Monday, Tuesday,. Wednesday, Thursday, Friday or Saturday of any week, or between the hours of 2:00 a.m. Eastern time and 12:00 noon Eastern time on Sunday of any week, within the City. Any violation shall be punishable as provided for in section 6-81 City of Valley Code of Ordinances. 
(Ord. No. 82-04, § 7, 1-12-1982; Ord. No. 2015-23, § 1, 9-29-2015) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2015-23, § 1, adopted Sept. 29, 2015, changed the title of § 6-36 from "Hours of prohibited sale" to read as set out herein. 
Sec. 6-37. - Employment of underage persons. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to hire, employ or allow any person under 21 years of age to serve, handle or dispense liquor, wine or beer at any place in the city. No one under 21 years of age shall be allowed in the building. 
(Ord. No. 82-04, § 8, 1-12-1982) 
Sec. 6-38. - Frequenting premises where illegal liquors are kept. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to visit or resort to any house, room or other place in the city where prohibited liquor, wine or malt or brewed beverages are kept. 
(Ord. No. 82-04, § 9, 1-12-1982) 
Sec. 6-39. - Sales to certain persons forbidden. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person or for any employee, servant, or agent of any person to sell, or offer for sale, any liquor, wine or beer to any person visibly intoxicated, or to an insane person, or to any underage person, or to any habitual drunkard. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person who operates any business of selling liquor, beer or wine to allow any liquor, beer or wine to be sold to any underage person, or to be consumed by any underage person on the premises where such liquor, beer or wine is sold. 
(Ord. No. 82-04, § 10, 1-12-1982) 
Sec. 6-40. - Purchase or possession by underage person. 
    Except as otherwise provided in Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3A-25(a)(19) or other law, it shall be unlawful for any underage person to purchase, buy or have in his possession any liquor, beer, wine or other intoxicating beverage in the city or in the police jurisdiction of the city. 
(Ord. No. 82-04, § 11, 1-12-1982) 
Sec. 6-41. - Civil penalties. 
    If the basic license fee specified in this article is not paid on or before January 2 of each year (except for businesses initially licensed subsequent to January 2) a penalty of 20 percent shall be paid and added to the amount then due. If any licensee shall fail to make any payment provided for in this article prior to the end of the month in which such payment has become due, then the license for the sale of alcoholic beverages shall be subject to revocation by the city council. 
(Ord. No. 82-04, § 13, 1-12-1982) 
Sec. 6-42. - Other penalties. 
    Any person who violates any provisions of this article or any regulation promulgated by the alcoholic beverage control board relating to the sale of beer, malt or brewed beverages or any provisions of law contained in the Alcoholic Beverage Licensing Code (Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3A-1 et seq.) shall be punished as provided in section 1-11, and the license of any such person shall, upon conviction, be subject to revocation by the city council. 
(Ord. No. 82-04, § 14, 1-12-1982) 
Secs. 6-43-6-70. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - ON-PREMISES RETAIL SALES 

Sec. 6-71. - Application. 
    The provisions of this article shall apply to the retail sale of alcoholic beverages for on-premises consumption and to the retail sales of all alcoholic beverages for off-premises consumption by on-premises licensees, but shall not apply to those businesses engaged solely in the retail sale of such beverages for off-premises consumption, nor to the wholesale sale of alcoholic beverages. Those licenses and ordinances pertaining to the retail sale of alcoholic beverages for off-premises consumption and/or to the wholesale sale of wine and malt and brewed beverages shall remain in full force and effect. 
(Ord. No. 94-12, § 2, 4-25-1994) 
Sec. 6-72. - Regulation of sale of alcoholic beverages. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the on-premises retail sale of alcoholic beverages within the city without first obtaining a license as provided in this article. No person shall be granted a license for such sale of alcoholic beverages within the city, unless such person operates a restaurant-lounge, restaurant-pub, or club, tavern or lounge as defined in section 6-1, or is granted a special retail license as provided in this article, and unless such person is duly licensed by the state alcoholic beverage control board, and unless such person is licensed to do so by the city and conforms to all the regulations provided in this article, and to all regulations promulgated by the state alcoholic beverage control board, and unless such person pays all the license fees levied under this article. In addition, such person shall file written application on the form provided by the state with the city clerk prior to consideration of the application by the city council. Licenses shall be granted and issued by the city only to reputable individuals or to associations whose members are reputable individuals or to reputable corporations duly qualified under the laws of the state to do business in the state, and then only when it appears that all officers and directors of the corporation are reputable individuals. In addition, no license shall be granted under this article if the front door of the establishment seeking such license is within 350 feet from a school or church building. In addition, no license shall be granted under this article until after the required ABC license shall have been duly issued by the state alcoholic beverage control board. 
(Ord. No. 94-12, § 3, 4-25-1994) 
Sec. 6-73. - Levy of license fee. 
(a)  Establishments with liquor licenses. In addition to all other taxes now imposed by law, any person prior to the sale of any liquor, including wines, within the city and prior to the receiving of a license from the city for such purpose, shall pay to the city an annual license tax which is levied in the following amounts: 
(1)  A basic license fee of $1,000.00 is fixed and levied, which shall be due and payable on or before January 2 of each year, except that for the first year in which any licensee engages in business, such basic license fee shall be paid prior to the commencement of the licensee's business, and shall be paid annually thereafter. 
A basic license fee of $500.00 is fixed and levied for such businesses located without the city limits, but within the police jurisdiction of the city. The time of payment shall be the same as set forth in subsection (a)(1). 
(2)  The annual license fee for a club in the city limits shall be $1,000.00 ($500.00 for police jurisdiction), and the special events liquor license fee in the city limits shall be $1,000.00 for each special event ($500.00 in police jurisdiction), not to exceed seven consecutive days. 
(3)  Other license fees. The license fees levied in this subsection (a) shall be in addition to any and all other city licenses required for the operation of restaurants, hotels or motels and clubs established by other license ordinances of the city. 
(4)  Licenses issued after July 1. In any instance where a license provided for in this subsection (a) is issued to a person not previously licensed under the provisions of this article, on or after July 1 in any calendar year, the license taxes for the remainder of that year shall be in amounts equal to one-half the amounts provided for in this subsection (a) under the provisions of subsection (a)(1) of this section. 
(b)  Establishments with beer licenses. In addition to all other taxes imposed by law, every person, prior to the on-premises retail sale of any malt or brewed beverages in a restaurant-pub, restaurant-lounge, tavern, lounge, or other authorized establishment within the city, and prior to receiving a license from the city for such purpose, shall pay to the city an annual license fee which is levied in the following amounts: 
(1)  A flat license fee of $75.00 is hereby fixed and levied, which license fee shall be due and payable to the city on or before January 2 of each year, except that for the first year in which any licensee engages in business in the city, such basic license fee shall be paid prior to the commencement of the licensee's business, and shall be paid annually thereafter. 
(2)  The license fee levied in subsection (b)(1) of this section shall be in addition to any and all other city license fees required for the operation of restaurants or other business establishments by other business license ordinances of the city. 
(3)  Licenses issued after July 1. In any instance where a license provided for in this subsection (b) is due and issued on or after July 1 in any calendar year, for a person not previously and properly licensed under the provisions of this article, the flat license fee only for the remainder of that year shall be in an amount equal to one-half of the amount provided for under the provisions of subsection (b)(1) of this section. 
(c)  Establishments with wine licenses (no liquor license). In addition to all other taxes now imposed by law, every person, prior to the on-premises retail sale of any table wines in a restaurant-pub, tavern, or other authorized establishment within the city, and prior to receiving a license from the city for such purpose, shall pay to the city an annual license fee which is levied in an amount as prescribed in this subsection (c), to be paid in the manner specified: 
(1)  A basic license fee of $75.00 is fixed and levied, which license fee shall be due and payable to the city on or before January 2 of each year, except that for the first year in which any licensee engages in business in the city, such basic license fee shall be paid prior to the commencement of the licensee's business, and shall be paid annually thereafter. 
(2)  Other license fees. The license fee levied in this subsection (c) shall be in addition to any and all other city licenses required for the operation of restaurants or other business establishments by other license ordinances of the city. 
(3)  Licenses issued after July 1. In any instance where a license provided for in this subsection (c) is due and issued on or after July 1 in any calendar year, for a person not previously and properly licensed under the provisions of this article, the basic license fee only for the remainder of that year shall be in an amount equal to one-half of the amount provided for in this subsection (c) under the provisions of subsection (c)(1) of this section. 
(d)  Dual licensing. No license issued under this article shall be issued for more than one premises, nor for separate types of operation on the same premises. Each premises must have a separate retail license. Where more than one retail operation is located within the same building, each such operation under a separate or different ownership is required to obtain a separate retail license; and where more than one type of retail operation located within the same building is operated by the same licensee, such licensee must have a license for each type of retail operation. Where one of such dual operations is a lounge, the lounge operation must be conducted in a separate and distinct portion of the building and must be separated from the other operations conducted in the same building by a solid wall which extends from the ceiling to the floor, or separated by a building story. 
(Ord. No. 94-12, § 4, 4-25-1994; Ord. No. 2006-08, § 2, 4-24-2006) 
Sec. 6-74. - Levy of license in police jurisdiction. 
    Upon every person engaged in the doing of any act, or who shall do any act, or continuing in the doing of any act, or engaged in the operation of any business, or who shall engage in the operation of any business, within the police jurisdiction of the city, but beyond the corporate limits, for which or upon which a privilege or license tax is, in this article, levied or required within the corporate limits of the city, there is levied, in addition to all other taxes of every kind now imposed by law or by municipal ordinance, to be collected as provided in this section for the privilege or license taxes levied within the corporate limits of the city, a privilege or license tax equal to one-half of that provided, levied or required in this article for the doing of such act, or the engaging or continuing therein, or the engaging or continuing in the operation of such business within the corporate limits of the city. Except for the amount of the privilege or license tax levied in this section within the police jurisdiction of the city, but without the corporate limits, all the provisions of this article shall extend and apply to all the area within the police jurisdiction of the city. 
(Ord. No. 94-12, § 4.1, 4-25-1994) 
Sec. 6-75. - Special retail liquor license. 
(a)  Special events. Upon application to the state alcoholic beverage control board at least 120 days in advance of the event for which a license is requested and forwarding such application to the city council for its consideration, the city council may issue a special events retail liquor license for a valid, responsible organization of good reputation for a period not to exceed seven days, and upon such terms and conditions as the city council may prescribe. Such license will authorize the licensee to sell at retail and dispense such alcoholic beverages to patrons, guests, or members of the organization at such locations or areas approved by the city council. The fee for a license for a special event is set forth in section 6-73. 
(b)  Special retail. The city council may issue a special liquor license to a public recreation authority, or the franchisee or concessionaire of a recreation authority, provided that the recreation authority is duly incorporated under the laws of the state. 
(Ord. No. 94-12, § 5, 4-25-1994) 
Sec. 6-76. - Limitations on sources of supply. 
    No licensee shall sell any alcoholic beverages in the city except such as have been purchased from a wholesaler or distributor duly licensed by the state alcoholic beverage control board and by the city, if required, and no licensee shall sell any alcoholic beverages unless all applicable state and local taxes have been paid on such alcoholic beverages. 
(Ord. No. 94-12, § 6, 4-25-1994) 
Sec. 6-77. - Records and reports. 
    Each person licensed under the provisions of this article shall keep accurate records of all sales and purchases of alcoholic beverages made by him and shall file a statement, verified by oath of the licensee or an authorized officer or agent, each month with the city clerk or his designated representative on forms furnished by the city showing the amount of sales of alcoholic beverages for the preceding month. In addition, the following reports shall also be filed: 
(1)  Restaurant-lounge. Each licensee shall report monthly on forms furnished by the city, the amount of gross sales of food and gross sales of alcoholic beverages for the preceding month. Gross sales and purchases of liquor and wine shall be reported on one combined form, and gross sales and purchases of malt and brewed beverages shall be reported on a separate form. 
(2)  Restaurant-pub. Each licensee shall report monthly on forms furnished by the city, the amount of gross sales of food and gross sales of table wine, and gross sales of malt and brewed beverages, and a separate form shall be filed for table wine. Such records required by the provisions of this section and supporting such reports include books of account, invoices, papers, memoranda, etc., which shall be preserved for not less than two years and shall be open to inspection by the city clerk or his authorized representative upon request during regular business hours. Upon written request by the city clerk or his agent, each licensee shall furnish within 15 days from receipt of the written request, invoices, receipts and other documents supporting the licensee's monthly reports and returns required to be filed under this article. If the licensee does not furnish such invoices, receipts and other written documents within 15 days of the written request, the city clerk shall set a hearing before the city council within 30 days, giving notice to the licensee that he shall appear at the hearing to address his failure to comply with the provisions of this article. If the licensee fails to appear or, upon appearing, fails to furnish proof of his compliance, the council shall revoke the license of the licensee issued under this article. 
(Ord. No. 94-12, § 7, 4-25-1994) 
Sec. 6-78. - Assignability of licenses. 
    Licenses issued under this article may not be assigned. The city may authorize the transfer of any license from one person to another, or from one place to another upon proper application being made to the city council; but no such transfer shall be made to a person who would not have been eligible to receive the license originally, nor for the transaction of business at a place for which the license could not originally have been issued lawfully. If 51 percent of the capital stock of a corporate licensee or partnership is sold or transferred to a person or entity not previously an owner of the business and licensee during six months prior to the sale, such sale or transfer shall be deemed as assignment and shall be deemed to terminate the license issued under this article, and shall require a new license to be purchased and issued for the continuation of such business. Every applicant for the transfer of the location of any license issued under this article shall file a written application with the city along with a transfer fee of $25.00. Such application for transfer shall be reviewed by the city clerk and shall be submitted to the city council for its review. 
(Ord. No. 94-12, § 8, 4-25-1994) 
Sec. 6-79. - Required closing time. 
    No restaurant-lounge, restaurant-pub, tavern, lounge, club or other establishment for the on-premises retail sale of wines, liquor and other alcohol distilled spirits, or any combination thereof, shall remain open to the public after the hour of 1:00 a.m. 
(Ord. No. 94-12, § 9, 4-25-1994) 
Sec. 6-80. - Civil penalties. 
    If the basic license fee specified in this article is not paid on or before January 2 of each year (except for businesses initially licensed subsequent to January 2) or if any of the additional license fees specified in this article to be paid monthly are not paid on or before the tenth of the month when due, as specified in this section, a penalty of 20 percent shall be due and payable to the amount then due. If any licensee shall fail to make any payment provided for in this article prior to the end of the month in which such payment has become due, then the license for the sale of alcoholic beverages shall be subject to revocation by the city council. 
(Ord. No. 94-12, § 10, 4-25-1994) 
Sec. 6-81. - Other penalties. 
    Any person who violates any provisions of this article or any regulation promulgated by the alcoholic beverage control board relating to the sale of beer, malt or brewed beverages or any provision of law contained in the Alcoholic Beverage Licensing Code (Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3A-1 et seq.) shall be punished as provided in section 1-11, and the license of any such person shall, upon conviction, be subject to revocation by the city council. 
(Ord. No. 94-12, § 11, 4-25-1994) 
Sec. 6-82. - Construction of article. 
    This article shall be construed as an exercise by the city of the police power of the state, delegated to the city, in the regulation of the traffic in malt or brewed beverages within the jurisdiction of the city, and not as an ordinance enacted for the purpose of raising revenue. 
(Ord. No. 94-12, § 12, 4-25-1994) 
Secs. 6-83-6-100. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - CONDUCT IN ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE ESTABLISHMENT 

Sec. 6-101. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Establishment dealing in alcoholic beverages means any business establishment operating within the city limits or police jurisdiction of the city which sells, dispenses or otherwise allows the consumption of alcoholic beverages on the premises. 
(Ord. No. 91-05, § 1(b), 7-22-1991) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 6-102. - Nudity and sexual conduct. 
(a)  No person shall expose to public view his or her genitals, pubic area, vulva, anus, anal cleft or cleavage, or any simulation of such act in an establishment dealing in alcoholic beverages. 
(b)  No female person shall expose to public view any portion of her breasts below the top of the areola or any simulation of such act in an establishment dealing in alcoholic beverages. 
(c)  No person maintaining, owning or operating an establishment dealing in alcoholic beverages shall suffer or permit any person to expose to public view his or her genitals, pubic area, vulva, anus, anal cleft or cleavage or simulation of such act within the establishments dealing with alcoholic beverages. 
(d)  No person maintaining, owning or operating an establishment dealing in alcoholic beverages shall suffer or permit any female person to expose to public view any portion of her breasts below the top of the areola or any simulation of such act within the establishment dealing in alcoholic beverages. 
(e)  No person shall engage in and no person maintaining, owning or operating an establishment dealing in alcoholic beverages shall suffer or permit any sexual intercourse, masturbation, sodomy, bestiality, oral copulation, flagellation, any sexual act which is prohibited by law, touching, caressing or fondling of the breasts, buttocks, anus, or genitals or the simulation of such acts within an establishment dealing in alcoholic beverages. 
(f)  No person shall cause and no person maintaining, owning or operating an establishment dealing in alcoholic beverages shall suffer or permit the exposition of any graphic representation, including pictures or the projection of film, which depicts human genitals, pubic area, vulva, anus, anal cleft or cleavage, female breasts below the top of the areola, sexual intercourse, masturbation, sodomy, bestiality, oral copulation, flagellation, any sexual act prohibited by law, touching, caressing or fondling of the breasts, buttocks, anus, or genitals, or any simulation of such acts within any establishment dealing in alcoholic beverages. 
(Ord. No. 91-06, § 2, 7-22-1991) 
Sec. 6-103. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Any person violating the provisions of this article shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 91-05, § 3, 7-22-1991) 
Chapter 10 - ANIMALS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Environment, ch. 30. 
State Law reference- Animals, Code of Ala. 1975, § 3-1-1 et seq.; municipal regulation of dogs and cats, Code of Ala. 1975, § 3-7-A-14; animals at large, impoundment, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-110; municipal powers as to health, cleanliness, sanitation, quarantine, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-130 et seq.; cruelty to animals, Code of Ala. 1975, § 13A-11-14. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 10-1-10-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ANIMAL CONTROL 

Sec. 10-31. - Purpose of article. 
    The purpose of this article is to promote harmonious relations in the interaction between man and animal by: 
(1)  Protecting animals from improper use, abuse, neglect exploitation, inhumane treatment, and health hazards; 
(2)  Delineating the animal owner's responsibility for the acts and behavior of his animal at all times; 
(3)  Providing security to residents from annoyance, intimidation, injury, and health hazards by animals; 
(4)  Encouraging responsible pet ownership; 
(5)  Providing standards for any and all persons and agencies, public or private, engaged in confinement, buying, selling, harboring, or dealing in animals in any manner whatsoever within the corporate limits of the city; and 
(6)  Ensuring the physical safety of humans. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 1, 2-14-1994) 
Sec. 10-32. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Animal means any animal which is required by state law to be inoculated for rabies. 
    Animal at large means when an animal is in any public street, alley, park, or other public grounds, or when off the premises of the owner or person who has custody of the animal, and not constrained by a leash or under the immediate control of the owner or person who has custody of the animal. 
    Animal bite means to be seized with the teeth or jaws so that a person or animal has been nipped, gripped, wounded, or pierced, and saliva of the biting animal has contacted the resulting break or abrasion of the skin. 
    Animal control officer means any agent designated by the city council, the city clerk, or the chief of police to enforce this article. 
    Animal shelter means a facility designated by the city council and used to temporarily confine and house animals that have been seized. 
    Complaint means any written or oral report of an incident or condition alleged to be in violation of this article. 
    Dangerous animal means any animal of potential danger that is known to be of a bad temperament toward humans or is known to have behaved in a threatening manner, without provocation, toward humans. 
    Domestic animal means an animal species, which through long association with man, has been bred to a degree which has resulted in changes affecting the temperament, color, conformation, or other attributes of the species to an extent that makes them unique and different from wild individuals of their kind. 
    Exotic animals mean animals that don't occur naturally, either presently or historically, in the United States. 
    Exposed to rabies means seized with the teeth or claws, so that the skin of the person or animal seized has been nipped or gripped, or has been wounded or pierced and includes suspected or confirmed contact of saliva with a break or abrasion of the skin or with any mucous membrane, as determined by a licensed physician. 
    Guard dog means a dog which is trained or used for the express purpose of protecting and guarding property. 
    Guide dog means a dog, especially trained for the purpose, that is used as a guide to ambulation by a person who is totally or partially blind. 
    Hearing dog means a dog, especially trained for the purpose, that is used as a guide to ambulation by a person who is hearing impaired. 
    Licensed veterinarian means a veterinarian duly licensed to practice veterinary medicine in the state. 
    Livestock and farm animals mean any animal that is considered livestock or a farm animal, such as chickens, horses, mares, jacks, jennies, colts, cows, calves, yearlings, bulls, oxen, sheep, goats, lambs, kinds, hogs, shoats and pigs. 
    Mauling means a serious injury inflicted by an animal to a human or another animal. A mauling is differentiated from a bite by the degree of injury. Serious injury differentiates a bite from a mauling. 
    Native animals mean animals that occur naturally, either presently or historically, in the United States and its territories. In addition, native wild animals include those animals introduced into the United States that have become widespread and are generally considered native. 
    Neutered means made incapable of sexually reproducing offspring (male animals). 
    Nuisance means animals that: 
(1)  Are allowed to act or perform in such a manner as to cause damage or unsanitary conditions to public property or to the property of another; 
(2)  Enter any place where food is stored, prepared, served, or sold to the public, except guide dogs that are accompanying a totally or partially blind person and hearing dogs that accompany a hearing impaired person; 
(3)  Chase, run after, or jump at vehicles using public streets or alleys; 
(4)  Habitually snap, growl, snarl, jump upon or otherwise threaten persons who are lawfully sing public sidewalks, streets, alleys, parks, recreation fields, or other public places; 
(5)  Habitually attack other animals; 
(6)  Feed from, turn over, or otherwise disturb garbage containers; 
(7)  Scratch or dig in flower beds, gardens or soil, or animals that damage the property of persons other than the owner; 
(8)  Are allowed to mate in full or partial view of the public, except for animals inside enclosures designed to keep mating from unwanted public viewing; 
(9)  Disturb the peace by constantly or incessantly barking or howling, or by constantly or incessantly making other disturbing noises. 
    Owner means any person having a right of property in the animal, or who keeps or harbors the animal, or who has it in his care, or acts as its custodian, or who permits the animal to remain on or about any premises occupied by him. 
    Restraint means when any of the following conditions exist: 
(1)  The animal is confined in a building, or fenced pen or yard (excluding electronic fences) on its owner's property or on the property of another person with the other person's consent, adequate to prevent contact with the general public or any persons who enter the premises with the actual or implied permission of the owner or keeper of the animal. 
Persons presently using electronic fences at the time of adoption of this ordinance shall be allowed to continue to do so provided they register with the city clerk within 30 days of adoption of this ordinance. Provided further that should the fence not contain the animal and any complaint be made to the city, this grandfathered status shall be lost and full compliance required. 
(2)  The animal, when off the premises of the owner, is under the immediate and effective control of a responsible person adequately restrained by leash sufficient to prevent the animal from engaging any other human or animal. 
    Spayed means made incapable of sexually reproducing offspring (female animals). 
    Stray means any dog or cat not tagged with a rabies inoculation tag and/or city registration tag and/or personal identification tag. 
    Vaccination means the administration of anti-rabies vaccines or other vaccines by the county rabies officer, his authorized representative or any licensed veterinarian at such intervals as required by state law. 
    Vicious animal means any animal of any species, domestic or wild, native or exotic, that is known to have: 
(1)  A known propensity, tendency or disposition to attack, to cause injury or otherwise endanger the safety of human beings or animals as evidenced by habitual or repeated chasing, snapping or barking at human beings or domestic animals, or in a vicious or terrorizing manner approaching any person in an apparent attitude of attack, whether or not the attack is actually consummated or capable of being consummated; or 
(2)  Attacks a human being or other domestic animal without provocation; provided that a dog shall not be deemed vicious if the threat, injury or damage was sustained by a person who, at the time, was committing a willful trespass or other tort upon the premises occupied by the owner or keeper of the dog, or was teasing, tormenting, abusing or assaulting the dog, or has in the past, abused or assaulted the dog or was committing or attempting to commit a crime; or 
(3)  Any animal which, according to the records of the appropriate authority, has inflicted injury on a human being without provocation; or 
(4)  Any animal which, according to the records of the appropriate authority, has killed a domestic animal without provocation while off the owner's property; or 
(5)  Any animal owned or harbored primarily or in part for the purpose of fighting or any animal trained for fighting. 
    Wild animals mean animals other than those defined as domestic, including mammals, birds, reptiles, and amphibians, which are either native or exotic. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, §§ 2, 12, 13, 2-14-1994; Ord. No. 2005-14, § 1, 10-11-2005) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 3-5-1, 3-7A-1. 
Sec. 10-33. - Enforcement of article provisions. 
    The provisions of this article shall be enforced by the police department or any other agent designated by the city council. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 3, 2-14-1994) 
Sec. 10-34. - Vaccination; tag; costs. 
    Coincident with the issuance of a certificate of vaccination, the rabies officer, his authorized representative, or any licensed veterinarian, who provided the certificate, shall furnish a serially numbered tag bearing the same number and year as that of the certificate, which tag shall be attached to a collar or harness worn by the dog or cat for which the certificate and tag have been issued. The animal owner shall be responsible for paying all costs related to vaccination. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 4, 2-14-1994) 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Ala. 1975, § 3-7A-4. 
Sec. 10-35. - Licensing. 
(a)  Required. The owner or custodian of any animal over the age of four months shall be required to purchase a City of Valley Animal License, but if the animal is under the age of one year the owner will not be required to have the animal spade or neutered until it is at least one year old. The first year of the animal's life the fee for a license shall be $10.00. If the animal has not been spade or neutered upon the renewal date the following year, the animal license shall be $25.00 for the second year. Thereafter the renewal shall be $5.00 per year, but if the owner is 65 or older or a duly certified disabled person the renewal fee shall be $2.50. 
(b)  Fees. License fees shall be paid for a license that is valid for the life of the animal subject to an annual renewal fee of $5.00 due June 1 of each year commencing June 1, 2006 and delinquent if not paid by June 30. This fee shall be $2.50 for persons 65 years and older or duly certified disabled persons. A late fee of $5.00 shall be due for any renewals not made by June 30 of each year. 
(c)  Application. Application for a license shall be made to the city clerk and shall state the name, physical address, and telephone number of the owner, and the name, breed, color, sex, distinguishing marks of the animal. 
(d)  Tagging. The appropriate license fee shall be paid to the city clerk, and, upon payment, there shall be issued to the person making such payment, a tag with the words "City of Valley" plainly inscribed thereon, provided that the owner or custodian of the animal shall have proof from a county rabies officer, an authorized representative thereof or a licensed veterinarian that the animal was currently vaccinated for rabies and has been inoculated for any other diseases with current vaccinations as may be required by state or federal statutes. 
(e)  Collar and tag. The owner shall keep on the animal, excluding cats, at all times a collar, to which shall be affixed the vaccination tag issued by the veterinarian and the city license tag issued by the city clerk. No license issued shall be worn by any animal other than the one described on the inoculation certificate and for which a tag gas been issued. 
(f)  Proof of neutering or spaying. Before a city license may be issued for the lower fee for an animal which has been spayed or neutered, the owner or custodian of such animal shall provide evidence that the animal has been spayed or neutered. The form shall state the name of the doctor or veterinarian who performed the operation, the name of the clinic where such operation was performed, the street address of such licensed veterinarian or clinic, the telephone number, the precise or appropriate date when the operation was performed, and sufficient description of the animal. 
(g)  Proof of vaccination. The city clerk shall issue a license only after presentation of a current rabies vaccination certificate signed by a county rabies officer, an authorized representative thereof, or a licensed veterinarian. The vaccination certificate need not be presented whenever the animal has a condition of illness which renders it unfit to be vaccinated, and this is proved to the satisfaction of the city clerk, who must require written proof to be made by a licensed veterinarian. 
(h)  License exemption. Any person owning a guide dog or a hearing dog shall be exempt from the license fee payment requirement of this section upon application to the city clerk and presentation of a current rabies vaccination certificate as prescribed by the provisions of this section. 
(i)  Duplicate licenses. If a license is destroyed or lost, a duplicate or replacement may be obtained from the city clerk for a fee of $1.00. 
(j)  Revocation of license. The city clerk, director of environmental services, chief of police, city attorney, or presiding municipal court judge may revoke any license if the person holding the license refuses or fails to comply with the regulations of this article or any state law governing the keeping of animals. Any person whose license is revoked shall, within ten days thereafter, humanely dispose of all animals being owned, kept, or harbored by such person, and no part of the license fee shall be refunded. As an option to destroying the animal, an owner may have the animal permanently relocated to a premise outside the city's limits or police jurisdiction. 
(k)  Animal license inspections. Upon receipt of reasonable cause to suspect that an animal has not been licensed, as required by this article, the animal control officer or any police officer of the city shall be authorized to enter upon the private property of an animal owner or harborer to request proof of a license. 
(l)  Inspection of animals and premises where kept. It shall be a condition of the issuance of any license to the owner of animals kept for commercial purposes that the city animal control officer and police officers shall be permitted to inspect all animals and the premises where animals are kept at any reasonable time. If permission for such an inspection is refused by the owner, the city clerk shall revoke the license of the refusing owner. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 5, 2-14-1994; Ord. No. 2005-14, § 2, 10-11-2005; Ord. No. 2011-20, 7-11-2011 ) 
State Law reference- Refusal to permit inspection, Code of Ala. 1975, § 13A-10-3. 
Sec. 10-36. - Restrictions on the number of animals. 
    Not more than five animals shall be allowed in or on any residence of the owner or the person who has custody of the animals, except by special approval by the city council, or except for a mother animal temporarily nursing a larger litter of recently born baby animals. The police department and/or the county health department shall investigate the residence applying for a variance to this section before the presentation of the special application to the council. The first two sentences of this section shall not apply to kennels and other animal-related businesses that are licensed and permitted according to federal and state statutes. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 6, 2-14-1994) 
Sec. 10-37. - Restraint. 
(a)  Constant restraint required. Animal owners are at all times required to keep their animals under restraint as defined herein. 
(b)  Special requirement for business districts. Animal owners shall keep their animals leashed whenever their animals are in a business district. 
(c)  Special requirements during sweep periods. The city council may adopt a resolution to designate periods during which all animals must be kept leashed, kept in a private building, kept in a fenced run, or kept in a fenced yard. These periods shall be known as sweep periods and shall be instituted as necessary to assist the animal control personnel in apprehending stray animals. Any apprehended animal, not under leash restraint, not in a private building, not in a fenced run, or not in a fenced yard, shall be subject to the provisions of section 10-35, licensing. 
(d)  Minimum space requirements for dog pens, kennels and containment areas. Dog Pens, Kennels and Containment Areas shall have minimum space sizes as determined below. 
(1)  Dogs that weigh from one to 35 pounds shall be provided a minimum containment space of at least 80 square feet. 
(2)  Dogs weighing from 36 to 75 pounds shall be contained in areas not less than 100 square feet. 
(3)  Dogs weighing 76 or more pounds shall not be confined in areas of less than 120 square feet. 
(4)  Additional space shall be provided for each additional dog contained in the same area, and the minimum additional space needed for each additional dog shall be calculated by adding 50 percent of the minimum space required for the largest dog contained in the area. 
(5)  Minimum space requirements apply to dog kennels, fenced-in and other containment areas in which dogs live. 
(e)  Animal safety within dog kennels, pens and containment areas. Dog kennels, fenced-in and other containment areas shall be adequately maintained to restrain the dogs as required by Ordinances 94-03 and 2005-14, as amended. These areas shall be kept in such a manner as to be free of conditions that pose a threat to the dog's safety and health. 
(f)  Protection from exposure to weather required. Dog kennels, fenced-in and other containment areas shall have adequate ventilation and shall provide clean, dry shelter from inclement weather, exposure to direct sun and exposure to extreme temperatures. 
(g)  Cleanliness required. Dog kennels, fenced-in and other containment areas shall be kept humanely clean, shall be free of excessive build-up of feces and shall have adequate supplies of fresh water and food. Food shall be controlled in a manner that will not promote the proliferation of rats, vermin, insects or other pests that pose a danger to the health of the dogs or of humans. 
(h)  Reasonable dog medical treatment provided by owner. Dogs housed in kennels, fenced-in and other containment areas shall be kept reasonably free of injury and disease and shall be provided veterinarian care and treatment as required to maintain reasonably good health for all dogs within the restraint areas. It shall be the responsibility of the dog owner to bear the costs of restraint and veterinarian services. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 7, 2-14-1994; Ord. No. 2005-14, § 3, 10-11-2005; Ord. No. 2011-24, § 7, 9-26-2011 ) 
Sec. 10-38. - Impoundment. 
(a)  Animals not licensed or vaccinated pursuant to this article, or found abandoned or not under restraint may be seized and impounded by the animal control officer, any police officer, or other authorized agent of the city. Impoundment may be in any animal shelter designated by the city council. 
(b)  Notwithstanding the provisions of subsection 10-37(a), constant restraint required, if an animal is found at large, not under restraint, and its owner can be immediately identified and located, such animal need not be impounded but may, instead, be released to the owner with a warning or citation issued at the time of release. 
(c)  If the owner of an impounded animal can be readily identified, the animal control officer shall make reasonable attempts to locate the owner and inform him of the requirements for obtaining release of the animal. 
(d)  If, after four days, an animal that was found at large, not under restraint, is not redeemed by the owner and the owner is unknown, the animal may be disposed of by using an approved, humane method. In all other cases, the minimum holding period shall be seven days. 
(e)  If an animal has been hit by a vehicle or is suffering from another cause and it is deemed by a licensed veterinarian or an animal control officer or a city police officer to be beyond help, the animal may be humanely destroyed without a period of confinement. In such cases, it shall be the responsibility of the animal's owner to dispose of the animal's carcass in a manner that meets state and federal health rules and regulations. If the owner of the animal cannot be determined, the city shall be responsible for properly disposing of the carcass. 
(f)  The animal control officer or any city police officer is empowered to issue a citation to the owner of any animal which is in violation of this article, with first violation being $25.00, second $50.00 and third $100.00. After third violation animal may be declared a nuisance and the owner shall be required to permanently remove the animal from the city or its police jurisdiction. 
(g)  An owner or person redeeming a currently licensed animal from the authorized animal shelter shall furnish proof of current rabies vaccination and current license specifically applicable to the animal being redeemed. Such person or owner shall also present an authorization for release to the city clerk at the time the authorization is issued. Upon presentation of the authorization for release and upon payment of the boarding charges to the animal shelter by the owner, the animal may be released to the owner or guardian of the impounded animal. A release fee of $25.00 must be paid prior to the release. 
(h)  A currently unlicensed animal, defined as an animal wearing one or both of its required tags, but at least one has expired, or a stray animal may be released from impoundment to its owner under the following conditions: The owner must pay the regular boarding charge to the facility where the animal is confined. If the animal has a city license, but does not have a current rabies vaccination, the owner must take the animal to a county rabies officer, an authorized representative thereof or a licensed veterinarian for the vaccination. The owner must then show proof of the vaccination to the rabies control officer, the health officer, or the city clerk. If the animal has a current rabies vaccination, but no city license, the owner just take the current rabies vaccination certificate to the city clerk to obtain the city license. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 8, 2-14-1994; Ord. No. 2005-14, § 4, 10-11-2005) 
Sec. 10-39. - Female dogs. 
    It shall be unlawful for a person to allow female dogs that are in their sexually receptive cycle of estrus, commonly known as being in heat, to go upon or have access to the streets, roads, or public areas within the city limits. Female dogs shall be confined in such places and in such a manner as will avoid nuisances being caused by the natural attraction of male dogs. If the owner of a female dog has properly confined the female dog and male dogs are attracted to the female dog in estrus, then the dogs that try to get to the female dog are not in proper restraint as required by this article and constitute a nuisance. Under such circumstances, it is the responsibility of the owners of the male dog to confine their animal until the natural condition estrus in the female dog is over and the female dog no longer attracts male dogs. A female dog in estrus is not properly confined by being on leash. If a female dog in estrus is taken to public areas on a leash and males dogs are attracted to the female dog, then the owner of the female dog is defined to have created a nuisance and may be issued a citation for being in violation of this article. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 9, 2-14-1994) 
Sec. 10-40. - Rabies. 
(a)  Any animal that has or is suspected of having rabies, any animal which has bitten or exposed a human being, or any animal that has been exposed to rabies, shall be reported immediately to the police department. The police department shall perform an investigation to determine if the animal is in conformance with this article and to determine if it has been inoculated within the required time periods. Upon investigation by the police department, the findings of the investigation shall be reported by the police department to the person bitten and/or to the attending physician within 24 hours of the time the animal bite was first reported to the police. 
(b)  The following actions shall be taken as well: 
(1)  Quarantine generally. 
a.  If a dog or cat is in conformance with all provisions of this article, it shall be quarantined in a licensed veterinary clinic for observation for a period of ten days subsequent to the date of the exposure, or as otherwise directed by the state health officer, as required by state law. The owner must pay boarding and observation fees to the clinic when the animal is released. 
b.  If a dog or cat is not vaccinated for rabies and therefore is not in conformance with this article, it shall be quarantined in a licensed veterinary clinic for a period of ten calendar days and must receive a rabies vaccination before being released. Board fees will be the responsibility of the victim if the owner is unknown. 
c.  The quarantine requirement may be waived, if the owner signs a euthanasia agreement (agreement to have the animal humanely destroyed) and pays the fees covering the euthanasia and the expenses of sending the animal's head to the state health department laboratory for examination. 
d.  If the animal is a canine corps dog or has been registered as a guard dog, a guide dog or a hearing dog at the time the bite occurred and the animal was acting as a canine corps dog, a guard dog, a guide dog or a hearing dog when the bite occurred, the owner shall report any relocations of the animal that occur within ten days of the bite to the city police department. The owner shall also be required to confirm that the dog has received rabies vaccinations that were current at the time of the bite. If such confirmation cannot be made, then the dog shall be confined at a licensed veterinary clinic for observation for a period of ten calendar days from the time of the bite, and the dog must receive a rabies vaccination before being released. 
(2)  Animal suspected of rabies or exposed to rabies. 
a.  If the dog or cat has been properly vaccinated for rabies, it shall be quarantined for observation in a licensed veterinary clinic for a period of ten calendar days from the date the exposure was reported to the police department. The animal's owner is responsible for boarding and observation fees. 
b.  If the dog or cat has bitten a human being, is not licensed, and the owner cannot be determined, the animal shall be quarantined in a licensed veterinary clinic until it can be humanely destroyed. 
c.  If the dog or cat is not properly vaccinated for rabies, it shall be quarantined in a licensed veterinary clinic until it can be humanely destroyed. The head of the animal suspected of rabies or exposure to rabies shall be submitted according to state and federal regulations, for appropriate examination by the state health department laboratory. 
(3)  Other animals. 
a.  The period of quarantine for animals other than domesticated dogs and cats which have bitten or exposed a human being shall be determined by the state department of public health upon consultation with the U.S. Public Health Service; provided, however, that for those animal species where reliable epidemiologic data are lacking regarding duration of rabies virus secretion from the salivary glands, such animals shall be humanely destroyed and the head submitted for rabies examination to the state health department laboratory. 
b.  Those domesticated species, other than dogs and cats, for which antirabies vaccine is recognized and recommended, upon exposure or potential exposure to a known rabid animal, shall be humanely destroyed or slaughtered immediately; provided, however, that the owner may have the option of quarantining such animals based on the recommendations of the state department of public health upon consultation with the U.S. Public Health Service. 
(4)  Rabid animal. 
a.  Every animal confirmed to have rabies shall be committed to the care and quarantine of a licensed veterinary clinic and shall be disposed of in accordance with the laws of the state. 
b.  Information, regarding an animal which has been confirmed to have rabies and which has bitten a human being, shall be reported by the veterinarian who has custody of the rabid animal and to the attending physician of the person who was bitten. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 10, 2-14-1994) 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 3-7A-9, 3-7A-10. 
Sec. 10-41. - Animals at large. 
    No person shall permit any animal to be at large in the city limits at any time. Within one hour after an animal escapes from either the owner or the person having custody of the animal, the owner or custodian of the animal shall report the escape of the animal to the police department. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 11, 2-14-1994) 
Sec. 10-42. - Vicious animals. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or harbor a vicious animal in the City of Valley, Alabama, as such animals are defined in section 10-32 herein. 
(b)  Any vicious animal found off the premises of its owner may be seized by any police officer or animal control officer and, upon establishing of the vicious character of the animal by a court of competent jurisdiction, the animal may be destroyed or otherwise disposed of as ordered by the court, with the owner being liable for all costs of boarding, treatment, and disposal of the animal. 
(c)  This section shall not apply to animals under the control of a law enforcement or military agency, nor to animals which are kept for the protection of property by commercial establishments provided the animal is restrained by an adequate cage or fence (excluding electronic fences) preventing contact with general public or any persons who enter the premises with the actual or implied consent of the owner or keeper of the animal. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 12, 2-14-1994; Ord. No. 2005-14, § 5, 10-11-2005) 
Sec. 10-43. - Nuisance control. 
    Without regard to other provisions of this article or to other sections of this chapter, it shall be unlawful for owners of animals to allow, permit, or by negligence fail to prevent the animals under control from acting or performing in such a manner as to cause a nuisance. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 13, 2-14-1994) 
Sec. 10-44. - Livestock. 
    No animal defined in section 10-32 as livestock or farm animals is to be kept in any R-1, R-2, R-3, or commercial zone unless the animal is part of the operations or product of a duly licensed processing plant. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 14, 2-14-1994) 
Sec. 10-45. - Prohibited animals. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful to keep any wild carnivore species, or hybrids (wolf-dog hybrids, etc.) of animals as pets within the city. It shall be unlawful to keep, as pets, any reptiles that are considered inherently dangerous to humans. Commercial traffic of these animals for such purpose is prohibited. 
(b)  Animals whose owners or keepers are duly licensed and permitted by federal and state agencies to keep dangerous animals in a manner that protects the public welfare and safety are exempt from this section. 
(c)  Animals considered inherently dangerous to humans are as follows: 
(1)  Class mammalia. 
Racoon, skunk, and coyote 
African buffalo ( syncerus caffer ) 
Hippopotamus ( hippopotamus amphibius ) 
Wolves, dingoes, jackals, all species of foxes (family canidae ) 
Hyenas, all species except arrdwolves ( proteles eristatus ) (family hyaenidae ) 
Wild black-footed ferret ( mustelidae nigripes ) (endangered species) 
Wolverine ( gulo ) 
Honey badger or ratel ( mellivora campensis ) 
Old world badger ( meles ) 
Bears (family ursidae ) 
Lions, jaguars, leopards, tigers (genus panthera ) 
Clouded leopard ( neofelis nebulosa ) 
Cheetah ( acinonyx jubatus ) 
Cougar or mountain lion ( felis concolor ) 
Elephants (family elephontidae ) 
Rhinoceroses (family rhinocerptidae ) 
Gibbons, siamangs (family hylobatidae ) 
Orangutans, chimpanzees, gorillas (family pongidae ) 
Baboons, drils, mandrills (genus papio ) 
Macaques (genus macaca ) 
Gelada baboon ( theropithecus gelada ) 
(2)  Class reptilia. 
Gavials (family gavialidae ) 
Crocodiles (family crocodylidae ) 
Alligators, caimans ( alligatoridae ) 
Cobras, coral snakes (family elapidae ) 
Sea snakes (family hydrophidae ) 
Adders, viper (family viperidae ) 
Pit vipers (family crotalidae ) 
All poisonous rear-fanged species (family colubridae ) 
(3)  Constricting snakes over eight feet long. The following species of constricting snakes over eight feet in length: 
Cribo ( spilotes pullatus ) 
Indian rat snake ( ptyas mucosus ) 
Boa constrictor ( boa constrictor ), all subspecies 
Rainbow boa ( epicrates cenchria ) 
Emerald tree boa ( corallus caninus ) 
Anaconda ( eunectes murinus ) 
Indian python ( python molurus ) 
Reticulate python ( python reticulatur ) 
Blood python ( python reticulatus ) 
Rock python ( python sebae ) 
(4)  Monsters, lizards and dragons. 
Gila monsters and beaded lizards (family helodermatidae ) 
Komodo dragon ( varanus komodoensis ) 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 15, 2-14-1994) 
Sec. 10-46. - Release of animals. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to release any animal into the environment to find food for itself and to survive on its own without the approval or supervision of a licensed veterinarian. Animals and their owners who are officially participating in federal/state animal release/conservation programs are exempt from the provisions of this section. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 16, 2-14-1994) 
Sec. 10-47. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Except for warnings described in this article, any person violating the provisions of this article shall be subject to a fine of not less than $25.00 or more than $500.00 and/or imprisonment not exceeding 30 days, plus court cost, as well as the cost of boarding, treatment, and disposal of the animal where applicable. 
(Ord. No. 94-03, § 17, 2-14-1994; Ord. No. 2005-14, § 6, 10-11-2005) 
Sec. 10-48. - Cruelty: Animals in vehicles. 
    No vehicle owner, passenger or operator shall place or confine an animal or allow it to be placed or confined or to remain in an unattended vehicle without sufficient ventilation or under conditions for such a period of time as may reasonably be expected to endanger the health or well-being of such animal due to heat, lack of water or such other circumstances as may be expected to cause suffering, disability or death. 
( Ord. No. 2011-20, 7-11-2011 )
