ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 14-1. - Property Maintenance Code; adopted. 
    That certain document on file in the office of the city clerk, which is incorporated herein by reference, regulating the conditions and maintenance of property, buildings and structures, is adopted as the Property Maintenance Code of the City of Valley, Alabama. 
(Ord. No. 2003-18A, § 1, 8-25-2003) 
Sec. 14-2. - International Residential Code; adopted. 
(a)  The council adopts as the Valley Residential Code the 2006 Edition of the International Residential Code, including Appendix, three copies of which are filed in the city clerk's office. This code shall regulate the construction, alteration, movement, enlargement, replacement, repair, equipment, location, removal and demolition of detached one and two family dwellings and multiple single family dwellings (townhouses) not more than three stories in height with separate means of ingress and egress as herein provided, and provide for the issuance of permits and collection of fees therefore. 
(b)  Deleted and amended portions of adopted International Residential Code, 2006 Edition: 
(1)  The following sections shall be deleted from the International Residential Code: R103 and R112. 
(2)  That Section P2603.6.1 shall be amended to read as follows: 
P2603.6.1-Sewer Depth. The building sewers that connect to private sewage disposal systems shall be a minimum or 12 inches below finished grade at the point of septic tank connection. Building sewers shall be a minimum of 12 inches below grade. 
(3)  That section P3103.1 shall be amended to read as follows: 
P3103.1-Roof Extension. All open vent pipes which extend through a roof shall be terminated at least 12 inches above the roof or 12 inches above the anticipated snow accumulation, except that where a roof is to be used for any purpose other than weather protection, the vent extensions shall be run at least seven feet above the roof. 
(4)  To comply with Alabama Power Company standards for ungrounded services, Chapter 35, Services, Section E3502 Service Size and Rating, Item E3502.1 of the 2006 International Residential Code shall be amended to read as follows: 
E3502.1 Ampacity of ungrounded conductors. Ungrounded service conductors shall have an ampacity of not less than the load served. For one family dwellings, the ampacity of the ungrounded conductors shall be not less than 150 amperes, 3 wire. For all other installations the ampacity of the ungrounded conductors shall not be less than 60 amperes. 
(Ord. No. 2006-05, § 1, 3-27-2006; Ord. No. 2007-35, § 1(Exh. A), 8-13-2007 ; Ord. No. 2012-14, § 1, 7-9-2012 ) 
Sec. 14-3. - International Property Maintenance Code; adopted. 
(a)  The council adopts as the Valley Property Maintenance Code the 2006 Edition of the International Property Maintenance Code, three copies of which are filed in the city clerk's office. This code shall regulate and govern the conditions and maintenance of all property, buildings and structures; by providing the standards for supplied utilities and facilities and other physical things and conditions essential to ensure that structures are safe, sanitary and fit for occupation and use; and the condemnation of buildings and structures unfit for human occupancy and use and the demolition of such existing structures and providing for the issuance of permits and collection of fees therefore. 
(b)  The following sections of the 2006 International Property Maintenance Code are hereby revised: 
Section 101.1. Insert: City of Valley. 
Section 103.5. Insert: As Adopted by the Valley City Council. 
106.3.1 Authority of City to Abate Weeds, Grass, and Plants at Expense of Property Owner. 
Should the owner or other person in charge of premises subject to conditions described in Section 302.4 of the 2006 International Property Maintenance Code (herein referred to as the "Code") fail or refuse to abate the nuisances or to remove the weeds and grass described in such sections upon being notified to do so as provided in said Code, the city is authorized to abate the nuisance at the expense of the owner of such property, the cost thereof to be a lien upon the property and to be collected as any other debts are collected or liens enforced. 
Each unlawful act defined in Chapter 2 Section 202 of the Code (as hereby amended) is declared to be a public nuisance, and in the event the owner or person in charge, fails to remove the cause of such violation within 14 days after notice to do so by the applicable city department as stated in Section 107.3 of the Code, such person shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. When such person allows the same type violation to reoccur on three or more occasions within a 12-month period, the appropriate city department may issue a summons and complaint against the violator, or the City may abate the nuisance without prior written notice to the owner or person in charge, the cost of which shall be a lien upon the property. 
Add to Section 202: Definitions 
Commercial Property shall mean any lot, tract, parcel, land, or other property located within the city, that is zoned or designated for uses other than residential purposes. 
Hazardous Plant Nuisance shall mean trees, shrubs, ornamental or non-ornamental plant growth, growing or standing on private property that is dead, damaged, deteriorated, decayed or has otherwise become hazardous for any reason that could pose a danger to the property on which it is located, any adjacent property, whether public or private, or to the public in general, by danger of falling, splitting, uprooting, or shedding limbs, or any other reason determined to be a hazard. 
Improved Subdivision shall mean a division of a tract of land or acreage into tracts or parcels, and the improvement thereof by construction of streets, water lines and, where applicable, sewer lines to serve the subdivided property. 
Natural Condition shall mean uncultivated and unseeded land, still in a state of nature. But any growth on land once it has been cleared or plowed is not a natural condition, even though it has not been planted or cultivated by anyone. 
Owner or Owners of Property shall mean any person, agent, operator, firm or corporation having a legal or equitable interest in the property; or recorded in the official records of the state, county or municipality as holding title to the property; or person last assessed for payment of ad valorem taxes; or otherwise having control of the property, including the guardian of the estate of any such person, and the executor or administrator of the estate of such person if ordered to take possession of real property by a court. 
Person shall mean any individual, owner, title holder, agent, firm, corporation, partnership, association, or organization of any kind. It shall include, but not be limited to, any tenant, lessee, manager, operator, occupant, executor, executrix, administrator, guardian, trustee, bankruptcy trustee, or other person in charge of, care of, possession of, or control of any real or personal property. 
Premises shall mean any lot, yard, plot, tract, parcel, or other piece of land or property located within the city. 
Residential Property shall mean any lot, tract, parcel, land, or other property located within the city, on which single or multifamily structures used as a residence or for human habitation exist, or any property that is located within an area that is zoned for residential uses by the city. 
Weed Nuisance shall mean any abundance of overgrown weeds or grass within the city, which could be injurious to the general public health, safety and general welfare by; providing breeding grounds and shelter for rats, mice, snakes, mosquitoes and other vermin, insects and pests; or attaining such heights and dryness so as to constitute a serious fire threat or hazard; or bearing wingy or downy seeds, that when mature, could cause the spread of weeds or, when breathed could cause irritation to the throat, lungs and eyes of the public; or hiding debris, such as broken glass or metal, which could inflict injury on any person going upon the property; or being unsightly; or any growth of weeds, other than ornamental plant growth, which exceeds 12 inches in height; or anything defined as a hazardous plant nuisance. 
Section 302.4 Weed, Grass, Plant, Nuisance. 
All premises and exterior property shall be maintained free from weeds or plant growth in excess of 12 inches in height. All noxious weeds shall be prohibited. A weed nuisance shall have meaning as defined in Section 202 and shall include all annual plants and vegetation. 
Section 304.14 Insert: January 1st thru December 31st. 
Section 602.3. Insert: January 1st thru December 31st. 
Section 602.4. Insert: January 1st thru December 31st. 
( Ord. No. 2007-34, §§ 1, 2, 8-13-2007 ; Ord. No. 2010-12, 6-14-2010 ) 
Sec. 14-4. - International Building Code; adopted. 
    The council adopts as the Valley Building Code the 2006 Edition of the International Building Code, including Appendix E, F, G, H, I, J, and K, three copies of which are filed in the city clerk's office. This Code shall regulate the construction along with the governing of the conditions and maintenance of all property, buildings and structures; by providing the standards for supplied utilities and facilities and other physical things and conditions essential to ensure that structures are safe, sanitary and fit for occupation and use; and the condemnation of buildings and structure unfit for human occupancy and use and the demolition of such structures as herein provided, and provide for the issuance of permits and collection of fees therefore. 
( Ord. No. 2007-36, § 1, 8-13-2007 ) 
Sec. 14-5. - Building numbers to be assigned. 
(a)  There shall be assigned to each house and building located on any street, avenue, alley or highway in the city, a number identifying the address of the property. The owner of the property shall place or caused to be placed upon each house or building and/or both sides of a curb mounted mailbox controlled by him the number assigned. 
(b)  Such numbers shall be placed or if missing, replaced within 20 days after the numbers are assigned. The cost of the numbers shall be paid for by the property owner. 
(c)  The standard minimum height of numbers placed on buildings shall conform to the International Property Maintenance Code Section 304.3 which states as follows: Buildings shall have approved address numbers placed in a position to be plainly legible and visible from the street or road fronting the property. These numbers shall contrast with their background. Address numbers shall be Arabic numerals or alphabet letters. Numbers shall be a minimum of four inches high with a minimum stroke width of 0.5 inches. If a curb mounted mailbox or marker is used the letters shall be a minimum of three inches high with a minimum stroke width of 0.4 inches. 
(1)  With single-family dwellings the numbers shall be placed immediately above or at the side of the door or on both sides of a curb mounted mailbox. 
(2)  With multi-family dwellings the numbers shall be placed on the building face most visible from the parking area or street. 
(3)  With commercial buildings whose public entrance is visible from the street the numbers shall be placed above, on, or at the side of the door of each individual business. If no entrance is visible from the street, the building will be numbered on the side (s) most visible from the street. 
(4)  Whenever any building is located more than 50 feet from the curb or edge of street, the number of such building shall be conspicuously displayed on the owners property at the right-of-way line (owners property line) near the driveway or common entrance to such building and upon any the gate post, fence, post, both sides of a curb mounted mailbox, or other appropriate place so as to be easily describable from the street. 
(d)  All numbers shall be of a durable material with numbers in contrast to background color. 
( Ord. No. 2008-02, § 1, 1-28-2008 ) 
Sec. 14-6. - New buildings. 
    Whenever any house, building or structure shall be erected or located in the city, in order to preserve the continuity and uniformity of numbers of the houses, buildings and structures, it shall be the duty of the owner or builder to get the proper number assigned by the director of planning and development. Once the number has been assigned it is the responsibility of the owner or builder to procure the correct number, of a four-inch minimum size for attachment to houses, buildings or structures and three-inch minimum size for attachment to a curb mounted mailbox or other devices stated in this ordinance and to immediately fasten the said number, so assigned, upon said building or approved device as provided by this ordinance. No building permit shall be issued for any house, building or structure until the owner has been assigned an official number by the director of planning and development for the premises. Final approval of any structure erected, repaired, altered or modified after the passage of this section shall be withheld until permanent and proper numbers have been affixed to said structure. 
( Ord. No. 2008-02, § 2, 1-28-2008 ) 
Secs. 14-3-14-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - DANGEROUS BUILDINGS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Environment, ch. 30. 

Sec. 14-31. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Dangerous building means any building, shed, fence or other manmade structure that: 
(1)  Is dangerous to the public health because of its condition, and may cause or aid in the spread of disease or injury to the health of the occupants of it or neighboring structures; 
(2)  Because of faulty construction, age, lack of repair or any other cause, is especially liable to fire and constitutes or creates a fire hazard; 
(3)  By reason of faulty construction or any other cause, is liable to cause injury or damage by collapsing or by a collapse or fall of any part of such structure; or 
(4)  Because of its condition or because of lack of doors or windows is available to and frequented by malefactors or disorderly persons who are not lawful occupants of such structure. 
(Ord. No. 85-10, § 1, 7-22-1985) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 14-32. - Declared nuisance. 
    Any dangerous building in the city is declared to be a nuisance. 
(Ord. No. 85-10, § 1, 7-22-1985) 
Sec. 14-33. - Prohibited acts. 
    It shall be unlawful to maintain or permit the existence of any dangerous building in the city. It shall be unlawful for the owner, occupant or person in custody of any dangerous building to permit the building to remain in a dangerous condition, or to occupy or otherwise use such building or permit it to be occupied or otherwise used while it is or remains in a dangerous condition. 
(Ord. No. 85-10, § 2, 7-22-1985) 
Sec. 14-34. - Abatement. 
(a)  Whenever the building official, the fire marshal, the health officer or the chief of police shall be of the opinion that any building, shed, fence or other manmade structure in the city is a dangerous building, he shall file a written statement to this effect with the city clerk. The clerk, with the consent of the mayor, shall thereupon cause written notice to be served upon the owner, and/or upon the occupant of such structure, if any, by certified mail or by personal service or, if unoccupied, by posting the notice in a conspicuous place on the premises structure. Such notice shall state that the structure has been declared to be in a dangerous condition, and that such dangerous condition must be removed or remedied by repairing or altering the structure or by demolishing it, and that the condition must be remedied at once. Such notice may be in the following terms: 
    "To (owner-occupant of premises) of the premises known and described as ____________ ." 
    "You are hereby notified that ____________ (describe structure) on the premises above mentioned has been classified as a nuisance and a dangerous building after inspection by ____________ ." 
    "The causes for this decision are ____________ (here insert the facts as to the dangerous condition)." 
    "You must remedy this condition or demolish the dangerous building immediately, or the City will institute an action in the circuit court to abate or cause such improvements to be removed after which, cost of the same will be assessed as a lien against the real property in question." 
    "This decision is not final, and you have the right to request a hearing before the council by filing a written request for a hearing within ten days from receipt of this notice. You will be notified when the council will hear any objection you may have. If no objection is taken or if the council shall not allow your objection, then action in the circuit court to abate or remove such improvements will be commenced." 
(b)  Upon filing of suit in the circuit court, notice of such suit shall be posted on the premises and shall state substantially as follows: 
    "The City of Valley, Alabama, has found the structure erected hereon to be a "dangerous building" as defined in chapter 14, article II, of the Code of Ordinances, City of Valley, Alabama. This structure is unfit for human habitation or other use; the use or occupancy of this structure for human habitation or other use after ____________ / ____________ / ____________ , 20 ____________ , is unlawful and prohibited by chapter 14, article II, of the Code of Ordinances, City of Valley, Alabama. Suit for destruction or abatement of the dangerous building is now pending in the Circuit Court of Chambers County." 
(Ord. No. 85-10, § 3, 7-22-1985; Ord. No. 86-03, 1-27-1986) 
Sec. 14-35. - Fire limits. 
(a)  Any frame building or structure within the city limits, which has been or may be damaged by fire, decay or other causes to the extent of 50 percent of its value, shall be torn down and removed, or rebuilt in a safe condition. 
(b)  Upon written notice by the building official, the health officer, the fire marshal or the chief of police to the effect that such building has been so damaged, filed with the city clerk, the clerk shall notify the mayor of the receipt of such notice. 
(c)  The mayor shall then appoint three persons to determine whether or not such building or structure has been damaged to the extent of 50 percent of its value. 
(d)  A copy of the notice of the appointment of this board of three persons to determine the damage shall be served upon the owner of the premises by personal service or by certified mail at his last known address. 
(e)  Such notice shall be in substantially the following form: 
    "To ____________ " 
    "You are hereby notified that ____________ had determined that the building owned by you at ____________ located within the city limits of the City of Valley has been damaged by fire, decay or otherwise to the extent of 50 percent of its value and that a board of three persons has been appointed to verify this finding, which board will hold its first meeting in room ____________ in the city hall on the ____________ day of ____________ / ____________ / ____________ 20 ____________ , at ____________ m., at which time it will determine whether or not this finding is correct." 
    "If this finding is verified by the board you must tear down and remove the building, or rebuild it to a safe condition." 
(f)  If this finding is verified by the board of three members and it determines that the building in question has been damaged to the extent of 50 percent of its value, it shall be the duty of the owner to tear down and remove the building starting within 20 days and completing within 90 days after the finding of such board, or to remodel it to a safe condition within the same time period. It shall be unlawful to occupy or otherwise use or permit the occupancy or other use of such building after such finding until it is so remodeled, and notice of such prohibition shall be posted in a conspicuous place on the premises and remain until compliance or removal by the city. 
(Ord. No. 85-10, § 4, 7-22-1985; Ord. No. 86-03, 1-27-1986) 
Sec. 14-36. - Statutory procedures for correcting conditions. 
    In addition to the provisions of this article, the city may demolish, abate or otherwise correct or require the correction of dangerous or unsafe conditions in buildings and structures as provided in Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-40-30 et seq. or any other applicable law. 
Sec. 14-37. - Penalties for violation of article. 
(a)  Any violation of any of the provisions of this article is declared a nuisance, and proceedings may be instituted in any court of competent jurisdiction for injunctive or other relief to abate such nuisance. 
(b)  Any person who shall violate any provision of this article shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 85-10, § 5, 7-22-1985) 
Sec. 14-38. - Enforcement. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person in the city to allow the house or building in which the people live or own or the premises around the house or the alley or street abutting the premises to become or remain in an unsanitary or unsightly condition. 
(a)  Enforcement. This provision shall be enforced by the city code enforcement officer who upon finding that this section is being violated, shall issue written notification to the last party assessing the property for state taxes to the address on file in the tax office, by certified or registered mail. The mailing of the certified or registered mail notice, properly addressed and postage prepaid, shall constitute notice as required by this section. In addition, a copy of the notice is also posted at the property site. The notice shall require the violation to be corrected within 14 days of the date of the notice. 
The owner or person assessing the property for taxes shall have the right to file a written request for a hearing before the city council on this notice provided that the request is made in writing to the city clerk within 14 days of the notice. This notice shall be required to set forth any objections to the finding by the city official. 
(b)  Action if appeal is made. If an appeal is made within the allotted time, the city council shall hear the report, together with any objections which may be raised by any owner whose property is liable to be assessed for the work and the council may make such modifications in the report as they deem necessary, after which by resolution the report may be confirmed or denied. If the report is confirmed, the council shall allow the owner ten days to address the violation. Should the violation not be addressed within this time the council may authorize the code enforcement officer to abate the violation by cleaning the property and removing any trash or other violating condition from the property. The code enforcement officer of the city shall coordinate an effort to go upon the property and address the abatement utilizing city services or contracting for the service. After completion of this work, the code enforcement officer shall render an itemized report to the council showing the cost incurred in abating the nuisance. Upon the filing of this cost a public hearing shall be held for consideration thereof, with notice being given to the person assessing the property for taxes by first class mail. 
At the public hearing, if the council may approve the report of the code enforcement office and pass a resolution assessing a lien against the property for the recovery of the costs of abatement. 
(c)  Action if no appeal is made. If no request for hearing is made within the time required, and the violation has not been corrected, the code enforcement officer shall appear before the council and render his written report of the violation. Upon considering the report the council may find that the violation of the section exists and may authorize the code enforcement officer to abate the violation by cleaning the property and removing any trash or other violating condition from the property. The code enforcement officer of the city shall coordinate an effort to go upon the property and address the abatement utilizing city services or contracting for the service. After completion of this work, the code enforcement officer shall render an itemized report to the council showing the cost incurred in abating the nuisance. Upon the filing of this cost a public hearing shall be held for consideration thereof, with notice being given to the person assessing the property for taxes by first class mail. 
At the public hearing if the council may approve the report of the code enforcement office and pass a resolution assessing a lien against the property for the recovery of the costs of abatement. 
(d)  Lien assessment. The amounts of the costs for the abating a violation of this section shall constitute special assessments against the land, and as thus made and confirmed shall constitute a lien on the property for the amount of such assessment. Thereafter, such amounts shall be collected at the same time and in the same manner as ordinary municipal assessments are collected and shall be subject to the same penalties. A copy of the resolution shall also be filed in the office of the Probate Court of Chambers County, Alabama imposing a lien on the property. 
(e)  Criminal penalty. The code enforcement officer or any law enforcement officer may issue a citation to the owner and occupant of the property upon which the violation exists requiring the person to appear in municipal or district court to answer charges for the violation of this section. Such citation shall name the party charged, the address of the property where the alleged violation is located, and the nature of the offense or violation. It shall also apprise the person of the date, time and place at which to appear in court. Such citation, returnable to the municipal or district court shall be served on the owner of the property by any code enforcement officer for the city. 
Instead of placing a person under custodial arrest, may issue a summons and complaint against a person charged with a violation of this section. For purposes of this section the city authorizes the use of the uniform non-traffic citation and complaint form currently utilized by the city. 
The procedure for issuing a citation is that, when an arrest is to be made, the arresting officer releases the person upon his written promise to appear in court at the designated time and place. If the person refuses to sign the citation and appear in court, the officer is to take the person into custody and bring him before any officer or official authorized to approve a bond. 
(f)  Means of enforcement. The code enforcement officer or any law enforcement officer may institute either or both enforcement procedures set forth above. The institution of one procedure does not preclude the subsequent or simultaneous institution of the other procedure, provided the criminal procedure is not used to collect any outstanding civil assessments against the subject property. 
(g)  Penalties. Any person violating any provisions hereof shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction, shall be fined not less than $50.00 nor more than $200.00, and if the violation or failure or refusal to obey or comply with such section is a continuing one, each day's violation shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punished accordingly. 
(Ord. No. 2018-03 , § 1, 2-26-2018) 
Secs. 14-39-14-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - DEMOLITION OF BUILDINGS 

Sec. 14-61. - Definitions. 
    The following definitions shall apply and govern in connection with the provisions of this article: 
    Applicant: Any person filing an application for a demolition permit. 
    Application: An application for a permit for demolition of a building or structure. 
    Building: Any combination of materials forming a shelter for persons, animals or property. 
    Building official: Any person authorized to issue demolition permits in the city. 
    City: The City of Valley, Alabama. 
    Demolition: The act of pulling down, destroying, removing, or razing a building or structure or commencing the work of total or substantial destruction with intent of completing the same. For the purpose of this article, "demolition" shall not include routine maintenance, interior renovations, removal or construction of porches, decks, windows or similar types of renovations. 
    Permit: A permit issued by a building official for demolition of a building or structure pursuant to an application. 
    Person: An individual, corporation, partnership, association, trust or society. 
    Premises: The parcel of land upon which the demolished building or structure was located and all adjoining parcels of land under common ownership or control. 
    Structure: Any constructed, erected, or placed material or combination of materials in or upon the ground, excluding sidewalks, paving on streets, driveways, parking areas and patios. 
( Ord. No. 2014-09, § 1, 4-14-2014 ) 
Sec. 14-62. - Permit required. 
    The demolition of any building or structure shall require a permit which has been reviewed and approved by the building official in conformance with this article. Nothing contained herein shall limit the authority of the building official to order a structure demolished in a life or health threatening emergency situation or as may be otherwise authorized by state statute, city ordinance or regulation. 
( Ord. No. 2014-09, § 2, 4-14-2014 ) 
Sec. 14-63. - Application. 
    In order to obtain a building demolition permit for the demolition of any building or structure, a permit application form must be completed and submitted to the building official. The building demolition permit application must include the following information: 
(1)  Location of the property and name or names of legal owner or owners of the property with a deed reference and tax identification number provided for the property. 
(2)  Map, plat, drawing or survey of the property. 
(3)  Demolition plan identifying structures to be demolished, the expected starting date and the amount of time anticipated to complete the demolition and the method of demolition. Demolition work shall be performed between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. eastern time. No demolition work shall occur on Sundays. 
(4)  Specific plans for the reuse of the property if the demolition permit is approved. If the reuse plan contemplates the construction of a structure, an application shall include building plans and specifications prepared in compliance with the provisions of the existing building code in effect in the city. 
(5)  Site restoration plans. If commencement of a new structure is not planned to occur within 60 days after completion of demolition, then the application shall include a detailed site restoration and maintenance plan depicting all work required to restore the subject property, within 60 days after completion of the demolition, to a safe, clean condition until construction of a new structure has commenced including without limitation backfilling of any excavation, grading, seeding, fencing, stormwater management, utility connection and the like. 
(6)  Storm water management. Applicant shall be responsible for implementing adequate soil and erosion control. A notice of intent permit shall be filed with ADEM (Alabama Department of Environmental Management) on all disturbed areas one acre or larger. 
(7)  Traffic control plan. A traffic control plan which depicts the subject property, surrounding roads, lots and parking lots that indicate where construction vehicles and workers will be parking during the duration of the demolition/construction of the structure shall be submitted to the city with the demolition permit application. The city may make revisions to the traffic control plan based upon the volume of traffic on adjacent roads, width of roads, existing no-parking restrictions, and location of drive approaches and time of work. Large scale demolition projects will be assigned specific haul routes and procedures to minimize damages to city's infrastructure. 
( Ord. No. 2014-09, § 3, 4-14-2014 ) 
Sec. 14-64. - Procedures for permit approval. 
    The building official and building inspection personnel will be responsible for the processing and review of any building demolition permit application. As a part of the review process, an inspection of the subject property may be performed by the building official and any inspection personnel. The building official will review all building demolition permit applications in accordance with this article and any other applicable city ordinances as well as in accordance with the following standards: 
(1)  The granting of a permit shall not be detrimental to the public health, safety, and general welfare of the community. 
(2)  Adequate utilities, access ways, drainage and other necessary facilities must be provided for a permit to be granted. 
    The building official may impose such conditions and restrictions upon the issuance of the permit as may be necessary in order to comply with the standards set forth herein. If a building demolition permit application is approved by the building official, any demolition which takes pl ace shall be done in accordance with the provisions of the ICC International Building Code in force at the time, the requirements of this article, and any other additional requirements or conditions as placed on the applicant by the building official. The applicant shall also be required to submit to the city proof of disconnection of utilities prior to commencing demolition of the building or structure. 
( Ord. No. 2014-09, § 4, 4-14-2014 ) 
Sec. 14-65. - Demolition bond. 
    The applicant shall post with the city, at the time of issuance of any demolition permit, a cash demolition bond or letter of credit in the form approved by the building official. The bond shall be in an amount equal to $1.00 per square foot, or any part thereof, of floor space contained in the building or structure to be demolished. No surety shall be required on any bond of less than $4,000.00. Such bond shall be in addition to all other application and processing fees and performance securities required by codes or ordinances of the city. 
    The city shall have the right at all times, at its option, to draw on the demolition bond for costs, including legal fees and administrative expenses, incurred or to be incurred by the city in exercising any of its rights under this article in the event the applicant undertakes any work in violation of any provisions of this article or any permit issued or plan approved pursuant to this article, or the applicant fails or refuses to complete any work authorized by any permit issued under this article and in accordance with the plans approved in connection with said permit. 
(1)  Replenishment of bond. If the city draws on the bond, then the applicant shall replenish the bond to the full amount required by this section immediately after demand therefore is made to the applicant by the city. Any failure of the applicant to replenish the bond shall result in cancellation of the related permit, which permit shall not be reissued thereafter except after filing a new application therefore, payment of the permit and establishment and payment of a new bond. 
Upon completion of demolition, the permit holder shall submit a written request for the refund of the demolition bond or release of demolition letter of credit. The city shall return any unused portion of the demolition bond to the applicant, without interest, within 30 days after final demolition inspection of the subject property and approval of the completed demolition by the building official. 
( Ord. No. 2014-09, § 5, 4-14-2014 ) 
Sec. 14-66. - Fee. 
    A $100.00 non-refundable permit application fee shall be required for a building demolition permit and the fee must be submitted with the demolition application. Any revision in this fee may be made by the city council by passage of an appropriate resolution revising the fee. 
( Ord. No. 2014-09, § 6, 4-14-2014 ) 
Sec. 14-67. - City's right to complete work. 
    Every permit authorizing demolition of a building or structure issued pursuant to this article shall be conditioned on the agreement of the applicant and the owner of the subject property that: 
(1)  If the applicant fails or refuses to complete the work authorized by said permit in accordance with all plans approved in connection with said permit or if said permit is expired or been cancelled and the applicant has failed to secure a new permit to complete the work, or if the applicant has violated any provisions of this article or of any permit issued or plan approved pursuant to this article and fails and refuses to cure such violation, then the city shall have the right, in addition to all other rights afforded to the city by law, at the city's option, to complete such work or to correct any defect or deficiency, using the city's own forces or contractors hired for that purpose. 
(2)  The city shall have the right to draw on the surety bond provided by the applicant or demand payment directly from the applicant or the owner, for the cost of such city work, including without limitation, legal fees and administrative expenses, based either on costs and expenses incurred by the city or on the city's reasonable estimates of costs to be incurred. 
(3)  The city shall give the applicant written or oral notice of seven days and an opportunity to cure to the applicant before taking such action; provided, however, that no such notice and opportunity to cure shall be required in the event of repeated violations or in the event that a condition on or near the subject property poses, in the determination of the building official, a threat of any kind to the public or safety. The applicant and the owner of the subject property shall be jointly and severally responsible for all costs and expenses incurred by the city, including without limitation attorney's fees and administrative expenses, in completing the demolition work. 
( Ord. No. 2014-09, § 7, 4-14-2014 ) 
Sec. 14-68. - Conduct of work. 
    Upon the issuance of a permit for demolition of a building or structure, the building or structure shall be promptly demolished or removed, provided, that all work done under the permit shall be subject to the supervision of the building official and to such reasonable restrictions as the building official may impose in regard to elements of safety and health. It shall be unlawful for the applicant or property owner to demolish or remove a building or structure from the premises in such a manner that there remain holes or depressions dangerous to the public safety or that there shall remain debris or rubbish on the premises. The applicant shall fill any existing holes left on the property, level the property, remove all debris and junk from the property and replant the property with appropriate vegetation within the time period designated by the building official. The acceptance of areas designated to be seeded shall be based upon the building official's determination that the property ground preparation, seeding, etc., has been accomplished and a satisfactory stand of grass has been established. If a satisfactory stand of grass is not established, the area shall be reseeded and mulched. A satisfactory stand of grass is defined as a living and growing area of grass of not less than 100 percent ground coverage. This may be deemed to include grass that is dormant during a cold or dry season but has roots which have taken hold in the soil and show sprouts that are capable of growing after the unfavorable period has passed. The building official may permit the applicant or owner to retain the foundation if it is safe to do so and the applicant, the owner or their agent either removes the foundation to a depth of 12 inches below grade or leaves an empty hard surface slab covering the foundation. The applicant or owner shall immediately repair or cause to be repaired any damage to public rights-of-way and utilities. 
( Ord. No. 2014-09, § 8, 4-14-2014 ) 
Sec. 14-69. - Penalty. 
    Any person, firm, corporation, partnership or other entity is adjudged guilty of violating any provisions of this article or any rule or regulation made pursuant to this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished as provided in the city's Code of Ordinances for such misdemeanor violation. This article shall be enforced by the building official or his or her designated agent. The application of the penalty shall not be construed to prevent removal of prohibited conditions. 
( Ord. No. 2014-72, § 9, 11-19-2014 ) 
Sec. 14-70. - Building and zoning code provisions. 
    Nothing in this article shall be construed to exempt property owners from complying with existing city building and zoning codes, nor prevent any property owner from making any use of his property not prohibited by other statutes, ordinances or regulations. 
( Ord. No. 2014-09, § 10, 4-14-2014 ) 
Chapter 18 - BUSINESSES[1]
