ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 18-1. - General business license ordinance adopted by reference. 
    Ordinance No. 2008-18, pertaining to business licenses, as now or hereafter amended, is hereby adopted as a part of this chapter as if set out at length in this section. 
( Ord. No. 2008-18, 12-22-2008 ; Ord. No. 2009-15, 5-14-2009 ; Ord. No. 2011-30, 11-28-2011 ; Ord. No. 2012-10, 5-14-2012 ; Ord. No. 2012-12, 6-25-2012 ; Ord. No. 2015-26 , § 1, 11-30-2015; Ord. No. 2017-01 , 2-27-2017; Ord. No. 2017-15 , 11-27-2017) 
Secs. 18-2-18-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - TRANSIENT LODGINGS 

Sec. 18-31. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Transient means a person to whom rooms or lodging are rented for a period of less than 30 continuous days. 
(Ord. No. 96-04, § 1(e), 2-26-1996) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 18-32. - Levy of license tax in city. 
(a)  There is hereby levied and imposed, in addition to all other taxes of every kind now imposed by law, a privilege or license tax upon every person engaging in the city in the business of renting or furnishing any room or rooms or lodgings to transients in any hotel, motel, inn, tourist camp, tourist cabin, or any other place in which rooms or lodgings are regularly furnished to transients for a consideration. Such license tax shall be in an amount equal to seven percent of the charge for such room, rooms, or lodgings, including the charge for use or rental of personal property and services furnished in such rooms; provided, however, that charges for property sold or services furnished which are required to be included in the computation of the tax levied in Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-23-1 et seq., such article being commonly referred to as the "state sales tax statutes," shall not be included in the computation of the license of tax levied in this section. 
(b)  The amount of license taxes specified in this section shall be in addition to all other licenses levied, and the license tax referred to in this section shall apply only to, and be measured only by, the charges for the rental of rooms or lodgings supplied to transients, and shall not apply to, or be measured by the charges for the rental of rooms or lodgings supplied for a period of 30 continuous days or longer. 
(Ord. No. 96-04, § 2, 2-26-1996; Ord. No. 2003-21, § 1, 9-22-2003; Ord. No. 2008-19, 12-22-2008 ) 
Sec. 18-33. - Imposition of privilege or license tax in police jurisdiction. 
(a)  There is hereby levied and imposed, in addition to all other taxes of every kind now imposed by law, a privilege or license tax upon every person engaging in the police jurisdiction of the city in the business of renting or furnishing any rooms or lodgings to transients in any hotel, motel, inn, tourist camp, tourist cabin, or any other place in which rooms or lodgings are regularly furnished to transients for a consideration. Such license tax shall be in an amount equal to 31/2 percent of the charge for such room, rooms, or lodgings, including the charge for use or rental of personal property and services furnished in such rooms; provided, however, that charges for property sold or services furnished which are required to be included in the computation of the tax levied in Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-23-1 et seq., such article being commonly referred to as the "state sales tax statutes," shall not be included in the computation of the license of tax levied in this section. 
(b)  The amount of license taxes specified in this section shall be in addition to all other licenses levied, and the license tax referred to in this section shall apply only to, and be measured only by, the charges for the rental of rooms or lodgings supplied to transients, and shall not apply to, or be measured by the charges for the rental of rooms or lodgings supplied for a period of 30 continuous days or longer. 
(Ord. No. 96-04, § 3, 2-26-1996; Ord. No. 2003-22, § 1, 9-22-2003; Ord. No. 2008-19, 12-22-2008 ) 
Sec. 18-34. - Due date of taxes and monthly reports. 
    The taxes levied under the provisions of this article, except as otherwise provided, shall be due and payable in monthly installments on or before the 20th day of the month next succeeding the month in which the tax accrues. On or before the 20th day of each month, every person on whom the taxes levied in this article are imposed, shall render to the city treasurer, on a form prescribed by the city treasurer, a true and correct statement showing the gross proceeds of the business subject to such tax for the then next preceding month, together with such other information that the city treasurer determines to be required for the administration of this article. At the time of making such monthly report the taxpayer shall compute the taxes due and shall pay to the city treasurer the amount of the taxes shown to be due. 
(Ord. No. 96-04, § 4, 2-26-1996) 
Sec. 18-35. - Credit collections. 
    Any person subject to the taxes levied in this article who conducts business on a credit basis may defer reporting credit rentals and charges until after their collection, and if he so defers reporting them, he shall thereafter include in each monthly report all credit collections made during the then preceding month and shall pay the amount of taxes measured thereby at the time of filing such report. 
(Ord. No. 96-04, § 5, 2-26-1996) 
Sec. 18-36. - Interest and penalty. 
    Any person who fails to pay the tax levied within the time required in this article shall pay, in addition to the tax, a penalty of ten percent of the amount of the tax due, together with interest thereon at the rate of one-half of one percent per month, or its fraction, from the date at which the tax levied became due and payable. Such penalty and interest shall be assessed and collected as part of the tax; provided, however, that the city council may, if a good and sufficient reason is shown, waive or remit the penalty or any portion of the penalty. 
(Ord. No. 96-04, § 6, 2-26-1996) 
Sec. 18-37. - Annual returns. 
    On or before 30 days after the end of each calendar year, each person subject to the taxes levied in this article shall file with the city treasurer a return, verified by oath, showing the gross proceeds of the business done during such calendar year, shall compute the amount of tax chargeable against such person in accordance with the provisions of this article, shall deduct the amount of monthly payments made as provided in this article, if any have been made, and pay to the city treasurer with such report the residue of the taxes levied in this article that are chargeable against such person. 
(Ord. No. 96-04, § 7, 2-26-1996) 
Sec. 18-38. - Recordkeeping. 
    It shall be the duty of every person engaging or continuing in this city in any business for which a privilege or license tax is imposed by this article, to keep and preserve suitable records of the gross sales, gross proceeds of sales, and gross receipts or gross receipts of sales of such business and such other books or accounts as may be necessary to determine the amount of tax for which he is liable under the provisions of this article. Such records shall be kept and preserved for a period of two years and shall be open for inspection at any reasonable time by the city treasurer or his duly authorized representative of the city. 
(Ord. No. 96-04, § 8, 2-26-1996) 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-23-9. 
Sec. 18-39. - Oaths. 
    The monthly reports required in this article to be submitted are not required to be made on oath, but the annual returns provided for in section 18-37 shall be sworn to by the taxpayer or his agent before some officer authorized to administer oaths. Any false statement of a material fact made with intent to defraud shall constitute perjury, and, upon conviction, the person so convicted shall be punished as provided by law. 
(Ord. No. 96-04, § 9, 2-26-1996) 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-23-10. 
Sec. 18-40. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Any person subject to the provisions of this article who, for any reason, fails to make the reports as required, who fails to keep the records as required, or who fails to pay the amount due the city within the time limits as required, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished as provided in section 1-11 for each offense, all as assessed by a court of competent jurisdiction. 
(Ord. No. 96-04, § 10, 2-26-1996) 
Secs. 18-41-18-70. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - TATTOO ESTABLISHMENTS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 18-71. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Certificate of inspection means written approval from the health officer that a tattoo establishment has been inspected and meets all the terms of this article relating to physical facilities, equipment and layout for operation of such business, as well as any county or state regulations pertaining to the operation of such business. 
    Operator means any individual, firm, company, corporation or association that owns or operates an establishment where tattooing is performed and any individual who performs or practices the art of tattooing on the person of another. 
    Tattoo, tattooed, tattooing means any method of placing indelible designs, letters, scrolls, figures, symbols or other marks upon or under the skin with dye, ink, pigment or any other substance resulting in the coloration of the skin by the aid of needles, scalpels or any other instruments designed to touch or puncture the skin. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 4, 9-14-1992) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 18-72. - Health and sanitary requirements. 
    Each person who operates a tattoo establishment shall comply with the following requirements: 
(1)  The room in which the tattooing is done shall have an area of not less than 100 square feet. The walls, floors, and ceiling shall have an impervious, smooth and washable surface. 
(2)  A toilet shall be located in the establishment and shall be accessible at all times that the tattoo establishment is open for business. The lavatory shall be supplied with hot and cold running water, soap and sanitary towels. 
(3)  All tables and other equipment shall be constructed of easily cleanable material, shall be painted or finished in a light color, with a smooth washable finish, and shall be separated from waiting customers or observers by a panel at least six feet high or by a door. 
(4)  The entire premises and equipment shall be maintained in a clean, sanitary condition and in good repair. 
(5)  The operator shall wash his hands thoroughly with antiseptic soap and water before starting to tattoo; the hands shall be dried with individual, single use towels. 
(6)  No tattooing shall be done on any skin surface that has any rash, pimples, boils, infections or manifests any evidence of unhealthy conditions. 
(7)  No skin area shall be penetrated, abraded or treated with chemicals for the purpose of removing, camouflaging or altering any blemish, birthmark, scar or tattoo. 
(8)  Safety razors with a new, single-service blade for each customer or patron or a straight razor may be used and shall be thoroughly cleaned and sterilized before use on each customer or patron. 
(9)  The area to be tattooed shall first be thoroughly washed for a period of two minutes with warm water to which has been added an antiseptic liquid soap. A sterile single-use sponge shall be used to scrub the area. After shaving and before tattooing is begun, a solution of 70 percent alcohol shall be applied to the area with a single-use sponge used and applied with a sterile instrument. 
(10)  Only petroleum jelly in collapsible metal or plastic tubes, or its equivalent as approved by the health officer, shall be used on the area to be tattooed and it shall be applied with sterile gauze. 
(11)  The use of styptic pencils, alum blocks, or other solid styptics to check the flow of blood is strictly prohibited. 
(12)  Inquiry shall be made, and anyone giving a history of recent jaundice, hepatitis, HIV virus or any other communicable disease may not be tattooed. 
(13)  Single-service or individual containers of dye or ink shall be used for each patron and the container therefor shall be discarded immediately after completing work on a patron and any dye in which the needles were dipped shall not be used on another person. Excess dye or ink shall be removed from the skin with an individual sterile sponge or a disposable paper tissue which shall be used only on one person and then the tattooed area shall be washed with sterile gauze saturated with an antiseptic soap solution approved by the health officer, or a 70 percent alcohol solution. The tattooed area shall be allowed to dry and petroleum jelly from a collapsible or plastic tube shall be applied, using sterile gauze. A sterile gauze dressing shall then be fastened to the tattooed area with adhesive. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 5, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 18-73. - Care of instruments. 
(a)  Storing of instruments. All clean and ready-to-use needles and instruments shall be kept in a closed glass or metal case or storage cabinet while not in use. Such cabinet shall be maintained in a sanitary manner at all times. 
(b)  Sterilizing of instruments. A steam sterilizer (autoclave) shall be provided for sterilizing all needles and similar instruments before use on any customer, person or patron. Alternate sterilizing procedures may only be used when specifically approved by the health officer. Sterilization of equipment will be accomplished by exposure to live steam for at least 30 minutes at a minimum pressure of 15 pounds per square inch, temperature of 240 degrees Fahrenheit or 116 degrees Celsius. 
(c)  Use of instruments. The needles and instruments required to be sterilized shall be so used, handled and temporarily placed during tattooing so that they will not be contaminated. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 6, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 18-74. - Recordkeeping. 
    Permanent records for each patron or customer shall be maintained by the licensee or operator of the establishment. Before the tattooing operation begins, the patron or customer shall be required personally to enter, on a record form provided for such establishments, the date, his name, address, date of birth, social security number, security number if a member of the armed forces, place of employment and his signature. Such records shall be maintained in the tattoo establishment and shall be available for inspection by the health officer. Records shall be retained by the operator or licensee for a period of not less than five years. In the event of a change of ownership or closing of the business, all such records shall be made available to the health officer. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 7, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 18-75. - Infections. 
    No person, customer or patron having any skin infection or other disease of the skin or any communicable disease shall be tattooed. All infections resulting from the practice of tattooing which become known to the operator shall promptly be reported to the health officer by the person owning or operating the tattoo establishment, and the infected client shall be referred to a physician. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 8, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 18-76. - Pigments and dyes. 
    All pigments, dyes, inks, colors, etc., used in tattooing shall be sterile and free from bacteria, virus particles and noxious agents or substances, and the pigments, dyes and colors used from stock solutions for each customer or patron shall be placed in a single-service receptacle, and such receptacle and remaining solution shall be discarded after use on each customer or patron. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 9, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 18-77. - Bandages and surgical dressings. 
    All bandages and surgical dressings used in connection with the tattooing of a person shall be sterile. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 10, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 18-78. - Inspections. 
    At reasonable times, the health officer may conduct periodic inspections of any tattoo establishment for the purpose of determining whether or not the establishment and the persons performing the art of tattooing therein are in compliance with all applicable health provisions of this article, as well as any other city, county or state provisions. It shall be unlawful for any person or operator of a tattoo establishment willfully to prevent or restrain the health officer from entering any licensed establishment where tattooing is being performed for the purpose of inspecting the premises, after proper identification is presented to the operator. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 12, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 18-79. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    In addition to the revocation and suspension of any license, any person violating any provision of this article shall be punished as provided in section 1-11 for each offense. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 13, 9-14-1992) 
Secs. 18-80-18-100. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE 

Sec. 18-101. - Required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of operating a tattoo establishment without first obtaining a license to engage in such business in accordance with the provisions of this division. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 1, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 18-102. - Application fee. 
    An application for a license shall be accompanied by a fee in the amount of $250.00; provided, however, that no application fee shall be required for renewal of an existing license. Any change of ownership shall require a new application and license, with payment of fees therefor. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 2, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 18-103. - Certificate of inspection. 
    An applicant for a license to operate a tattoo establishment shall first obtain a certificate of inspection from the health officer, indicating the establishment has been inspected and is in compliance with the provisions of this article or any other city, county or state regulations. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 11, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 18-104. - Fee. 
    The license fee for engaging in the business of operating a tattoo establishment within the city shall be $750.00. 
(Ord. No. 92-09, § 3, 9-14-1992) 
Secs. 18-105-18-140. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - TOBACCO PRODUCTS 

Sec. 18-141. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Cigarette means a roll of finely cut tobacco or any substitutes therefor enclosed in paper prepared for smoking by individuals. 
In addition to the definition of cigarettes found in Ordinance 92-02, cigarettes shall also include cigarillos, which are sold in packages. Cigarillos sold in packages shall be taxed as cigarettes and not as cigars. 
    Dealer means any wholesale dealer or retail dealer, as defined in this section. 
    Package means the individual box or other container from which or in which retail sales of tobacco products mentioned in this section are normally made or intended to be made. 
    Retail dealer means any person, firm or other entity, other than a wholesale dealer, who sells or delivers tobacco products within the city or the police jurisdiction of the city, and any person, firm or entity operating under a retail dealer's license. 
    Retail price means the retail selling price of the tobacco products before adding the amount of the tax assessed in this article or any tobacco tax assessed by the state. 
    Sold and sale mean any transfer of title or possession, or both, exchange or barter, conditional or otherwise, in any manner or by any means whatsoever for a consideration or any agreement therefor, including rewards, prizes or premiums of tobacco products given as a result of operations on punch boards, shooting galleries or other activities. 
    Stamps means the stamp or stamps by the use of which the taxes levied on cigarettes under this article are paid. 
    Store and stored mean the storage or warehousing of tobacco products in any manner, or the withdrawal or use of the same for any purpose, other than for resale or reshipment outside the city. 
    Tobacco products means cigarettes, cigars, chewing tobacco, smoking tobacco, snuff or any substitute of these products. 
    Wholesale dealer means a person who sells or delivers within the city, or its police jurisdiction, at wholesale only, tobacco products to retail dealers for the purpose of resale only. 
(Ord. No. 92-02, § 2, 4-27-1992; Ord. No. 2001-10, § 1, 9-24-2001) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 18-142. - Construction of article. 
(a)  This article shall not be construed to tax interstate commerce or any business of the United States government or any branch or agency. 
(b)  This article shall not be construed to apply to tobacco products stored for the purpose of resale or reshipment outside the city and its police jurisdiction and which are actually so resold or reshipped. 
(c)  This article shall not be construed to repeal any of the provisions of the general license provisions of the city, but shall be held to be cumulative. 
(d)  Whenever the requisite amount of stamps has been affixed to cigarettes and whenever the tax levied in this article on other tobacco products has been paid, this article shall not be construed to require additional stamps or additional tax. 
(Ord. No. 92-02, § 3, 4-27-1992) 
Sec. 18-143. - Levy of tax in city. 
    In addition to all taxes now imposed by law, every person who is engaged in the business of selling or delivering any tobacco products shall pay a license tax to the city, and a license tax is fixed and levied, which license tax shall be in the following amounts for the sale, storage and delivery of the following named tobacco products in the city: 
(1)  Cigarettes. A license tax in the police jurisdiction in the sum of $0.06 for each package containing 20 cigarettes or cigarillos (small cigars) or less. When cigarettes or cigarillos are packaged in cartons, this tax is for each package within the carton. 
(2)  Cigars, including cheroots and stogies. A license tax in the sum of $0.12 for each cigar, or substitute therefor, so sold, stored or delivered. 
(3)  Chewing tobacco. A license tax in the sum of $0.12 for each package of chewing tobacco prepared in such a manner as to be suitable for chewing only and not suitable for smoking so sold, stored or delivered. 
(4)  Smoking tobacco. A license tax in the sum of $0.12 for each package of smoking tobacco including granulated, plug cut, crimp cut, ready rubbed and other kinds and forms of tobacco prepared in such a manner as to be suitable for smoking in a pipe or cigarette so sold, stored or delivered. 
(5)  Snuff and other tobacco products used in a similar manner. A license tax in the sum of $0.12 for each package of all snuff and other tobacco products used in a similar manner, not smoked or chewed, so sold, stored or delivered. 
(Ord. No. 92-02, § 4, 4-27-1992; Ord. No. 2003-19, § 1, 9-8-2003; Ord. No. 2005-02A, 3-7-2005; Ord. No. 2005-03, 3-21-2005) 
Sec. 18-144. - Levy of tax in police jurisdiction. 
    In addition to all taxes now imposed by law, every person who is engaged in the business of selling, storing or delivering tobacco products within the police jurisdiction of the city shall pay a license tax to the city, and such license tax is hereby fixed and levied for the sale, storage or delivery of tobacco products in the police jurisdiction of the city in an amount equal to one-half of the amount levied for the sale, storage or delivery of tobacco products in the corporate limits of the city. 
(Ord. No. 92-02, § 5, 4-27-1992) 
Sec. 18-145. - Stamps sold by city clerk; inscription; sale to wholesalers and others. 
    The city clerk shall keep on hand for sale an adequate quantity of stamps to be affixed to each package of cigarettes in the denominations as required under this article. Each stamp shall have inscribed thereon the words "City of Valley - Tobacco Tax," but such words need not be arranged in the foregoing order, and may be abbreviated. Such stamps may be sold to wholesale dealers only by the city clerk at a price equal to 90 percent of the full amount, the remaining ten percent of such full amount representing compensation to the wholesale dealer for the labor of affixing such stamps to the packages in which the cigarettes are contained. Such ten percent compensation to be allowed to such wholesale dealer shall apply only to purchases of stamps having a face value of not less than $200.00. All other persons, except wholesale dealers, must pay the full face amount of the stamps, but no person shall be entitled to purchase any such number of stamps as shall cause the purchase price to include a fraction of a cent. 
(Ord. No. 92-02, § 6, 4-27-1992) 
Sec. 18-146. - Affixing stamps. 
    Before any cigarettes shall be sold, stored or delivered within the corporate limits of the city, or within its police jurisdiction, by any person, such person shall affix, or cause to be affixed, to each package of cigarettes a stamp obtained from the city clerk, in the amounts set out in this article in payment of the license taxes imposed by this article. Every person shall, within one hour after receipt of any cigarettes within the city, or within the police jurisdiction of the city, unless sooner offered for sale, cause stamps of the requisite amount of taxes to be affixed, as provided in this section, and shall cause the stamps to be canceled by writing or stamping with waterproof ink across the face of each stamp such registered number as shall be furnished to such person by the city clerk. After such stamping has been begun, it shall be continued with reasonable diligence by such person until all unstamped cigarettes shall have been stamped, and the stamps canceled as provided in this section, but no stamps required to be affixed to any package of cigarettes shall, after the stamps have been affixed as provided in this section, be again used in payment of any part of the tax levied under this article. In the case of cigarettes sold by retail in packages, the stamps shall be affixed to each individual package in such a way that such stamps shall be torn in two or mutilated when such package is opened. 
(Ord. No. 92-02, § 7, 4-27-1992) 
Sec. 18-147. - Records and reports of dealers; reports of violations. 
    Every wholesale dealer shall, at the time of selling or delivering tobacco products into the city or its police jurisdiction, make a true duplicate invoice of the sale or delivery, which shall show full and complete details of the sale or delivery of such tobacco products. Every wholesale and every retail dealer shall keep a record of the purchase, sale, exchange or receipt of tobacco products. All such invoices and records and all canceled checks and memoranda pertaining to any such purchase, sale, exchange or receipt of tobacco products shall be retained for a period of 18 months, and shall be subject to inspection by an agent of the city, who shall have the power and authority to enter upon the premises of any dealer at all reasonable times for the purpose of examining such invoices, records, canceled checks or other memoranda. Any person who purchases or receives, in any manner whatsoever, tobacco products which does not have stamps affixed in the manner required by this article shall, within three days after receipt of such tobacco products, report the receipt and purchase to the city clerk, giving the date of purchase or receipt, the name of the person from whom purchased or received, and a list describing the tobacco products so purchased or received. Such report must be made by registered or certified mail or in person. 
(Ord. No. 92-02, § 8, 4-27-1992) 
Sec. 18-148. - Taxes due and payable date. 
    The tax levied under the provisions of this article, on all tobacco products (with the exception of cigarettes), shall be due and payable in monthly installments on or before the 20th day of each month next succeeding the month in which the tax accrued. On or before the 20th day of each month, every wholesale dealer in tobacco products shall file with the city clerk a true and correct monthly statement in writing of all tobacco products (except cigarettes) sold, or delivered during the preceding months, for which he is or shall be liable for the payment of the license tax and shall, in each and every instance, upon the filing of a statement, furnish to the clerk such additional information, either oral or in writing, as the clerk may require as to the sale or delivery of any tobacco products covered by such statement and shall, at the time of making such statement, pay to the city clerk, for the city, the amount of the license tax for the preceding month covered by such statement. 
(Ord. No. 92-02, § 9, 4-27-1992) 
Sec. 18-149. - Prohibited acts. 
    Among others, the following acts and omissions shall be unlawful: 
(1)  It shall be unlawful for any person who is required by this article to affix stamps to cigarettes to fail to affix such stamps, or to cancel such stamps in the manner or within the time required by this article. 
(2)  It shall be unlawful for any person to sell, offer for sale, store or deliver within the city, or within its police jurisdiction, any cigarettes where stamps have not been affixed and canceled, as provided in this article. 
(3)  It shall be unlawful for any person to have in his possession or under his control any cigarettes where stamps have not been affixed in the manner as required by this article for more than six hours after receipt of such cigarettes on the premises of such person. The possession of each package of cigarettes not having proper stamps affixed as required by this article shall be deemed a separate offense. 
(4)  It shall be unlawful to manufacture, buy, sell, offer for sale, or possess, or to attempt so to do, any reproduction or counterfeit of the stamps provided for in this article, or to possess tools, implements, instruments or materials of any kind necessary or appropriate to reproduce or counterfeit such stamps, or to alter or cause to be altered any stamps provided for in this section. 
(5)  It shall be unlawful to remove from a package or otherwise prepare any stamp with intent to use or cause the same to be used, after it has already been used, or to buy, sell, offer for sale or give away any washed, removed, altered or restored stamp to any person, or to have in possession any such washed or restored or altered stamp, or, for the purpose of indicating payment of any tax under this article, to reuse any stamp which has theretofore been used for the payment of any tax provided in this article, or to sell any stamp provided for herein except as to sales made by the city clerk. 
(6)  It shall be unlawful to reuse or refill with cigarettes any package from which cigarettes have been removed and with respect to which the tax has theretofore been paid. 
(7)  It shall be unlawful for any person, who is in this article required to keep records, to fail or omit to keep the records in the manner provided in this article, or to refuse to permit the agent of the city to inspect the records at any reasonable hour, or to interfere with or obstruct the agent of the city in the making of any such inspection. 
(8)  It shall be unlawful for any person who is herein required to file statements with the city clerk, to fail or omit to make or file any statement provided in this section, within the time specified in this section, or to make any false statement therein, and any such offense shall be a continuing offense against the city, and each day during which such person shall sell, or deliver tobacco products in the city or police jurisdiction during such default, shall constitute a separate offense. 
(9)  It shall be unlawful for any person who is required to pay the license tax provided for in this article to fail or omit to pay the tax within the time specified in this article, and such offense shall be a continuing offense against the city, and each day during which such person shall sell, store or deliver tobacco products in the city or its police jurisdiction during such default shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 92-02, § 10, 4-27-1992) 
Sec. 18-150. - Inspection of machines. 
    The city inspector is hereby authorized to require the owner of any cigarette vending machine or the person in charge of the premises where such machine is located to open the machine for the purpose of permitting the examination of the cigarettes therein to ascertain if they are properly stamped. The failure or refusal to open the machine upon being ordered to do so shall be a misdemeanor. 
(Ord. No. 92-02, § 11, 4-27-1992) 
Sec. 18-151. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Any person violating the provisions of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished as provided for in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 92-02, § 12, 4-27-1992) 
Chapter 22 - CEMETERIES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 62. 
State Law reference- Exercise of police jurisdiction over cemeteries, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-22; municipal cemeteries and burial grounds, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-40 et seq.; death certificates, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-9A-14 et seq.; dead bodies, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-19-1 et seq.; location and extension of boundaries of cemeteries, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-20-4; funeral services, Code of Ala. 1975, § 34-13-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 22-1. - [Burial spaces for qualified indigent persons.] 
    The mayor and cemetery sexton shall be authorized to select and make available cemetery lots for indigent burial to persons deemed qualified by the mayor. Sufficient information shall be provided by the family or appropriate person seeking burial in order to determine the indigent status of the party seeking burial. The mayor is authorized to sign and deliver any appropriate cemetery deed to the nearest living relative seeking burial of the deceased relative. The deed will provide a reversionary clause should the person ever be disinterred. In addition, the transfer of the lot shall not obligate the city for any costs of burial. 
( Ord. No. 2013-02, 1-28-2013 ) 
Secs. 22-2-22-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - CEMETERY COMMITTEE; CEMETERY FUND[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Boards and commissions, § 2-161 et seq. 

Sec. 22-31. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Cemeteries means the Bethlehem, Fairfax, Langdale, River View, and Shawmut Cemeteries. 
(Ord. No. 95-29, § 1, 9-25-1995) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 22-32. - Purpose of article. 
(a)  It is the purpose of this article to create a City of Valley Cemetery Committee and a City of Valley Cemetery Fund. The City of Valley Cemetery Fund shall be sued to improve, enhance, conserve, preserve, maintain, and enlarge (if necessary) the Bethlehem, Fairfax, Langdale, River View, and Shawmut Cemeteries including, but not limited to, fences, monuments, burial plots, access roads, and landscapes. 
(b)  The City of Valley Cemetery Committee shall be authorized to solicit and receive donations to the City of Valley Cemetery Fund for the maintenance, improvement, preservation, conservation and enhancement of the cemeteries. 
(c)  The City of Valley Cemetery Committee shall promote the orderly, fair, and reasonable use of the remaining burial plots of the cemeteries and shall ensure donors that the cemeteries will be properly administered and maintained. 
(Ord. No. 95-29, § 1, 9-25-1995) 
Sec. 22-33. - City of Valley Cemetery Committee. 
(a)  The City of Valley Cemetery Committee shall be composed of the mayor and three members of the city council. Additionally, one ex officio member for each cemetery shall be appointed by the council to serve on the City of Valley Cemetery Committee for a term specified by the council. The city clerk shall be the secretary of the City of Valley Cemetery Committee, and the city treasurer shall be the treasurer of the City of Valley Cemetery Committee. 
(b)  The City of Valley Cemetery Committee is authorized to receive personal property including, but not limited to, money, bonds, stocks, checks, certificates of deposit, and real property. These donations may be held, invested, banked and/or sold. Donations may be received from individuals, estates, trusts, corporations, partnerships, associations, and/or any and all government bodies and agents. All donations shall be placed in the City of Valley Cemetery Fund. Donations of all types may be sold, invested or otherwise expended at the discretion of the City of Valley Cemetery Committee, provided that all proceeds are deposited into the City of Valley Cemetery Fund. 
(c)  The City of Valley Cemetery Committee may prepare a list of names, dates of birth, dates of death, and other relevant information concerning the individuals buried in the cemeteries. The committee may also create and maintain information on the owners of burial plots. A list of names of person buried in the cemeteries may be published for genealogical research and reference. 
(d)  The City of Valley Cemetery Committee shall maintain a central file, which shall be kept in the city hall. This file shall include all correspondence, transactions, records, minutes of meetings, and all other writings or copies pertaining to the administration of the City of Valley Cemetery Fund and to the administration of the cemeteries specified by this article. 
(e)  The City of Valley Cemetery Committee shall adopt such rules and procedures of conduct as it deems necessary, provided that such bylaws, rules, and procedures are consistent with the stated purposes and provisions of this article and do not violate state or federal laws. 
(Ord. No. 95-29, § 2, 9-25-1995) 
Sec. 22-34. - City of Valley Cemetery Fund. 
(a)  The City of Valley Cemetery Fund shall be independent of all other city accounts and funds and shall be dedicated to those activities specified within this article. 
(b)  The City of Valley Cemetery Committee may hold, exchange, transfer or convey donated properties at private or public property sales and may mortgage or otherwise encumber property in order to accomplish the purposes of the City of Valley Cemetery Committee and the City of Valley Cemetery Fund. Disclosure shall be made of all financial affairs and transactions related to the City of Valley Cemetery Fund. 
(c)  The City of Valley Cemetery Fund may be spent for surveying plots, creating and updating cemetery maps, locating boundaries and burial sites, preparing long range plans, hiring consultants to create cemetery plans or designs, employing a sexton, and paying for any expense of investment directly related to the care, operation and maintenance of the listed cemeteries. 
(Ord. No. 95-29, § 3, 9-25-1995) 
Sec. 22-35. - Administration of funds. 
(a)  Annual statements of receipts and expenditures shall be kept and made available at the city hall for review by any citizen, donor, prospective donor, descendent, owner, or other interested person. Names of donors who wish to remain anonymous shall not be disclosed. 
(b)  A list of donors shall be maintained by the administration of the city, but such list shall be confidential and for exclusive use by the city for the purpose of supporting the specified cemeteries. 
(Ord. No. 95-29, § 4, 9-25-1995) 
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2. 
Sec. 22-36. - Rules and regulations. 
    The rules and regulations contained herein apply to all city cemetery lot owners. The effective date of these rules and regulations shall be December 27th 2005, unless otherwise provided by additional ordinances. Rules and regulations specified by independent cemetery associations prior to this date or specified within burial lot deeds issued prior to this date remain in effect and are "grandfathered". Aside from these exceptions, these rules and regulations apply equally to all city cemetery users. 
I.  General. 
1.  The cemeteries will be open to visitors during the day but no visitors will be allowed after sunset or before sunrise. Children under 13 years of age must be accompanied by a responsible adult. 
2.  The speed limit on cemetery roads is five miles per hour. No parking will be allowed off paved or designated roads. 
3.  The City of Valley shall be notified at least 24 hours in advance of the day and time of a burial, to verify lot ownership, and approve the burial location. The City of Valley shall be given all pertinent information regarding the deceased and the responsible survivors prior to burial. 
4.  Flower receptacles shall be plastic, masonry, bronze or pottery. Glass, wood, paper and corrodible metal containers may not be used as flower receptacles. Flower receptacles should be placed next to the monument or grave marker, not on the grass. 
5.  Should lot owners desire to sell their unused lot(s), they must sell it to the City of Valley for the original purchase price. A lot may be transferred from one family member to another by notifying and obtaining approval of the City of Valley. This change must be shown on the original deed, or a new deed shall be required. Cost for changing or creating new deeds must be paid by the lot owner requesting the change. 
6.  Games, recreational activities, and social gatherings not associated with burials, memorial services, or grave visitations, are prohibited unless specifically approved by the City of Valley. 
II.  Interments and disinterments. 
1.  All interments shall be enclosed in a regular concrete or metal vault. Vaults of other constructions must be approved in writing by the City of Valley. Burial vaults shall be covered by at least 18 inches of soil. 
2.  No interment will be permitted in a grave space that has not been fully paid for. 
3.  No burial will be permitted unless a permit has been issued by the City of Valley. 
4.  No disinterment will be allowed until proper authority is given. 
5.  A cemetery lot is to be used only as a burial lot for human remains. 
6.  The City of Valley shall not be held responsible for interments in the wrong cemetery lot for cases in which the City of Valley was not involved in the location of the lot. 
III.  Monuments and markers. 
1.  All monument dealers and grave diggers operating within the City of Valley shall be licensed by the City of Valley. 
2.  All monument dealers and grave diggers operating within city cemeteries will be responsible for damage they may cause to cemetery property, markers, and/or monuments. 
3.  The City of Valley shall not be held responsible for scratches or marks on privately owned grave markers or monuments that may have occurred during normal maintenance or as a result of natural deterioration. 
4.  Headstones, and ground level flat bronze markers, will be permitted in all city owned cemeteries. 
5.  Headstones shall not exceed three feet six inches in height above the ground. 
6.  Each grave shall be properly marked within twelve months following burial with a headstone or flat marker made from granite, marble or bronze. 
IV.  Maintenance. 
1.  The City of Valley shall be responsible for maintenance and upkeep of its officially designated city cemeteries. 
2.  Lot owners may maintain their own lots, provided they adhere to the following city cemetery rules: 
(A)  Ground levels must not be altered. 
(B)  Grass must be cut on schedule coinciding with the city's cutting schedule. 
(C)  No mounds will be allowed over graves beyond three months from the burial date. 
(D)  No walls shall be built on or around burial lot(s). 
(E)  No shrubbery, trees, or flowers shall be planted on the lots. 
(F)  One single bench or seat made of marble, granite or concrete may be placed on a family lot. 
(G)  No signs, banners, flags or decorations, other than floral and American flags not exceeding 18 inches in height, shall be placed on lots unless the City of Valley has proclaimed a special memorial occasion for which special decorations may be used on a temporary basis. 
V.  Sexton. The duties and responsibilities of the city cemetery sexton shall include the following: 
1.  Furnish information to the City concerning sale of burial lots and any other information relating to record keeping. 
2.  Be available to show prospective burial lot buyers location of lots for sale. 
3.  Be available to assist family members and funeral directors in locating burial lots. 
4.  Monitor the condition of city cemeteries on a regular basis. 
(Ord. No. 95-29, § 5, 9-25-1995; Res. No. 2005-172R, Att., 12-27-2005) 
Chapter 26 - CIVIL EMERGENCIES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2; fire prevention and protection, ch. 34; law enforcement, ch. 46. 
State Law reference- Emergency management, Code of Ala. 1975, § 31-9-1 et seq.; local emergency management organizations, Code of Ala. 1975, § 31-9-9 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 26-1-26-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - EMERGENCY POWERS OF MAYOR 

Sec. 26-31. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Emergency management means as provided in Code of Ala. 1975, § 31-9-3(1). 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 26-32. - Article provisions operative during emergency. 
    The provisions of this article shall be operative only during the existence of a state of emergency management emergency. The existence of such emergency may be proclaimed by the governor of the state, or by the state legislature, pursuant to Code of Ala. 1975, § 31-9-8, or by resolution of the city council, if the city council in such resolution finds that a natural disaster of major proportions has actually occurred within the city and that the safety and welfare of the inhabitants of the city require an invocation of the provisions of this article. Any such emergency, whether proclaimed by the governor, by the legislature or by the city council, shall terminate upon the proclamation of the termination of such emergency by the governor or the passage by the legislature or by the city council of a resolution terminating such emergency. 
(Ord. No. 95-34, § 1, 10-9-1995) 
Sec. 26-33. - Powers enumerated. 
    During the period in which a state of emergency management emergency exists or continues, the mayor shall have and may exercise the following additional emergency powers: 
(1)  To enforce all laws, articles, rules and regulations relating to emergency management and to assume direct operational control of all emergency management forces and helpers in the city. 
(2)  To expend funds, make contracts, obtain and distribute equipment, materials and supplies for emergency management purposes. 
(3)  To procure by purchase, lease or other means, construct, store, maintain, renovate or distribute materials and facilities for emergency management without regard to the limitations of any existing ordinance or regulation. 
(4)  To appoint, employ or provide, with or without compensation, rescue teams, auxiliary fire, police and utility personnel and other emergency management workers. 
(5)  To assign and make available for duty all employees, property and equipment of the city. 
(6)  To alter and extend work schedules of all city employees and to authorize and approve overtime compensation for all city employees and temporary workers. 
(7)  To waive procedure and formalities otherwise required by law pertaining to the performance of public work, entering into contracts, the incurring of obligations, the employment of temporary workers, the utilization of volunteer workers, the rental of equipment, the purchase and distribution with and without compensation of supplies, materials and facilities and the appropriation and expenditure of public funds. 
(8)  To exercise any other power granted to the governor in Code of Ala. 1975, § 31-9-8 that may lawfully be granted to the mayor. 
(Ord. No. 95-34, § 2, 10-9-1995) 
Sec. 26-34. - Report by mayor of actions and contracts. 
    The mayor shall immediately make public all actions necessary to meet the state of emergency management emergency and shall report to the city council, without delay, all contracts he may let to meet such emergency. 
(Ord. No. 95-34, § 3, 10-9-1995) 
Chapter 28 - EMERGENCY SERVICES 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 28-1-28-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - AMBULANCES 
DIVISION I. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 28-31. - Purpose. 
    In order to ensure that the residents of the City of Valley continue to receive quality care rendered by emergency medical service providers (EMSP), to ensure quality control over the EMSP and to facilitate the prompt and coordinated dispatch of emergency transport units when needed to protect life, safety and health, and to further prompt the health, safety and welfare of its citizens, it is hereby declared that the City of Valley, Alabama designates the City of Valley, Alabama EMS Service as the medical service for all emergency and non-emergency calls within the city limits and the EMS service area pursuant to the procedures hereinafter stated. Additionally, the city EMS director will determine if the patient is to be transported by a private ambulance provider or by city EMS transport vehicle. The rules and regulations of private ambulances and municipal emergency and non-emergency transport vehicles in the city as set out herein are hereby established by the city council exercising sound legislative judgment. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 1, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-32. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Advanced Life Support (ALS). The use of equipment and procedures by any personnel licensed and authorized by the Alabama Department of Public Health for Advanced Life Support. 
    ALS transport vehicle. Any motor vehicle constructed, reconstructed, arranged, equipped, or used for the purposes of transporting the sick and injured. 
    Ambulance. Any motor vehicle constructed, reconstructed, arranged, equipped or used for the purpose of transporting ill, sick, injured or individuals in need of or requesting medical attention and meeting standards and requirements of the State of Alabama Department of Public Health. 
    Ambulance call. The act of proceeding with an ambulance for the purpose of transporting any patient for compensation. 
a.  Emergency. A response to a call in which it is believed that the illness, injury or disability requires immediate medical services wherein delay of such services may endanger personal health or safety. This call shall be accomplished with use of all warning devices and lights. 
b.  Non-emergency. A response that does not require the use of warning devices including but not limited to: inter-hospital transfers, discharges to home, visits to physician's offices and dialysis centers. 
    Emergency medical services provider. Any person who licensed as an EMSP, with the minimum level of EMT-Basic and who for compensation has the duty of performing or assisting in the performance of an ambulance call. 
    Basic life support. The use of equipment and procedures recognized by the Alabama Department of Public Health as being within the scope of practice of an EMSP. 
    911 dispatch center. The Chambers County Emergency Communications District. 
    Certificate. A certificate of public convenience and necessity. 
    City. The city council of Valley, Alabama. 
    Emergency. Any occurrence or situation involving illness, injury or disability requiring immediate medical services, wherein delay in the provisions of such services is likely to aggravate the condition and endanger personal health or safety. 
    911 dispatch center. The Chambers County Emergency Communications District which is the central communications center from which all E-911 dispatches originate for the City of Valley, Alabama. 
    EMS director. The EMS director for the City of Valley, Alabama. 
    Emergency medical services department. The EMS Service provided by the City of Valley, Alabama. 
    Emergency transport vehicle. Any motor vehicle operated by the City of Valley, Alabama EMS Department that meets the criteria for advanced life support and emergency transport. 
    Owner. A person engaged in business as the owner, manager, officer or proprietor of a company, firm or organization providing private ambulance service within the city. 
    Off line medical director. A physician licensed by the State of Alabama, who has been selected by the individual ambulance service or advanced life support service and approved by the regional EMS system to provide advice, consult and review techniques by the service to which he is an adviser. 
    Permit. The written authorization issued by the EMS director to the provisions of this article for designating that: 
(1)  A particular ambulance company has met the minimum requirements of the State of Alabama and all vehicles used for emergency transport have been inspected and found to be in compliance with the provisions of the Emergency Medical Service Rules, Alabama Department of Public Health, thereby authorizing its operation. 
(2)  A particular ambulance company has been issued a certificate of necessity from the city council. 
(3)  The ambulance company has applied for and has received a business license to operate in the City of Valley, Alabama. 
    Private ambulance . Any motor vehicle meeting the criterial designated by this article for ambulances which are owned and operated by a company or corporation doing business within the city. 
    State. The State of Alabama. 
    State of Alabama Office of EMS and Trauma. The Alabama State agency, within the Department of Public Health for the purpose of regulating emergency medical services in the State of Alabama. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 2, 12-5-2016) 
Secs. 28-33-28-50. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - AMBULANCE SERVICE IN GENERAL 

Sec. 28-51. - Certificate, permits and fees required. 
    No company shall operate an ambulance for hire on any street in the city until all of the following items are met: 
(1)  A certificate of public convenience and necessity has been approved by the city council and issued by the EMS director. 
(2)  The ambulance company permit fee has been paid. 
(3)  A City of Valley, Alabama license has been purchased. 
(4)  The EMS director has issued an ambulance company permit. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 3, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-52. - Emergency transport exceptions. 
    The City of Valley, Alabama EMS Department operations shall be exempt from all certificates, permits, business licenses and fees required by this article. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 3, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-53. - Certification required: exceptions. 
    No certificate of public convenience and necessity shall be required for any person operating emergency ambulance or other vehicles under the following conditions: 
(a)  Rendering assistance during any catastrophe or major emergency when the ambulance authorized to operate in the city by certificate are either insufficient in number or inadequate for any reason, as determined by the EMS director or his designee. 
(b)  Operating an ambulance brought in solely for the purpose of a drill or training exercise. 
(c)  Operating any ambulance rendering requested assistance authorized by the city in cases of disaster or major emergency. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 3, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-54. - Emergency transport service. 
    After the effective date of this article, the City of Valley EMS Department shall be the primary responder to all emergency and non-emergency calls of a medical nature. 
(a)  The emergency transport vehicle may transport any patient deemed appropriate by the medic and/or on-line medical control. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 3, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-55. - EMS director. 
(a)  It shall be the duty and responsibility of the EMS Director or his designee to administer the provisions of this article. 
(b)  Investigate or cause his designee to investigate all complaints within its authority, working with the regional and state EMS, involving any type of ambulance service within the city and take appropriate action where necessary. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 3, 12-5-2016) 
Secs. 28-56-28-75. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - PRIVATE AMBULANCE SERVICE 

Sec. 28-76. - Certificate of public convenience and necessity. 
    Application for a certificate of public convenience and necessity for operation of an ambulance within the city shall be in writing, signed to and sworn by the applicant, and shall be filed with the EMS director of the city or his duly authorized representative. This application shall be on a form prescribed by the EMS director and shall contain at least the following: 
(a)  The name and address of the applicant and the trade name under which the applicant does or proposes to do business; if the applicant is an individual, the name, age, and address of the applicant and the length of time the applicant has resided in the State of Alabama; or if a partnership or association, the business name thereof and the name, age and address of each partner and the length of time each partner has resided in the State of Alabama; or if a corporation, the names and addresses of all officers and directors of the corporation. 
(b)  The number of vehicles the applicant desires to operate and the chassis make, class (emergency, convalescent or combination), size, type (I, II or III) and color scheme of each vehicle. 
(c)  Whether or not the applicant has ever been convicted of any crimes directly or indirectly related to the duties and responsibilities of operating ambulances. 
(d)  Whether or not the applicant, his associates or employees have any claims or judgment against them for damages resulting from the negligent operation of any ambulance or any other vehicle. 
(e)  The nature and character of the service that the applicant proposes to render; then facts showing the demand for such service, the experience that the applicant has had in rendering such service and the period of time, if any, that he has rendered it in the city or other jurisdictions. 
(f)  Documentation from the applicant's insurance carrier, stating that the insurance required hereunder is available to the applicant and that such coverage is or will be provided prior to the issuance by the EMS director of the permit to operate hereunder. In this regard, such applicant shall be required to have in full force and effect an automobile liability insurance policy covering such ambulance providing coverage of not less than $1,000,000.00 for injury or damage to any one person and $1,000,000.00 for injury or damage to any number of persons arising out of any one accident resulting from the operation of such ambulance or ambulances. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-77. - Investigation of application. 
    Upon receipt of a properly filed application for a private ambulance service certificate of public convenience and necessity, the EMS director or his designee, shall cause an investigation to be made of the information provided in the application to determine if it is accurate and complete. The city council shall be provided the results of the investigation in writing. 
(a)  Whether or not the public convenience and necessity require the operation of such ambulance or ambulances. 
(b)  Whether the applicant will be able to provide ambulance service of such performance and quality as to best serve the public interest. 
(c)  The experience that the applicant has had in rendering ambulance service. 
(d)  The past experience of the applicant in satisfying judgments, if any, to claimants as a result of injuries received by reason of negligent operation of the ambulance. 
(e)  The financial ability of the applicant to respond to damages to property resulting from the negligent operation of an ambulance. 
(f)  The character and condition of the ambulance(s) and capabilities of ambulance attendant personnel to be used by the proposed ambulance business. 
(g)  Adequacy of the communication system to be used by the applicant. 
(h)  Whether adequate ambulance response time will be provided. 
    In the event the city council finds that the public convenience and necessity requires the issuance of such a certificate and that the applicant meets the required qualification and will be able to give proper and adequate service in the best interest of the inhabitants of the city, the mayor shall direct the EMS director or his designee to issue a certificate of public convenience and necessity to the applicant; said certificate of public convenience and necessity shall state any restrictions mandated by the city council, including but not limited to time periods and number of authorized ambulances. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-78. - Form, contents and issuance of certificate. 
    Every certificate issued hereunder shall be authorized by the city council, signed by the mayor, and attested by the city clerk, and shall contain, in addition to the name and address of the applicant, the number of vehicles authorized to be operated pursuant to such certificate along with the time limits or other restrictions which may be applicable. 
    The EMS director, upon receiving direction from the mayor to issue a certificate to an applicant for the operation of ambulances hereunder, shall issue a certificate to the applicant. A copy of every certificate issued shall be filed with and maintained by the EMS director and the city clerk. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-79. - Annual permit fees. 
    No permit for any ambulances shall be issued or confirmed unless the holder thereof has paid an annual permit fee of $800.00 for each vehicle to be operated in the city. The number of ambulances for which permits are issued shall not exceed the number authorized in the certificate of public convenience and necessity issued pursuant to this article. The permits required herein shall be valid for one calendar year, commencing January 1 st and ending December 31 st of each year, and any owner desiring to continue the operation of any ambulance shall make application for renewal of any and all permits issued hereunder prior to November 1 of any year for the privilege of operating during the following calendar year. The fee shall accompany the application and shall not be refundable. The amount of the permit fees hereunder prescribed shall not be pro-rated for fractional parts of a calendar year, nor shall it relieve the owner of the necessity of obtaining any state or county occupation licenses or complying with all other requirements established by statute. Each permit shall designate a specific ambulance and shall not be transferable or assignable without the prior written consent of the EMS director. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-80. - Causes for revocation, alteration or suspension of certificates or permits. 
    Every certificate or ambulance permit issued hereunder shall be subject to revocation, alteration or suspension by the city if any of the following conditions should occur: 
(a)  The public convenience and necessity no longer warrant such operation; 
(b)  The owner has refused to render the full service authorized by his certificate; 
(c)  The owner has been convicted of a crime which directly relates to the duties and responsibilities of the certified occupation; 
(d)  The certificate was obtained by an application in which any material fact was intentionally omitted or falsely stated; 
(e)  The owner has persisted in permitting his motor vehicles to be operated in violation of any law; 
(f)  The owner has willfully and knowingly violated or failed to comply with any of the provisions herein; 
(g)  The owner or his agent has, without good cause, induced or sought to induce a change of destination to or from a hospital or other place specified by the person hiring the ambulance; 
(h)  The owner or his agent has allowed the service to be operated in a negligent manner; 
(i)  The insurance coverage required herein has been canceled, reduced, withdrawn, suspended or terminated; 
(j)  The owner has allowed any of his vehicles or equipment to become damaged, deteriorated or unclean to the extent that it is unsatisfactory for public use; 
(k)  The owner fails to maintain the financial ability to comply with the terms of this article; 
(l)  The owner has failed to comply with the limitations imposed by the city council in the certificate; 
(m)  The owner has failed to comply with applicable federal, state or local laws or regulations. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-81. - Procedure for revocation, alteration or suspension of certificate or permit. 
    The EMS director or his duly authorized designee may at any time give notice in writing to the certificate or permit holder or person in control of the operation and maintenance of such ambulance services and the city clerk's office that the certificate issued for the operation and maintenance of such ambulance service has been suspended or revoked. The notice shall outline the reason or reasons for the suspension or revocation. The notice of suspension or revocation shall become final ten days after the notice of suspension or revocation is received unless on or before the expiration of such ten days the certificate holder shall file with the city clerk's office or the EMS director written notice of appeal of such suspension or revocation. The appeal shall operate as a stay of suspension or revocation of the certificate until such time as the city council shall grant a hearing and make a final adjudication which shall be appealable to the Circuit Court of Chambers County, Alabama. This hearing before the city council will be held not more than 30 days following the filing of a written notice of appeal. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-82. - Other state laws and regulations. 
    No portion of this article shall be construed in such a manner which is inconsistent with any federal, state or local law or regulation. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-83. - Private ambulance ALS. 
    Privately owned ambulance services within the city shall have the following ALS/emergency and non-emergency transport capabilities, duties and responsibilities: 
(a)  Inter-facility transfer of medically stable patients or ALS patients that require a paramedic to monitor fluids, EKG rhythms or administer medication. 
(b)  Patients who, during a routine non-emergency transport, develop problems that require a paramedic to perform ALS procedures. 
(c)  Continuation of ALS initiated outside the city limits and its police jurisdiction to a facility inside the city. 
(d)  Transport of those non-emergency patients who desire private ambulance service and who directly call the private organization to transport the individual to the facility of his or her choice. 
(e)  Assist the City of Valley Emergency Medical Service with patient care and transportation during situations involving mass casualties or when EMS units are unavailable. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-84. - Reimbursement of ambulance transport. 
    Private ambulance service shall be responsible for the billing and collection of fees from privately transported individuals. The city will not compensate private ambulance services for the private ambulance transportation services rendered. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-85. - Private ambulance service general rules and regulations. 
(a)  Central place of business. Each private ambulance service owner shall maintain a central place of business, within the City of Valley city limits, with at least one properly listed telephone for receiving all calls for ambulance service, where all business records and daily manifests herein required shall be maintained and available upon request and be generally responsible for the conduct and operation of its ambulance(s). Each owner shall, in writing, immediately notify the EMS director of any change of the business address or of the telephone number where said owner may be contacted at all times. 
(b)  Certificate holder's records and reports. Each certificate holder shall maintain a daily manifest upon which there shall be recorded the date, time call received and name of individual calling, time of arrival at requested location, place of origin, patient's name and address, designation and charges for each trip. Each such owner shall retain and preserve all daily manifests for at least 24 months and such manifests shall be available for inspection by the EMS director or his duly authorized designee upon request. Each certificate holder hereunder shall keep accurate records of the receipts and expenses from operations and such other operating information as may be required by the EMS director. Pre-hospital reports on all patients shall be retained for a period of not less than 90 days as shall all voice tapes of dispatches and instructions. Each such owner shall maintain such records at a place readily accessible for examination by the EMS director or his duly authorized designee. 
    Each certificate holder shall provide to the EMS director an annual statement which includes the following: 
(1)  A list of the company's current service fees; 
(2)  A list of any legal claims pending, or resolved in the past year; 
(3)  A statement showing the total number of calls made in the previous calendar year. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-86. - Operating regulation. 
(a)  Clean and sanitary bed linens shall be provided for each such patient carried and shall be changed after the discharge of each patient. 
(b)  Each ambulance shall have a minimum of two personnel, which shall consist of one paramedic and a minimum of one EMT-Basic, both of which must hold current licenses from the Alabama Department of Public Health. At least one member of the ambulance personnel shall remain in attendance with the patient being transported while the other may serve as the driver. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-87. - Standards for vehicle and equipment. 
(a)  All motor vehicles used for the purpose of providing ambulance service hereunder shall be designed and constructed to transport ill, sick or injured persons in comfort and safety, and shall be maintained in a clean, sanitary and first class mechanical condition at all times and comply with all applicable federal, state and local laws. 
(b)  All motor vehicles used for the purpose of providing ambulance services hereunder shall be equipped according to the current federal, state and local laws. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-88. - Radio dispatcher procedure. 
(a)  In the event an owner receives a private call for ambulance service which is an emergency nature, immediately after receiving such call, said owner shall report to the 911 dispatch center such call, giving the location and nature of the call, if known, and request clearance to use their warning devices giving both the location of the incident and, when determined, the destination of the patient. It shall be unlawful for private ambulance personnel or the owner to make an emergency ambulance call on the city streets without (I) having been requested by a private individual, City of Valley or 911 dispatcher and (2) subsequently being given route clearance by the dispatch center. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-89. - Use of emergency warning devices. 
(a)  All private ambulances responding to emergency calls outside the city must obtain route clearance from the 911 dispatch center to travel and operate ambulances and warning devices on city streets. 
(b)  After a private ambulance has responded to an apparent non-emergency call and arrived at the point of pick up, it shall be unlawful for the ambulance to proceed to the hospital or other destination with the use of emergency warning equipment except where serious medical conditions exist. The 911 dispatcher, however, must be notified by the private ambulance personnel of the circumstances surrounding the call and the need to use emergency warning equipment upon the city streets. 
(c)  No clearance shall be necessary for patients being transported from a point of pick up to a physician's office, clinic or nursing home, nor shall a clearance be necessary for the transport of a deceased patient from the point of pickup to any funeral home or morgue, but emergency warning equipment is not authorized for such transport. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-90. - Professional conduct. 
    All personnel employed by the owner hereunder, including all persons involved with billing and collection services shall, at all times, conduct themselves in an official and professional manner. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-91. - Private ambulance personnel. 
(a)  Qualifications of applicants for EMSP. 
(1)  EMSP Applicants shall meet the following minimum requirements: 
a.  Each EMSP must be the holder of a current valid driver's license. 
b.  Each EMSP must possess a current, valid EMS license issued by the Alabama Department of Public Heath that identifies their level of certification. No one may perform the duties of EMSP in the city without a current, valid state EMS license. 
c.  Each EMSP must be able to speak, read and write the English language. 
d.  Each EMSP shall not have been convicted of a crime that directly relates to the duties and responsibilities of the EMSP. 
e.  Each EMSP shall not be less than 18 years of age. 
f.  The owner is required to ensure that all EMSP's meet the criteria established herein. 
g.  The EMS director may establish a permit system which relates to the qualifications of an EMSP following the determination that such is warranted. Said minimum requirements shall be updated from time to time by the EMS director. It shall be the responsibility of the EMS director to provide each licensed ambulance operator with a list of any updated requirements not less than 60 days prior to the implementation of each updated minimum requirements. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-92. - Unlawful operation and prohibited acts. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to intentionally or knowingly: 
(1)  Follow any ambulance, police car or fire apparatus which is traveling in response to an emergency call within the city limits and police jurisdiction of the city or to follow any ambulance to or near the scene of any emergency call on the streets of the city. 
(2)  Solicit on the streets of the city or within the police jurisdiction of the city the business or transporting injured or sick persons. This prohibition shall not be construed to prohibit lawful advertisements. 
(3)  Intercept any communication concerning any emergency medical incident on the streets of the city or within the police jurisdiction of the city and divulge or publish the existence, contents, substance, purpose, effect or meaning of such intercepted communication and no such solicitor, owner or person, not being entitled thereto, shall receive or assist in receiving any such message emanating through the radio medium of the police or EMS dispatcher for his own benefit or for the benefit of another solicitor, owner or person in the business of furnishing ambulance service. 
(4)  Use of a vehicle siren or flashing light(s) other than brake lights without prior authorization by the Chambers County 911 Center. 
(5)  Use of a uniform, insignia, badge, title, identification card or vehicle marking that so closely resembles or mimics those of the City of Valley EMS Department as to confuse the public. 
(6)  Own or cause to be operated an ambulance on any street of the city or within the police jurisdiction of the City of Valley, Alabama without first having obtained a permit therefore in accordance with this article or unless exempted therefrom by the provisions of this article. 
(7)  Request the services of any ambulance which is not licensed or permitted in accordance with the provisions of this article or exempted therefrom by the provisions of this article. 
(8)  Perform duties as an EMSP without meeting the qualifications of this section 28-91. 
(9)  Permit or allow a person to perform duties as an EMSP without meeting the qualifications of section 28-91. 
(10)  Give false information to induce the dispatch of an ambulance. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Sec. 28-93. - Penalties. 
(a)  Any person who violates any provision of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor punishable by a fine not to exceed $500.00 and/or six months in jail. 
(b)  Each violation of this article shall constitute a separate offense. 
(c)  This section shall not serve to limit any other remedies available to the city in law or equity. 
( Ord. No. 2016-14 , Art. 4, 12-5-2016) 
Chapter 30 - ENVIRONMENT[1] 
Footnotes:
