(12)  Receive donations, grants, funds or gifts of historic property; 
(13)  Purchase, sell, contract to purchase, contract to sell, own, encumber, lease, mortgage and insure real and personal property in carrying out the purposes and responsibilities of the commission; the commission shall not obligate the city without prior consent of the city council; 
(14)  Review and make comments to the state historical commission concerning the nomination of properties within its jurisdiction to the National Register of Historic Places; 
(15)  Investigate, survey and process nominations of properties to the National Register of Historic Places; 
(16)  Investigate, survey and process applications for certification of historic properties for tax credits for preservation expenditures; 
(17)  Participate in private, state and federal historic preservation programs and with the consent of the city council, enter into agreements with the same to perform historic preservation related functions. 
(Ord. No. 92-09A, § 3(C), 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 42-36. - Annual reports of commission activities. 
    The commission shall prepare and file with the city council and with the state historical commission, an annual report of its activities as required by the city council and the state historical commission, covering the period from October 1 to September 30 of each year, which report shall be submitted in October of each year. The report shall include such items as the number of cases reviewed, historic district and property designations made, revised resumes of commission members/staff, appointments to the commission, attendance records and all minutes relating to the review of National Register nominations. The report shall document attendance at the orientation/training session as specified in section 42-40. 
(Ord. No. 92-09A, § 3(D), 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 42-37. - Conflict of interest. 
    At any time the commission reviews a project in which a member of the commission has ownership or other vested interest, that member will be prohibited from presenting, voting or discussing the project, other than answering a direct question. 
(Ord. No. 92-09A, § 3(E), 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 42-38. - Records of meetings. 
    A public record shall be kept of the commission's resolutions, proceedings and actions. 
(Ord. No. 92-09A, § 3(F), 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 42-39. - Responsibilities of members. 
    Each commission member, and anyone serving the commission in a technical/professional staff capacity, shall be required to attend at least two informational or educational meetings per year pertaining to historic preservation. Such meetings may include those sponsored by the state historical commission, board of advisors, the National Trust for Historic Preservation or a local preservation organization. One of the two should be a regional or statewide meeting. 
(Ord. No. 92-09A, § 3(G), 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 42-40. - Liaison between commission and the state historic preservation office (state historic commission). 
    Should the city council elect to become a certified local government, the city council shall designate a paid member to the city's staff or a person working under contract as a source of technical/administrative/professional assistance to be responsible for the operations of the commission in keeping with the requirements of certification for participation in the certified local government program. At least one member of the commission and/or the person serving as the commission's technical staff, and/or a representative appointed by the mayor who has an ongoing relationship with the commission, will attend the state certified local government orientation/training session sponsored by the state historical commission each year. 
(Ord. No. 92-09A, § 3(H), 9-14-1992; Ord. No. 94-04, 2-14-1994; Ord. No. 95-04, 2-27-1995) 
Sec. 42-41. - Recommendation and designation of historic districts and properties. 
(a)  Preliminary research. The commission shall compile and collect information and conduct surveys of historic resources within the city. After compiling and collecting this information, the commission shall present to the city council recommendations for historic districts and properties; provided, however, that prior to the commission's recommendation of a historic district or historic property to the city council for designation, the commission shall prepare a report consisting of: 
(1)  A physical description; 
(2)  A statement of the historical, cultural, architectural and/or aesthetic significance; 
(3)  A map showing district boundaries and classification (i.e., historic, nonhistoric, intrusive) of individual properties therein, and showing boundaries of individual historic properties; 
(4)  A statement justifying district or individual property boundaries; and 
(5)  Representative photographs. 
(b)  Designation of a historic district. 
(1)  Criteria for selection of historic districts. A historic district is a geographically definable area, which contains buildings, structures, sites, objects, landscape features and works or art or a combination, which: 
a.  Represents one or more periods, styles or types of architecture typical of one or more eras in the history of the municipality, county, state or region; 
b.  Represents a significant aspect of the cultural, political, economic, military or social history of the locality, region, state or nation; 
c.  Has had a significant relationship with the life of a historic person or event, representing a major aspect of the history of the locality, region, state or nation; 
d.  Is a part of the historic, architectural, archaeological or aesthetic heritage of the locality, region, state or nation; 
e.  Contains vernacular structures which contribute to an overall character and sense of place which is representative of the city. 
(2)  Boundaries of a historic district. Boundaries of a historic district shall be shown on the official zoning map or other map of the city which is designated as a public record. 
(3)  Evaluation of properties within historic districts. Individual properties within historic districts shall be classified as: 
a.  Historic (contributes to the district); 
b.  Nonhistoric (does not contribute but does not detract from the district); 
c.  Intrusive (detracts from the district). 
(c)  Designation of a historic property. 
(1)  Criteria for selection of historic properties. A historic property is a building, structure, site, object, work of art, including the adjacent area necessary for its proper appreciation or use, deemed worthy of preservation by reason of value to the city for one of the following reasons: 
a.  It is an outstanding example of a structure representative of its era. 
b.  It is one of the few remaining examples of past architectural style. 
c.  It is a place or structure associated with an event or persons of historic or cultural significance to the city, state or the region. 
d.  It is a site of natural or aesthetic interest that is continuing to contribute to the cultural or historical development and heritage of the city, county, state or region. 
e.  The building or structure is an example of an architectural style, or combination of architectural styles, which is representative of the city or which is unique to the city. 
(2)  Boundary description. Boundaries shall be shown on the map of the city which is designated as a public record. 
(d)  Requirements for adopting an ordinance for the designation of historic districts and historic properties. 
(1)  Application for designation of historic districts or property. Designations may be proposed by the city council, the commission, or a historical society, neighborhood association or group of property owners may apply to the commission for designation. 
(2)  Required components of a designation ordinance. Any ordinance designating any property or district as historic shall: 
a.  List each property in a proposed historic district or describe the proposed individual historic property; 
b.  Set forth the names of the owners of the designated properties; 
c.  Require that a certificate of appropriateness be obtained from the commission prior to any material change in appearance of the designated property; and 
d.  Require that the property or district be shown on the map of the city and kept as a public record to provide notice of such designation. 
(3)  Required public hearings. The commission shall hold a public hearing on any proposed article for the designation of any historic district or property. Notice of the hearing shall be published in at least three consecutive issues in the principal newspaper of the local circulation, and written notice of the hearing shall be mailed by the commission to all owners and occupants of such properties. All such notices shall be published or mailed not less than ten, nor more than 20 days prior to the date set for the public hearing. A notice sent by ordinary mail to the last known owner of the property shown on the county tax records and a notice sent by ordinary mail to the address of the property to the attention of the occupant shall constitute legal notice to the owner and occupant under this article. 
(4)  Recommendations on proposed designations. A recommendation to affirm, modify or withdraw the proposed ordinance for designation shall be made by the commission within 15 days following the public hearing and shall be in the form of a resolution to the city council. 
(5)  City council action on commission recommendation. Following receipt of the commission's recommendation, the city council may adopt the ordinance as proposed, may adopt the ordinance with any amendments it deems necessary, or may reject the ordinance. 
(6)  Notification of adoption of ordinance for designation. Within 30 days following the adoption of the ordinance for designation by the city council, the owners and occupants of each designated historic property, and the owners and occupants of each structure, site or work of art located within a designated historic district shall be given written notification of such designation by the commission, which notice shall apprise the owners and occupants of the necessity of obtaining a certificate of appropriateness prior to the undertaking any material change in appearance of the historic property designated or within the historic district designated. A notice sent by ordinary mail to the last known owner of the property of the property shown on the county tax records and a notice sent by ordinary mail to the address of the property to the attention of the occupant shall constitute legal notice to the owner and occupant under this article. 
(7)  Notification of other agencies regarding designation. The commission shall notify all municipal agencies within the city of the ordinance for designation. 
(8)  Moratorium on applications for alteration or demolition while ordinance for designation is pending. If an ordinance for designation is being considered, the commission shall have the authority to freeze the status of the involved property. 
(Ord. No. 92-09A, § 4, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 42-42. - Application to City of Valley Historic Preservation Commission for certificate of appropriateness. 
(a)  Approval of alterations, demolitions or new construction in historic districts or involving historic properties. After the designation by ordinance of a historic property or of a historic district, no historic property may be demolished, no building or structure in a historic district may be erected or demolished and no material change in the exterior appearance of such historic property, or of a structure, site, object or work of art within such historic district, shall be made or be permitted to be made by the owner or occupant, unless or until the application for a certificate of appropriateness has been submitted to and approved by the commission. 
(b)  Approval of new construction within designated districts. The commission shall issue certificates of appropriateness to new structures constructed within designated historic districts if these structures conform in design, scale, building materials, setback and landscaping to the character of the district specified in the design criteria developed by the commission. 
(c)  Approval of signs within designated districts. Signs shall be considered as structures and no sign on a historic property or in a historic district shall be changed, erected or demolished unless and until a certificate of appropriateness is approved by the commission. 
(d)  Approval of alterations or demolitions of public property within historic districts or public property which has been designated as a historic property. The requirement of a certificate of appropriateness shall apply to public property which has been designated as a historic property or which is contained in a historic district, and shall apply to all actions by public authorities which involve historic properties and properties within historic districts. 
(e)  Approval of painting originally unpainted surfaces. The painting of originally unpainted surfaces shall require a certificate of appropriateness. 
(f)  Interior alterations. In its review of applications for certificates of appropriateness, the commission shall not consider interior arrangement or use having no effect on exterior architectural features. 
(g)  Failure to maintain a historic property. Demolition by neglect and the failure to maintain a historic property or a structure in a historic district shall constitute a change for which a certificate of appropriateness is necessary. 
(h)  Guidelines and criteria for certificates of appropriateness. The commission shall adopt rules and regulations setting forth the procedure for submission and consideration of applications for certificates of appropriateness. The commission shall also adopt general design standards which shall apply in considering the granting and denial of certificates of appropriateness. Design standards shall be in compliance with the Secretary of the Interior's Standards for Historic Preservation Projects, including the Secretary's Standard for Rehabilitation. 
(i)  Submission of plans to commission. An application for a certificate of appropriateness shall be accompanied by such drawings, photographs, plans or other documentation as may be required by the commission. Applications involving demolition or relocation shall be accompanied by the post-demolition or relocation plans for the site. 
(j)  Acceptable commission reaction to applications for certificate of appropriateness. 
(1)  The commission shall approve the application and issue a certificate of appropriateness if it finds that the proposed material change in appearance would not have a substantial adverse effect on the aesthetic, historic or architectural significance and value of the historic property or the historic district. In making this determination, the commission shall consider, in addition to any other pertinent factors, the historical and architectural value and significance, architectural style, general design arrangement, texture and material of the architectural features involved and their relationship to the exterior architectural style and pertinent features of the other structures in the immediate neighborhood. 
(2)  The commission shall deny a certificate of appropriateness if it finds that the proposed material change in appearance would have substantial adverse effects on the aesthetic, historic or architectural significance and value of the historic property or the historic district. The commission shall not grant certificates of appropriateness for demolition or relocation without reviewing at the same time the post-demolition or post-relocation plans for the site. 
(k)  Public meetings and hearings on applications for certificates of appropriateness; notices and right to be heard. Applications for certificates of appropriateness shall be considered by the commission at public meetings, held at publicly accessible locations and times as may be designated and publicly announced by the commission or one of its officers. At least seven days prior to the review of a certificate of appropriateness, the commission shall take such action as may reasonably be required to inform the owners of any property likely to be affected by reason of the application, and shall give any applicant and such owners an opportunity to be heard. In cases where the commission deems it necessary, it may hold a public hearing concerning the application. 
(l)  Deadline for approval or rejection of application for certificate of appropriateness. 
(1)  The commission shall approve or reject an application for a certificate of appropriateness within 45 days after the filing by the owner or occupant of a historic property, or of a historic structure, site, object of work of art located within a historic district. Evidence of approval shall be by certificate of appropriateness issued by the commission. Notice of the issuance or denial of a certificate of appropriateness shall be sent by ordinary mail to the applicant and all other persons who have requested such notice in writing filed with the commission. 
(2)  Failure of the commission to act within 45 days shall constitute approval, and no other evidence of approval shall be needed. 
(m)  Necessary actions to be taken by commission upon rejection of application for certificate of appropriateness. 
(1)  If the commission rejects an application, it shall state its reasons for doing so, and shall transmit a record of such actions and reasons, in writing, to the applicant. The commission may suggest alternative courses of action it thinks proper if it disapproves of the application submitted. The applicant, if he so desires, may make modifications to the plans and may resubmit the application at any time after doing so. 
(2)  In cases where the application covers a material change in the appearance of a structure which would require the issuance of a building permit, the rejection of the application for a certificate of appropriateness by the commission shall be binding upon the building official or other administrative officer charged with issuing building permits, and, in such cases, no building permit shall be issued. 
(n)  Appeals. Any person having a request for a certificate of appropriateness denied by the commission, or architectural review board as provided in section 42-44, may appeal such denial to the county circuit court. 
(o)  Recording of applications for certificate of appropriateness. The commission shall keep a public record of all applications for certificates of appropriateness and of all the commission's proceedings in connection with the application. 
(p)  Requirements of conformance with certificate of appropriateness. 
(1)  All work performed pursuant to an issued certificate of appropriateness shall conform to the requirements of such certificate. If work is performed not in accordance with such certificate, the commission shall issue a cease and desist order and all work shall cease. 
(2)  The city council or the commission shall be authorized to institute any appropriate action or proceeding in a court of competent jurisdiction to prevent any material change in appearance of a designated historic property or historic district, except those changes made in compliance with the provisions of this article or to prevent any illegal act or conduct with respect to such historic property or historic district. 
(q)  Certificate of appropriateness void if construction not commenced. A certificate of appropriateness shall become void unless construction is commenced within six months of the date of issuance. Certificates of appropriateness shall be issued for a period of 18 months and are renewable. 
(r)  Technical advice. The commission shall have the power to seek technical advice from outside its members on any application. 
(Ord. No. 92-09A, § 5, 9-14-1992; Ord. No. 95-04, 2-27-1995) 
Sec. 42-43. - Maintenance of historic properties. 
(a)  Expedited review procedures for approval of routine maintenance. The commission may adopt expedited review procedures for approval of routine maintenance to historic properties or to buildings or structures in historic districts. Routine maintenance to historic properties includes ordinary maintenance or repair of any exterior architectural or environmental feature in or on a historic property to correct deterioration, decay or damage, or to sustain the existing form that does not involve a material change in design, material or outer appearance. Expedited review procedures shall waive the requirements for submission of an application for a certificate of appropriateness and for consideration at a public meeting. 
(b)  Failure to provide ordinary maintenance or repair. Property owners of historic properties or properties within historic districts shall not allow their buildings to deteriorate by failing to provide ordinary maintenance or repair. The commission shall be charged with the following responsibilities regarding deterioration by neglect: 
(1)  The commission shall monitor the condition of historic properties and existing buildings in historic districts to determine if they are being allowed to deteriorate by neglect. Such conditions as broken windows, doors and openings which allow the elements and vermin to enter, the deterioration of exterior architectural features, or the deterioration of a building's structural system shall constitute failure to provide ordinary maintenance or repair. 
(2)  If the commission determines a failure to provide ordinary maintenance or repair, the commission will notify the owner of the property and set forth the steps which need to be taken to remedy the situation. The owner of such property will have 30 days in which to do this. 
(3)  If the condition is not met in 30 days, the owner shall be punished as provided in section 42-46, and, at the direction of the city council, the commission may perform such maintenance or repair as is necessary to prevent deterioration by neglect. The owner of the property shall be liable for the cost of such maintenance and repair performed by the commission. 
(Ord. No. 92-09A, § 6, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 42-44. - Architectural review board. 
(a)  Creation. The city council may elect to create an architectural review board, hereafter called the board, to perform the duties and responsibilities of the commission in accepting, considering and approving or rejecting applications for certificates of appropriateness as set out in sections 42-42 and 42-43. 
(b)  Board membership; number; appointment; terms; compensation; officers; rules and regulations. 
(1)  If such a board is created, it shall be composed of not less than five members, who shall have demonstrated training or experience in the fields of history, architecture, architectural history, urban planning, archaeology or law. Members of the board need not be residents of the city. No member of the city council or the mayor shall serve as members of the board. Members of the board shall be nominated by the mayor of the city and appointed by the city council. Except for the original members of the board, members of the board shall serve three-year terms and shall be appointed in such manner as to serve overlapping terms. Two of the original members of the board shall be appointed to serve one-year terms, and the remainder of the original members of the board shall be appointed to serve three-year terms. Members of the board may be reappointed. 
(2)  Members of the board may be removed for cause by the city council. 
(3)  Vacancies on the board shall be filled by persons nominated by the mayor of the city and appointed by the city council. Such appointments shall be for the unexpired term of the member replaced. 
(4)  Members of the board shall elect a chair and vice-chair and such other officers as the members deem necessary. The board shall adopt rules of procedure and shall communicate those rules of procedure to the city council and the mayor. The rules of procedure of the board shall specify what number of members of the board shall constitute a quorum. 
(5)  Members of the board shall serve without compensation, but may be reimbursed for reasonable expenses incurred on behalf of the board, in accordance with the rules and regulations for the reimbursement of expenses adopted by the board. 
(6)  The board may employ such professional, technical, office and other personnel, as may be necessary, to carry out the purposes and responsibilities of the board. 
(7)  Meetings of the board shall be public meetings and shall be at designated times and places as specified in the commission's resolution creating the board. 
(8)  If, in the opinion of the city council, the work load of the board is, or is contemplated to be excessive, the city council may create more than one board, and designate the historic properties and historic districts with which each board will be concerned. Each historic property and each historic district designated by the city council shall be subject to the control of only one board. Each such board created shall have all of the powers and authority set forth in this article with respect to the historic properties and historic districts with which it is concerned. 
(Ord. No. 92-09A, § 7, 9-14-1992) 
Sec. 42-45. - Building and zoning codes. 
    Nothing in this article shall be construed as to exempt property owners from complying with existing city building and zoning codes, nor to prevent any property owner from making any use of his property not prohibited by other statutes, ordinances or regulations. 
(Ord. No. 92-09A, § 8, 9-14-1992) 
Cross reference- Buildings and building regulations, ch. 14; zoning, ch. 82. 
Sec. 42-46. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Violations of any provisions of this article shall be punished as provided in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 92-09A, § 9, 9-14-1992) 
Chapter 46 - LAW ENFORCEMENT[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2; civil emergencies, ch. 26; offenses and miscellaneous provisions, ch. 50; traffic and vehicles, ch. 70. 
State Law reference- Chief of police authorized, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-5; establishment, organization, etc., of police force, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-55; civil service merit systems, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-180 et seq.; law enforcement officers generally, Code of Ala. 1975, § 36-21-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 46-1-46-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - SUMMONS AND COMPLAINT IN LIEU OF ARREST 

Sec. 46-31. - Authorization. 
    Any law enforcement officer of the city, instead of placing a person under custodial arrest, may issue a summons and complaint against a person charged with any crimes for which such a summons is permitted, including violation of littering ordinances, leash laws, and class C misdemeanors not involving violence, threat of violence, or alcohol or drugs. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 1, 8-30-1999) 
Sec. 46-32. - Form of summons and complaint. 
    For the purpose of this article, the city authorizes the use of the uniform nontraffic citation and complaint form which is attached to Ordinance No. 99-09. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 2, 8-30-1999; Ord. No. 00-13, 9-11-2000) 
Sec. 46-33. - Procedure for arrest. 
    The procedure for issuing a citation is that, when an arrest is to be made, the arresting officer releases the person upon his written promise to appear in court at the designated time and place. If the person refuses to sign the citation and appear in court, the officer is to take the person into custody and bring him before any officer or official authorized to approve a bond. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 3, 8-30-1999) 
Sec. 46-34. - Penalty for violation of certain ordinances. 
(a)  Attached to Ordinance No. 99-09 is an exhibit which sets forth the penalty provisions of all municipal ordinances in force on the effective date of Ordinance No. 99-09. It is the intention of this article that these penalties, to be enforced by the uniform nontraffic citation and complaint form, are limited to those penalties provided by city ordinance. These fines or penalties shall be applicable at the time of a guilty plea or trial before the magistrate. The general penalty provision of any ordinance will not exceed that established under state law for the commission of a substantially similar offense, or as provided for in the applicable city ordinance pertaining to that offense. 
(b)  As required by the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-9.1(e), before implementing the summons and complaint procedure, the schedule of fines and penalties for city ordinances which may be prosecuted under this procedure shall be posted by the city clerk in a conspicuous place to the public within the district court clerk's office, city clerk's office and city police department. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 4, 8-30-1999) 
Secs. 46-35-46-70. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - CAPTURED PERSONAL PROPERTY 

Sec. 46-71. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Captured personal property means any personal property, as defined in Code of Ala. 1975, § 1-1-1(8), taken into the custody of a police officer in his official capacity for use as evidence or as lost, stolen or abandoned property, or otherwise. 
(Ord. No. 86-04, § 1, 4-14-1986) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 46-72. - Creation of office of custodian of property. 
    The office of custodian of property is created. The custodian shall be the duly appointed or acting chief of police. 
(Ord. No. 86-04, § 2, 4-14-1986) 
Sec. 46-73. - Receiving; numbering; security. 
    It shall be the duty of every police officer to deliver promptly to the custodian of property all captured personal property, including money, which he may take into his custody, and it shall be the duty of the custodian of property to receive such property. Upon delivery by a police officer to the custodian of property of any captured personal property, the custodian shall execute in duplicate a receipt for such property upon a form approved by the city clerk, describing the property as accurately as possible, which receipt shall be numbered and the duplicate retained by such custodian, and the original turned over to such police officer. The custodian of property shall attach to such property so received a tag bearing a number corresponding to the number placed on the receipt issued. The custodian of property shall keep such property safely in a room provided by the city or other secure location under the control of the city, unless the property is money, and, in that event, the money shall be deposited in a bank account to the credit of the city, identified as captured personal property. He shall keep such room or other location locked or otherwise secured, and no person other than the custodian shall have access thereto, unless accompanied by the custodian. The custodian shall maintain and keep in his office a permanent record showing the date of the taking of each piece of such property, the place where found and taken and a description of the property. 
(Ord. No. 86-04, § 3, 4-14-1986) 
Sec. 46-74. - Delivery to rightful owner. 
(a)  Any captured personal property other than property being held as evidence in any legal proceeding, pending or contemplated, and other than property subject to condemnation or forfeiture under the laws of the state or under the provisions of other ordinances of the city, shall become subject to demand of the rightful owner for its return upon the date of receipt by the custodian of property. Any captured personal property being held as evidence in any legal proceeding, pending or contemplated, other than property subject to condemnation or forfeiture under the laws of the state or under the provisions of other ordinances of the city, shall become subject to demand of the rightful owner for its return upon the date of final termination of such legal proceeding. 
(b)  The custodian of property shall deliver any property received by him as such custodian of property to the rightful owner upon demand made after such property has become subject to demand therefor within the terms of this article and before its sale as provided in this article, and upon payment by rightful owner of reasonable expenses of taking the property in charge, its maintenance and storage, and the cost of publication. 
(c)  Upon delivery by the custodian of property to an owner of any captured personal property, the custodian of property at the time of making such delivery shall take the receipt of such owner for the property so delivered upon the duplicate receipt of the custodian for such property or upon a paper annexed to such duplicate receipt. Such receipt of the owner shall show the day on which such delivery was made, the name and address of the person to whom such property was delivered, a brief description of the property delivered, and a number corresponding to the number of the original receipt of the custodian covering such property. 
(Ord. No. 86-04, § 4, 4-14-1986) 
Sec. 46-75. - Sale; generally. 
    On June 30 and December 31 of each year, any personal property, other than property being held as evidence in any legal proceeding, pending or contemplated, or subject to condemnation or forfeiture under the state law, or under the provisions of other ordinance provisions of the city, which shall have been taken up and stored and shall have remained in the custody of the custodian for a period of three months or more, shall be sold by the city purchasing agent at the direction of the chief of police at public auction to the highest bidder for cash. Such sales to be made after notice of the time and place shall have first been given by publication of notice once a week for two successive weeks in a newspaper published or of general circulation in the city. The first publication shall be at least 20 days before the sale. The owner of any of the property taken up and stored may redeem the property at any time prior to its sale under the provisions of section 46-74(b). Each article shall be sold separately and a notation in the storage record book shall be made of the amount received for each article. The person making the sale shall have the right to reject any and all bids if the amount bid is unreasonably low, and shall have the right to continue the sales from time to time if no bidders are present. If no bids are received, or the bid is rejected as being unreasonably low, or the city desires to purchase the article, then the purchasing agent of the city shall be permitted to bid a reasonable amount on behalf of the city, and the property shall then be sold to the city if its bid is the highest; provided, however, that the purchasing agent shall make no single purchase on behalf of the city under this article where the purchase price amounts to $1,000.00 or more, notwithstanding the provisions of other resolutions or ordinances of the city. The proceeds of the sale shall be paid into the general fund of the city after deducting and paying all expenses incurred in the taking up, maintaining and selling of the property. Where the captured personal property is money, no sale or publication shall be required, and if the money has not been claimed by the rightful owner on June 30 and December 31 of each year, all money having been held for a period of three months as captured personal property in an account, as provided in section 46-73, shall be paid into the general fund of the city after deducting expenses in connection therewith. 
(Ord. No. 86-04, § 5, 4-14-1986) 
Sec. 46-76. - Perishable property. 
    In all cases of perishable property it shall be the duty of the police officer who captures such property to report the property with all convenient speed to the custodian of property, who shall have the power in his discretion to order such property disposed of at public or private sale, and the proceeds of such sale shall become captured personal property and shall be treated the same as money is treated in sections 46-73 and 46-75, with the expenses of sale of such perishable property being deducted from the money upon delivery to its rightful owner. 
(Ord. No. 86-04, § 6, 4-14-1986) 
Secs. 46-77-46-110. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - RESERVE POLICE OFFICERS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Officers and employees, § 2-81 et seq. 
State Law reference- Reserve law enforcement officers, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-210. 

Sec. 46-111. - Appointment; powers and duties. 
(a)  The council or its designee may appoint, without compensation, not more than 12 reserve police officers to assist or aid full-time or part-time certified police officers as defined by this section, who shall serve at the pleasure of the council or its designee. 
(b)  Any person desiring appointment as a reserve law enforcement officer after April 12, 1990, shall submit a written application to the council or its designee certifying that the applicant is 19 years of age or older, of good moral character and reputation, and that he has never been convicted of a felony or of a misdemeanor involving force, violence or moral turpitude. The applicant must also consent in writing to a fingerprint and background search. 
(c)  For the purposes of this section, the term "certified police officer" shall mean a municipal police officer who has completed the training requirements of the state peace officers' standards and training commission as set out in Code of Ala. 1975, § 36-21-40 et seq. The functions of a reserve police officer appointed pursuant to this section shall be confined to the following: 
(1)  Patrol operation performed for the purpose of detection, prevention and suppression of crime or enforcement of the traffic or highway laws of the state, provided that the reserve police officer acts at all times under the direct control and supervision of a certified police officer. 
(2)  Traffic direction and control may be performed without direct supervision; provided, however, that supervisory control is exercised by a certified police officer whose total span of control would be considered within reasonable limits. 
(3)  Reserve police officers may render crowd control assistance at public gatherings or municipal functions as directed by the municipality, provided that supervisory control will be exercised by a certified police officer whose span of control would be considered within reasonable limits. 
(d)  No reserve police officer shall have authority to exercise any power of arrest unless he has completed the training requirements of the state peace officers' standards and training commission as set out in Code of Ala. 1975, § 36-21-40 et seq. 
(e)  No reserve police officer shall carry any firearm unless he has obtained a properly issued permit for such firearm, and the council or its designee has approved his use of such firearm. Reserve police officers may use such firearms only to the extent permitted by properly promulgated regulations of the council or its designee. A reserve police officer may carry a firearm upon his person while on duty, in uniform or in other clothing approved by the council or its designee. While on duty and in uniform, a reserve police officer shall conduct himself, within the scope of his authority, as a regular police officer. 
(Ord. No. 82-13, § II(C), 11-22-1982; Ord. No. 2011-31, § 1, 11-28-2011 ) 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-210. 
Sec. 46-112. - Regulations. 
(a)  After receiving confirmation that he has been appointed to serve as a reserve police officer, a person, upon accepting such appointment, shall take the same oath of office that the regular police officers of the city take. The mayor shall issue the oath of office to the appointee and confirm his oath in writing. 
(b)  The council or its designee shall prescribe the duties that the reserve police officers are to perform and the times at which the reserve police officers are to perform their duties. Reserve police officers are governed by the same rules and regulations that govern the police department and all regular police officers, as well as the special rules that pertain to the reserve police officers. 
(Ord. No. 82-13, § II(A), (B), 11-22-1982) 
Sec. 46-113. - Promulgation of rules. 
    Special rules pertaining to the reserve police officers, not expressed or implied in this article, shall be promulgated by the council or its designee and in addition to the regular rules and regulations governing the police department. Such special rules are for defining the following, but are not limited to the following: 
(1)  Entrance requirements as per Articles of Membership as defined under Articles of Membership, article VI. 
(2)  Limit of authority: A reserve police officer, while on duty and in uniform, has the authority as outlined in sections 46-111 and 46-112. See section 46-114 for off-duty authority. 
(3)  Chain of command as per Articles of Membership as defined in Articles of Membership, article V. 
(4)  Training required as defined elsewhere in this article per Articles of Membership, article VII. 
(5)  Specific duties authorized: Specifically, a reserve police officer is authorized to perform his duties only under the supervision of a regular police officer. The duties include those enumerated in sections 46-111 and 46-112. 
(6)  Required service time as per Articles of Membership, article VII. 
(7)  Insurance: The reserve police officer shall have: 
a.  Liability, comprehensive and collision insurance on at least one owned automobile. 
b.  Health and accident insurance policy that will cover him on at least a secondary basis while in uniform. 
(8)  Uniforms: Minimum requirements of the uniform to be owned by the reserve police officer are cap, shirt, shoes, pants, coat, name tag, whistle, handcuffs, flashlight, leather goods, baton and pistol. Articles of Membership, article IX, specifies which items are to be furnished by the police department. 
(Ord. No. 82-13, § III, 11-22-1982) 
Sec. 46-114. - On-duty and off-duty status. 
    Except as otherwise provided in this article, reserve police officers shall perform their duties only when in uniform. Reserve police officers are not on duty while in civilian clothing and retain the status of civilians when in civilian clothing. A reserve police officer does not have the status of an off-duty police officer when in civilian clothing, with the exception of being on duty in civilian clothing under the specified direction of the council or designee for duties specified by the council or its designee and only for such time as specified by the council or its designee. 
(Ord. No. 82-13, § IV(A), 11-22-1982) 
Sec. 46-115. - Accountability for property. 
    Accountability for all property issued to a reserve police officer is the responsibility of the council or its designee. 
(Ord. No. 82-13, § IV(B), 11-22-1982) 
Sec. 46-116. - Termination or resignation. 
(a)  The council or its designee may terminate the service of any reserve police officer at any time by giving the officer written notice of termination of service. All appointments of reserve police officers are terminated upon the repeal of this article. 
(b)  Any reserve police officer may resign his office by giving a written notice of resignation to the council or designee. 
(Ord. No. 82-13, § V, 11-22-1982) 
Sec. 46-117. - Use of funds. 
    No funds are to be used by the city for establishing or maintaining the reserve police force, except for funds appropriated in the police budget by line item, and designated in the budget for the purpose of liability insurance. 
(Ord. No. 82-13, § VI(A), 11-22-1982) 
Secs. 46-118-46-150. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - REGULATIONS FOR WRECKER/TOWING SERVICES[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Note- The Valley Police Department adopted parts 390-399 of Title 49, Code of Federal Regulations of the U.S. Department of Transportation and as they may be amended in the future. These regulations apply to al motor carriers both interstate, intrastate, private for hire, etc., with a gross vehicle weight rating or gross combination weight rating of 10,0001 or more pounds. To remain on the Valley Police Department wrecker rotation list, your company must comply with the safety regulations contained in CFR 49. One of the safety requirements contained in CFR 498 is Part 396.17, Periodic Inspections. This section requires every motor carrier to inspect his vehicle annually and have documentation that his vehicle has been inspected. If you have any questions concerning this requirement, you can contact a member of the Valley Police Department. Anyone who wishes to operate a commercial motor vehicle (GVWR 26,001) must possess a commercial drivers license issued by the Alabama Department of Public Safety and must pass knowledge and skills test to obtain it. If you have any questions concerning commercial driver license, you should contact the drivers license division/CDL Unit. 

Sec. 46-151. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Accident. The towing or movement of a vehicle involved in a motor vehicle collision upon any highway or roadway or other locations which is investigated by the Valley Police Department. 
    Authorization permit. The written authorization issued by the chief of police allowing a wrecker/towing service to be placed on the Valley Police Department Rotation List. 
    Automobile liability insurance. Insurance which covers damage to property and/or person injury to third party. 
    Certificate of insurance and casualty coverage. A document evidencing the [date] an insurance policy had been written includes a statement of the coverage of the policy in general. 
    Chief of police. The commander of the Valley Police Department/zone where such wrecker/towing service is located. 
    Department. The Valley Police Department. 
    Disabled vehicle. Any vehicle which has lost its ability to move under its own power on a public street by normal methods other than by wrecker but not involved in a traffic crash. This definition included abandoned vehicles, illegally parked vehicles and those vehicles impounded by the Valley Police Department. 
    Fire extinguisher. A fully charged portable fire extinguisher as defined by the National Board of Fire Underwriters with a capacity of not less than ten pounds chemical to meet Federal regulations for hazardous materials (10B:C). The Underwriters Laboratory approval will be secured and such fire extinguisher shall be in a quick release carrier. 
    Garage keepers legal liability. Insurance which provides coverage to owners of storage garages for liability as bailees with respect to damage or loss to automobiles in their custody. Coverage is contingent upon establishing liability on the part of the insured. 
    Garage/storage liability. Insurance which covers legal liability of garage/storage for claims of bodily injury and property damage arising out of business operations. Garage keeper's legal liability coverage can be written as a part of the garage liability policy. 
    Gross combination weight rating (GCWR). The value specified by the manufacturer as the loaded weight of a combination (articulated) vehicle. In the absence of a value specified by the manufacturer, GCWR will be determined by adding the GVWR of the power unit and the total weight of the towed unit and any load thereon. 
    Gross vehicle weight rating (GVWR). The value specified by the manufacturer as the loaded weight of a single vehicle. 
    Hold. Means a vehicle has been impounded for investigatory purposes or any reason whereas access is restricted. 
    Motor vehicle. Every vehicle that is self-propelled. 
    Normal business hours. "Normal business hours" or "business hours" used in this regulation means at least from 8:30 a.m. to 5:00 p.m. Monday through Friday and additional hours designated and posted by the company. 
    Officer. Any person with arrest powers employed by the Valley Police Department. 
    On-hook coverage. Insurance which protects the vehicle being towed when it is hooked up with a recovery line whether in transport or not. 
    Operator. Any individual, partnership, corporation, or business entity engaged for hire in the recovery, towing, or removal of wrecked, disabled, stolen, or abandoned motor vehicles. For the purpose of these regulations, a hired driver or employee shall be considered an agent of the wrecker operator and shall be governed by these rules. 
    Owner. Any person who holds a legal title to a motor vehicle or who has the legal right to possession thereof. 
    Person. An individual, firm, partnership, association, corporation company, organization, or any legal entity of any kind. 
    Place of business. A permanent structure which the operator occupies, either continuously or at regular times, with phone service where towing and recovery books and records are kept. 
    Release fee. The fee assessed to recover police department costs associated with the towing/impounding of a vehicle where an arrest and/or citation has been issued for violations of state and local laws. 
    Service call. Any rotation wrecker response in which the removal of the vehicle is not required. Such calls may include nut not limited to changing a flat tire, providing gas or use of jumper cables, assisting in starting or unlocking a vehicle. 
    Traffic hazard. Any disabled vehicle or abandoned vehicle other than those resulting from a vehicular accident as defined herein, and which is an obstruction to the normal movement of traffic on any public street or possess a significant safety hazard to the motoring public. 
    Vehicle. Every device in or by which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a public street, except such devices moved only by human power, or used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks. The term vehicle shall include trailers and semi-trailers. 
    Wrecker. Any motor vehicle designed for the purpose of towing or removing motor vehicles or other transport devices from one location to another location 
    Wrecker call. wrecker or towing request by an authorized representative of the Valley Police Department requesting the services of a wrecker/towing service to respond to a particular location as directed by the representative. 
    Wrecker/towing company. Any person or business organization engaged in towing or removing motor vehicles from one location to another in exchange for monetary consideration or other remuneration. 
    Wrecker rotation list. The list of companies authorized and as provided in the execution of these regulations. 
    Zone. The geographical area designed by the chief of police to be used when establishing the wrecker rotation list. The terms area or territory are interchangeable with the term zone. 
( Ord. No. 2009-01, 1-12-2009 ) 
Sec. 46-152. - Facilities. 
    Each operator shall maintain sufficient space available to accommodate the storage of all vehicles resulting from department dispatches. Such an area shall be either on the site of the operator's place of business or with a reasonable distance thereof. Both the place of business and the storage facility must be physically be within the City of Valley or Chambers County. No vehicles shall be stored out of states. 
    The storage lot shall be well lighted and enclosed by a minimum six-foot high chain link fence or equivalent and secured by a locked gate for properly accommodating and protecting all disabled motor vehicles, including their contents against damage or theft. 
    Each wrecker company on the rotation list must pace on the exterior of its business location and storage facility (if separate location) a clearly visible sign indicating the company name, telephone number, and business hours. 
    All vehicles towed under these regulations must be towed to and secured within the storage facility enclosure unless vehicle owner or a member of the department requests the vehicle be towed to another location. Each wrecker company will provide a means of protection for a minimum of two vehicles from the elements either with an enclosed building or tarps when such request is made by the investigating officer. A wrecker company must immediately notify the department upon change of address or telephone number. 
( Ord. No. 2009-01, § I, 1-12-2009 ) 
Sec. 46-153. - Equipment requirements. 
    Note: The minimum equipment standards referred to throughout these rules and regulations shall be determined solely by the manufacturer's specifications for the capabilities and capacities of the tow trucks and all towing equipments. 
    Any trucks and/or towing equipment meeting the requirements of the department prior to January 1, 2008, shall be deemed adequate for use up to January 1, 2009. Any trucks and/or towing equipment acquired after January 1, 2008, must meet the capacities and specifications set forth in these regulations. 
    Each tow truck shall be equipped with only those winches and cranes that have been produced and constructed by a manufacturer of such equipment who carries product liability, and which regularly produces winches and cranes. 
(a)  Wrecker classifications. 
(1)  Class A: Light duty wrecker. Class A wreckers, for towing vehicles weighing 7,000 pounds or less, (passengers cars, pickup trucks, motorcycles, small trailers, and similar vehicles) shall meet the following minimum requirements: 
a.  Conventional wrecker: 
1.  Minimum gross vehicle weight rating (GVWR) of not less than 10,000)pounds. 
2.  Individual boom capacity of not less than 8,000 pounds as rated by the manufacturer. 
3.  Individual PTO or hydraulic power winch capacity of not less than 8,000 pounds as rated by the manufacturer with at least 100 feet of three-eighth-inch cable drum. 
4.  A manufactured wheel-lift with a retracting lifting capacity of not less than 3,500 pounds as rated by the manufacturer, with safety chains. 
5.  Dual rear wheels. 
6.  Additional safety equipment as specified by the regulations. 
b.  Rollback wrecker: 
1.  Minimum gross vehicle weight rating (GVWR) of not less than 11,000 pounds. 
2.  Must have at least an 8,000 pound of winch as rated by the manufacturer with at least 50 feet of three-eighths-inch cable or larger. 
3.  Come-A-Longs, chains, or other similar devices shall not be used as substitutes for winch and cable. 
4.  A brake lock device. 
5.  Additional safety equipment as specified by the regulations. 
(2)  Class B: Medium duty wrecker. Class B Wreckers, for towing vehicles weighing between 7,001 and 17,00) pounds or multiple vehicles weighing 7,000 pounds respectively (medium-sized trucks, road tractors/trailers and similar vehicles), shall meet the following requirements: 
a.  The tow truck chassis shall have a minimum gross vehicle weight rating (GVWR) of not less than 22,000 pounds. 
b.  Must have at least a 12-ton boom assembly as rated by the manufacturer. 
c.  Two winches, each of 10,000 pound capacity or more as rated by the manufacturer. 
d.  A manufactured wheel-lift with a retracting lifting capacity of not less than 6,500 pounds as rated by the manufacturer, with safety chains. 
e.  Come-A-Longs, chains, or other similar devices shall not be used as substitutes for winch and cable. 
f.  Additional safety equipment as specified by the regulations. 
(3)  Class C: Heavy duty wrecker. Class C Wreckers, for towing vehicles in excess of 17,000 pounds (large trucks, road tractor/trailers and similar vehicles), shall meet the following minimum requirements: 
a.  Truck chassis having a minimum gross vehicle weight rating (GVWR) of not less than 46,000 pounds. 
b.  Tandem axles or cab to axle length of not less than 102 inches. 
c.  A single or double boom with a capacity of not less than 50,000 pounds as rated by the manufacturer. 
d.  A single winch with a capacity of 50,000 pounds as rated by the manufacturer or an individual power winch capacity of not less than 25,000 pounds as rated by the manufacturer and a total rating with both winches of 50,000 pounds. 
e.  A manufactured wheel-lift with a retracting lifting capacity of not less than 12,000 pounds as rated by the manufacturer, with safety chains. 
f.  A minimum of 200 feet of five-eights-inch cable or larger, plus 50 feet of five-eights-inch drop cable. 
g.  Airbrakes constructed so as to lock wheels automatically upon failure. 
h.  Light and air brake hookups. 
i.  Come-A-Longs, chains, or other similar devices shall not be used as substitutes for winch and cable. 
j.  Additional safety equipment as specified by the regulations. 
(b)  Additional requirements. Every wrecker to be placed on the Valley Police Department Wrecker Rotation List, regardless of class, shall meet the following standards: 
(1)  All equipment necessary for the towing vehicle or combination of towing vehicle and towed vehicle must comply with the requirements of CFR 39, parts 390-399, of the Federal Motor Carrier Rules and Regulations when applicable. 
(2)  Must be well maintained and in good conditions at all times and comply with all applicable state, federal, and local laws. 
(3)  Each wrecker shall have the following standard equipment at all times: 
a.  Tow bars. 
b.  Two or more safety chains. 
c.  A minimum, of two Class "C" fire extinguishers mounted in an accessible location. (Class C extinguishers should not be used around electricity and if used around gas the gas supple should be isolated). Each wrecker company is responsible for following all safety precautions relating to fir extinguishing. 
d.  One wrecking bar or pry bar with a minimum length of 30 inches. 
e.  A minimum of three flares of at least 15 minutes duration or triangle reflectors. 
f.  One push-type broom. 
g.  One flat shovel. 
h.  One axe. 
i.  One pair of bolt cutters with a minimum opening of one-half inch. 
j.  A minimum of 40 pounds of sand or absorbent material. 
k.  A yellow or amber rotating or strobe light or light bar shall be affixed about the top of the can of the wrecker. The warning lights shall be visible from 360 degrees and a distance of not less than 1,500 feet under normal atmospheric conditions at night. (sirens are prohibited). 
l.  Dual rear adjustable floodlights with a minimum of 20,000 candlepower each are required. 
m.  One pair of magnetically mounted tow lights to be mounted at rear of towed vehicle. See 32-5A-134(h) (Class A conventional and class B only). 
n.  Every wrecker must display a currant license plate of the proper classification. 
o.  Every wrecker shall have displayed in lower right corner of the passengers windshield a departmental decal indicating a current inspection and eligibly to be on rotation log. 
p.  The name, address, and telephone number of the wrecker company shall be permanently affixed to both sides of the wrecker, using letters and numerals, which are clearly visible from a distance of 100 feet. The lettering used for the company name shall be at least four inches high, and the lettering and numerals used for the address and telephone shall be at least tow inches. 
[q.  Reserved.] 
r.  The wrecker company shall not place or imprint on their vehicles, building, equipment, clothing or correspondence, anything that suggests or implies any official relationship between the wrecker company and any law enforcement agency. Specifically, paint colors/schemes similar to department vehicles; any decals similar in design to department decals; or any name or logo such as "city wrecker" are specifically forbidden. 
(c)  In addition to the above requirements of subsection (b), class C wreckers, as defined in this regulation are required to be equipped with the following items: 
(1)  Two chock blocks to prevent rolling or slippage of wrecker, these chock blocks should have the capability of being tied to the wrecker, and of a width equal to that of the dual wheels of the wrecker. 
(2)  At least six safety cones or triangle reflectors. 
(d)  Nothing in these regulations is meant to preclude innovative wrecker or auto recovery equipment or vehicles. Such new equipment may be considered for use by companies included on the wrecker rotation list upon written request directed to the chief of police. 
( Ord. No. 2009-01, § II, 1-12-2009 ) 
Sec. 46-154. - Applications. 
(a)  General. Each wrecker company desiring to be placed on the Valley Police Department Wrecker Rotation List shall complete an "Application for Placement on Rotation List," "Wrecker Information Sheet," "Driver Information Sheet," and "Agreement & Waiver Form." All forms will be submitted to the chief of police. 
(1)  The Valley Police Department will furnish each wrecker company making a request to be placed on the rotation list a copy of the rules, forms, regulations, and laws pertaining to the operations of wreckers included on a Valley Police Department Rotation List. 
(2)  The applicant will furnish the Valley Police Department Chief of Police with a copy of certificate of insurance and casualty coverage as defined in section 46-151, Definitions. This form must be signed by an authorized agent. 
(3)  The chief of police or designee shall conduct an investigation of the requesting wrecker company and determine if the business meets all qualifications that are required to be placed on the Valley Police Department Rotation List. 
(4)  The investigating officer will inspect all equipment that is to be used by the wrecker company and determine if it complies will all applicable laws and regulations. In addition, the investigating officer will conduct a preliminary background investigation of all operations covered in sections 46-157 and 46-158. He/she will submit the completed investigation to the chief of police. 
(5)  When the chief of police is satisfied the wrecker company is qualified, he/she will issue the wrecker company and "Authorization Permit" and place the company on the Valley Police Department Rotation List. 
(6)  The investigating officer will place a department decal on each wrecker passing the inspection. This decal will be affixed to the lower right corner of the passenger window to indicate current inspection and eligibility to be in the rotation list. 
(7)  A wrecker company that fails to pass inspection and qualification as prescribed by regulation will be notified of the deficiencies. When the wrecker company corrects the deficiencies, it may request a new inspection. 
(8)  Authorization permits shall be considered personal to the holder thereof, and shall be issued only to some definite legal business operating a wrecker service, and shall not be subject to lease nor shall the holder thereof sublet to permit the exercise by another in any manner, of the rights or privileges granted there under. 
(9)  An annual inspection will be conducted of the wrecker company's place of business storage facility, and all trucks and towing equipment. 
(10)  Any wrecker company that adds a new wrecker to its fleet will submit a "Wrecker Information Sheet" for that vehicle to the chief of police. It must then pass an inspection before being used on any rotation call. 
( Ord. No. 2009-01, § III, 1-12-2009 ) 
Sec. 46-155. - Insurance. 
    Each operator, from the time he moves or otherwise makes contact with any other vehicle to be towed, assumes liability for injury to persons, damage to property, fires or theft resulting from the operator's movement or other contact. 
    Each operator shall maintain an insurance policy issued by an insurer with a current authorization from the Alabama Department of Insurance to issue policy. 
    The operator shall main the following policies of insurance: 
(1)  Workers compensation insurance as required by current statute. 
(2)  Liability insurance on wreckers and business premises in an amount not less than $300,000.00 for a class A wrecker, $500,000.00 for a class B wrecker and $70,000.00 for a class C wrecker. 
(3)  "On-Hook" insurance that covers vehicles, cargo, and other property in or on the vehicle during transit in an amount of not less that $75,000.00 for a class A wrecker, $150,000.00 for a class B wrecker and $250,000.00 for a class C wrecker. 
(4)  Garage/storage keeper's liability insurance covering customer's vehicles in an amount not less that $100,000.00 for an class A wrecker, $200,000.00 for a class B wrecker and $200,000.00 for a class C wrecker. 
a.  A maximum deductible of $1,000.00 per occurrence. 
b.  Each policy required hereunder shall contain an endorsement providing for 30 days notice to the chief of police prior to any material change therein and/or cancellation thereof. 
c.  A copy of the certificate if insurance and casualty coverage is to be filed with the chief of police. The Valley Police Department will be listed as a certificate holder under all polices under this section. 
( Ord. No. 2009-01, § IV, 1-12-2009 ) 
Sec. 46-156. - Wrecker rotation list-Call allocation system. 
    The chief of police shall set up a wrecker rotation system that best meets the needs and best serves the Valley Police Department. The rotation system guidelines are set forth follows: 
(1)  To be eligible for approval to tow in the city or its police jurisdiction, the wrecker operator's place of business and storage facility must be located in Chambers County, however, except that if there are no qualified operators in a particular area, the chief of police may designate qualified out-of-county wrecker operators to be called into that area. 
(2)  Wrecker company operators shall be placed on the rotation list in order of application and will be called for service and for removal o a wrecked, disabled, stolen, impounded or abandoned vehicle according to the operator's placement on wrecker rotation list. 
(3)  The wrecker company must have a wrecker of sufficient size and strength to handle the job. The Valley Police Department reserves the right not to use a wrecker company that, in its opinion, fails to meet this qualification for a specific job. Under these conditions, the wrecker service not called will remain on the top of the rotation list. 
(4)  A wrecker company may respond with a wrecker of a higher class than requested, however, the wrecker company is limited to the rates of the requested classification. 
(5)  A wrecker company may not assign, transfer, pledge, surrender, encumber, or dispose his place on the rotation wrecker list. The wrecker company agrees to respond to all calls requested by the Valley Police Department 24 hours a day, seven days a week. If for any reason an operator cannot respond, he will be logged as unavailable. Operators who refuse to respond or develop a pattern of not responding to calls shall be subject to suspension or removal from the chief of police. 
(6)  In the event the call is an "owners" request, if the department cancels the call or a response is made without rendering service, the wrecker company will not be marked as unavailable on the list. 
(7)  A wrecker company will be listed on each wrecker rotation list only once. This listing will use the name of the wrecker company submitted during the application process and which they were qualified under. 
It is prohibited for a wrecker operator conducting business at one location to receive multiple listings or classifications by utilizing a different or fictitious name for trucks operating from the same location or by utilizing trucks with the same name out of a different location. 
Wrecker companies or corporations operating more that one rotation wrecker business within the same county or city, or in more that one county or city, must maintain completely separate officers, required paperwork, logs and assigned rotation wreckers at the approved location. Each business must have at least one wrecker available for call for each city approved for. 
Attempts to circumvent the intent of the rotation system will result in the removal for a period of not less than five years. 
(8)  When emergency conditions necessitate, the department reserves the right to request the services of the wrecker company or operator who is the best able to handle the emergency and can reach the scene in the shortest time regardless of the operator's position on the rotation list. If a call us made under these circumstances this call will count as that wrecker's next rotation call. 
(9)  Whenever heavy equipment or large vehicles are involved in an accident, and is determined that the wrecker next up in the rotation list does not have adequate to handle the accident, then the department reserves the right to call a large wrecker from an operator on the list that can handle the situation. 
    If a call is made under these circumstances, the operator will be repositioned accordingly. Call for large wreckers will be rotated around the companies having qualified larger wreckers. Having only on large rotation wrecker is not justification for being called to all truck accidents. 
    Example: an overturned truck usually requires more than one wrecker or specialized recovery equipment. The Valley Police Department would call the rotation company capable of solely handing the truck recovery. 
( Ord. No. 2009-01, § V, 1-12-2009) 
Sec. 46-157. - Operations. 
(a)  Wrecker companies will provide to the department a list of all wrecker operator personnel, including their full name, current address, date of birth, driver's license number, and social security number. Each wrecker operator shall be investigated regarding any criminal history. 
    Any criminal history of an operator, which affects the company's qualification for the job shall be grounds for rejection of the wrecker company. 
(b)  The chief of police will conduct an annual review of the records of the wrecker companies and operators on the wrecker rotation list to determine if any convictions of crimes, which would impact on the individual's qualifications to remain on the wrecker rotation list, have occurred since their initial inclusion. In addition to the annual review, the chief of police will conduct random inspections of as many current owner/operator records as manpower and time restrictions will permit. 
(c)  Before any newly hired employee of the wrecker company is allowed to drive a wrecker for any rotation call, the wrecker company who is currently on a wrecker rotation list will furnish the chief of police with a criminal and driver's history of the new employee. The chief of police will notify the wrecker company owner if the new hire us approved upon receipt of said histories. 
(d)  Each company must have the proper business license issued by all applicable governing bodies and provide the Valley Police Department with copies. 
(e)  No wrecker company owner or operator shall be on the rotation list who maintains a reputation in the community of associating with convicted felons, who tolerates or condones gambling the drinking of alcoholic beverages or the use of illicit drugs in or about the business premises; or who allows any other activity that imparts a poor reputation upon the business. 
(f)  No wrecker company employees shall be on the rotation list unless the wrecker company employee is proficient and competent in the operations of the wreckers used. It will be the responsibly of the business owner to ensure that all drivers and wrecker company operators are trained in the safe operation of vehicles and equipment used. Wrecker company operators will be removed form the rotation that demonstrate a lack of proficiency or respond with inadequate equipment. 
(g)  Each wrecker company will furnish the chief of police with one telephone number to be used for requests for service during the day and one telephone number to be used for requests for service during the night or on weekends. Immediate notification shall be made to the chief of police if there is any change in the aforementioned telephone numbers. Call forwarding, which provides immediate contact with the owner/operator, is permitted. Answering services, pager systems or any communications system will be allowed at the discretion of the chief of police. 
(h)  No operator shall proceed to the scene of an accident without being requested to do so by a law enforcement officer or agent of the Valley Police Department, or when requested by a member of his own wrecker company to assist as outlined in these regulations. (This is not to be constructed as sub-contracting). 
    Wrecker company operator shall not solicit business at the scene of an accident. Solicitation shall not include referral for repair/replacement of an auto or referral for any legal service. 
    No wrecker company operator will accept requests for services unless that operator had a vehicle immediately available to perform the requested service 
(i)  No wrecker company operator shall speed, or violate any other traffic laws, or disregard any traffic control device while answering a call, nor upon arrival needlessly congest the scone of the wreck. 
(j)  Wreckers dispatched must arrive to the scene within 30 minutes. If the time to reach the scene exceeds the above limits, and the wrecker company does not notify the Valley Police Department dispatcher of a valid reason for a delay with the said time, a second wrecker may be requested. Of the second wrecker is requested before the arrival of the first rotation wrecker, the initially requested wrecker will forfeit the call and will immediately leave the collision/incident scene. 
(k)  Repeated tardiness will result in suspension or removal from the Valley Police Department Wrecker Rotation list. 
(l)  Additional requirements: 
(1)  The investigating officer at the scene of a collision had the right to designate which vehicle will be towed by a certain wrecker. The wrecker operator first on the scene may have first choice of vehicle unless other wise directed by the officer. 
(2)  At no time shall any tow truck exceed its manufacturer's GVWR or the manufacturer's rated capacity for the towing assembly, not be attached to a vehicle which by its size and/or weight would male towing said vehicle an unsafe movement. 
(3)  It shall be the responsibilities of the wrecker company to perform a general clean-up of the accident area before leaving the scene of any accident. This responsibility requires the wrecker company to remove all debris such as broken glass, liquids, and materials from an accident area by sweeping up such debris and removing this material from the scene. 
(4)  Each wrecker company shall be responsible for securing personal property in a vehicle at an accident scene. The wrecker company shall be responsible for preserving personal property in a vehicle towed from an accident scene. 
(5)  Any officer acting in his official capacity may direct the wrecker company operator to take the vehicle being towed to the Valley Police Department facility or designated facility for examination in furtherance of an official investigation. This may include multiple vehicles towed by different companies to be stored at one wrecker facility. In this case the towed vehicles will be taken to and stored at the facility of the first operator to arrive on the scene unless otherwise directed by the investigating officer. 
(6)  All towing and recovery services who tow and store vehicles which have been abandoned upon a highway, will abide by the requirements as stated in 32-13-1 thru 8, Code of Alabama, 1975 and all applicable Revenue Codes. 
Vehicles towed and stored under these circumstances will be disposed of with 180 days of initial storage. Towing and recovery services will notify the Valley Police Department immediately of the sale of any abandoned vehicles. 
Subcontracting is prohibited: Rotation wreckers may not subcontract wrecker calls. This includes on scene operations. In the event the on scene rotation wrecker is unable to handle the towing operation, the officer will cancel that wrecker and a rotation wrecker capable of handling the operation will be called. 
(7)  All towing and recovery services will provide the department with its Business Tax ID Number (FEIN) and US DOT Numbers. 
( Ord. No. 2009-01, § VI, 1-12-2009 ) 
Sec. 46-158. - Storage procedures. 
(a)  All wrecker companies and operators shall employ reasonable safeguards and procedures so all personal belongings and contents in the vehicle are intact and returned to the vehicle's owner or agent upon release of the vehicle. 
(b)  All personal property left in the vehicle shall be inventoried and handled in accordance with existing laws. 
(c)  All wrecker company operators shall sign and accept custody of vehicles from the police department. 
(d)  All operators of wrecker service on the rotation list shall reasonable permit, during normal business hours and without charge, the owner or owner's designated representative of any vehicle stored upon or within the companies facilities, to inspect the same, remove items or personal belongings and the license plate there from. 
    In addition, the wrecker company shall also reasonable permit and allow, during normal business hours and with out charge, insurance agents, adjusters to enter, inspect and photograph any such vehicle. 
(e)  In the event a stored vehicle has been placed on "hold or impound" as defined in this manual, no access to the vehicle will be allowed without expressed permission from the chief of police or his/her designee. 
    This restriction shall not apply to access by a member if the department engaged in official duties. Department members will be allowed to access vehicles any anytime. And said access will be without charge to either the department or vehicle owner. 
(f)  No vehicle shall be moved, released or disposed of by a towing/wrecker service without permission of the chief of police and/or his/her designee. 
( Ord. No. 2009-01, § VII, 1-12-2009 ) 
Sec. 46-159. - Rates and charges. 
(a)  Wrecker/towing services on the Valley Police Department rotation list shall be subject to the following regulations:. 
(1)  Motorist(s) utilizing the Valley Police Department Rotation List will have the option of paying by major credit card. The wrecker company may request, prior to dispatching, if the motorist intends to pay by major credit card, if the wrecker company does not accept major credit cards, the next wrecker/towing services which accepts credit cards will be utilized. Any wrecker/towing service called that does not accept credit cards will remain on the top of the rotation list. 
(2)  Fees charged for rotation list calls shall be set annually by the chief of police. The fees charged and maximum limits will be determined in the following manner: 
(3)  All wrecker/towing companies shall submit proposed fees annually to the chief of police for each class of wrecker, and, for each class, the fee for standard towing heavy-duty towing, storage, and special operations as describe below:
