(3)  Upon every person engaged or continuing within the police jurisdiction in the business of selling at retail machines used in mining, quarrying, compounding, processing and manufacturing of tangible personal property, an amount equal to one percent of the gross proceeds of the sale of such machines; provided, however, that the term "machines" as used in this subsection shall include machinery which is used for mining, quarrying, compounding, processing or manufacturing tangible personal property and the parts of such machines, attachments and replacements, which are made or manufactured for use on or in the operation of such machines and which are necessary to the operation of such machines and are customarily so used. 
(4)  Upon every person engaged or continuing within the police jurisdiction in the business of selling at retail any automotive vehicle or truck, trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer, an amount equal to .375 percent of the gross proceeds of sale of the automotive vehicle or truck trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer; provided, however, that where a person subject to the tax provided for in this subsection withdraws from his stock in trade any automotive vehicle or truck, trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer for use by him or his employee or agent in the operation of such business, there shall be paid, in lieu of the tax levied in this subsection, a fee of $25.00 per year or its part during which such automotive vehicle, truck trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer shall remain the property of such person; provided, however, that each such year or part of a year shall be deemed to begin with the day or anniversary date, as the case may be, of such withdrawal and shall run for the 12 succeeding months or part of such period during which such automotive vehicle, truck, trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer shall remain the property of such person; and provided further that where any used automotive vehicle or truck trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer is taken in trade, or in a series of trades, as a credit or part payment on the sale or a new or used vehicle, the tax levied in this subsection shall be paid on the net difference, that is, the price of the new or used vehicle sold less the credit for the used vehicle taken in trade. 
(5)  Upon every person engaged or continuing within the police jurisdiction in the business of selling, through coin-operated dispensing machines, food and food products for human consumption, not including beverages other than coffee, milk, milk products and substitutes therefore, an amount equal to two percent of the cost of such food, food products and beverages sold through such machines, which cost for the purpose of this subsection shall be the gross proceeds of sales of such business. 
(6)  Upon every person engaged or continuing within the police jurisdiction in the business of selling at retail any machine, machinery or equipment which is used in planting, cultivating and harvesting farm products, or used in connection with the production of agricultural produce or products, livestock or poultry on farms, and the parts of such machines, machinery or equipment, attachments and replacements therefore which are made or manufactured for use on or on the operation of such machine, machinery, equipment, and which are necessary to and customarily used in the operation of such machine, machinery or equipment, an amount equal to one percent of the gross proceeds of the sale; provided, however, that the one percent rate prescribed in this subsection with respect to parts, attachments and replacements shall not apply to any automotive vehicle or trailer designed primarily for public highway use, except for farm trailers used primarily in the production and harvesting of agricultural commodities; and provided further, that where any used machine, machinery or equipment which is used in planting, cultivating and harvesting farm products, or used in connection with the production of agricultural produce or products, livestock and poultry on farms, is taken in trade or a series of trades as a credit or part payment on a sale of a new or used machines, machinery or equipment, the tax levied in this subsection shall be paid on the net difference, that is, the price of the new or used machine, machinery or equipment sold, less the credit for the used machine, machinery or equipment taken in trade. 
There are exempted however, from the provisions of this section and from the computation of the amount of the taxes imposed in this section, the gross receipts of any business and the gross proceeds of all sales which are presently exempted under the state sales tax statutes from the computation of the amount of the state sales tax. 
(Ord. No. 85-02, § 3, 1-28-1985; Ord. No. 2005-09, § 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 2006-21, § 2, 7-13-2006 ; Ord. No. 2012-04, § 2, 1-23-2012 ) 
Sec. 66-84. - Levy of use tax. 
    There is hereby levied and imposed excise taxes on the storage, use or other consumption of property in the police jurisdiction as provided in this section: 
(1)  An excise tax is hereby levied and imposed on the storage, use or other consumption in the city of tangible personal property (not including, however, materials and supplies bought for use in fulfilling a contract for painting, repairing or reconditioning of vessels, barges, ships and other watercraft of more than 50 tons burden) purchased at retail on or after January 1, 1994, for storage, use or other consumption in the city, at the rate of two percent of the sale price of such property, except as provided in subsections (2), (3), (4) and (5) below. 
(2)  An excise tax is hereby levied and imposed on the storage, use or other consumption in the police jurisdiction of any machines used in mining, quarrying, compounding, processing and manufacturing of tangible personal property, purchased at retail on or after January 1, 1994, for storage, use or other consumption in the city, at the rate of one percent of the sales price of any such machine; provided, however, that the term "machine" as used in this subsection, shall include machinery which is used in mining, quarrying, compounding, processing or manufacturing tangible personal property, and the parts of such machines, attachments and replacements, which are made or manufactured for use on or in the operation of such machines and which are necessary to the operation of such machines and are customarily used. 
(3)  An excise tax is hereby levied and imposed on the storage, use or other consumption in the police jurisdiction of any automotive vehicle or truck trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer purchased at retail on or after January 1, 1994, for storage, use or other consumption in the city, at the rate of .375 percent of the sales price of such automotive vehicle, truck trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer; provided, however, that where any used automotive vehicle or truck trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer is taken in trade, or in a series of trades as a credit or part payment on the sale of a new or used vehicle, the tax levied in this subsection shall be paid on the net difference, that is, the price of the new or used vehicle sold less the credit for the used vehicle taken in trade. 
(4)  An excise tax is hereby levied and imposed on the classes of tangible personal property, and at the rates authorized to be imposed on such classes, specified in subsections (1), (2) and (3) above, on the storage, use or other consumption in the performance of a contract in the police jurisdiction of any such tangible personal property, new or used, the tax to be measured by the sales price or the fair and reasonable market value of such tangible personal property when put into use in the city, whichever is less; provided, however, that the tax imposed by this subsection shall not apply where the taxes imposed by subsection (1), (2) or (3) above apply. 
(5)  An excise tax is hereby levied and imposed on the storage, use or other consumption in the police jurisdiction of any machine, machinery or equipment which is used in planting, cultivating and harvesting farm products, or used in connection with the production of agricultural produce or products, livestock or poultry on farms, and the parts of such machines, machinery or equipment, attachments and replacements therefore which are made or manufactured for use on or in the operation of such machine, machinery or equipment, and which are necessary to and customarily used in the operation of such machine, machinery or equipment, which is purchased at retail on or after January 1, 1994, for storage, use or other consumption in the city, at the rate of one percent of the sales price of such property, regardless of whether the retailer is or is not engaged in business in the city; provided, however, that the one percent rate prescribed in this subsection with respect to parts, attachments and replacements shall not apply to any automotive vehicle or trailer primarily for public highway use except farm trailers used primarily in the production and harvesting of agricultural commodities. 
    There are exempted from the provisions of this section, and from the taxes imposed by this section, the storage, use or other consumption of property the storage, use or other consumption of which is presently exempted under the state use tax statutes from the state use tax. Subject to those exemptions, every person storing, using or otherwise consuming in the city tangible personal property purchased, at retail on or after the effective date of the ordinance from which this division is derived shall be liable for the taxes imposed by this section, and the liability shall not be extinguished until the tax has been paid by such person; provided, however, that a receipt from the registered seller given in accordance with the provisions of the state use tax statutes, as made applicable to the taxes imposed by this section and incorporated in this subsection by reference and made a part of this section, to the purchaser of any property to be used, stored or consumed in the city shall be sufficient to relieve the purchaser from further liability for a tax to which such receipt may refer. 
(Ord. No. 85-02, § 4, 1-28-1985; Ord. No. 2005-09, § 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 2006-21, § 2, 7-13-2006 ) 
Sec. 66-85. - Payment of taxes levied in this division; reports by taxpayers. 
    The sales taxes levied in section 66-83 shall be due and payable in monthly installments on or before the 20th day of the month next succeeding the month in which the tax accrues; and the use taxes levied in section 66-84 shall be due and payable quarterly on or before the 20th day of the month next succeeding each quarterly period during which the storage, use or other consumption of the tangible personal property became taxable under this division, each such quarterly period to end on the last day of each of the months of March, June, September and December. The sales taxes levied in section 66-83 shall be paid to and collected by the City of Valley or its designated agent or independent contractor; and the use taxes levied in section 66-84 shall be paid to and collected by the City of Valley or its designated agent or independent contractor within the prescribed time periods. On or prior to the due dates of the taxes levied in this division, each person subject to such taxes, and any registered seller required, pursuant to the state use tax statutes and section 66-84, to collect any use tax levied in this division, shall file with the City of Valley or its designated agent or independent contractor within the prescribed time periods, a report or return in such form as may be prescribed by the department, setting forth, with respect to all sales and business that are required to be used as a measure of the sales taxes levied in this division, a correct statement of the gross proceeds of all such sales and the gross receipts of all such business, and setting forth, with respect to the use taxes levied in this division, the total sales price of all property, the use, storage or other consumption of which became subject to the taxes during the then preceding quarterly period. Such report shall include all such other items of information pertinent to the taxes and the amount as the state department of revenue may require. All reports or returns filed with the state department of revenue under this section shall be available for inspection by the city council or its designated agent at reasonable times during business hours. 
(Ord. No. 85-02, § 5, 1-28-1985; Ord. No. 2001-13, § 1, 11-12-2001) 
Sec. 66-86. - Sales tax to be added to sales price or admission fee. 
    Each person engaging or continuing within the police jurisdiction in a business subject to the sales taxes levied in section 66-83 shall add to the sales price or admission fee and collect from the purchaser or the person paying the admission fee the amount due by the taxpayer on account of such taxes. It shall be unlawful for any person subject to the sales taxes levied in section 66-83 to fail or refuse to add to the sales price or admission fee and to collect from the purchaser or the person paying the admission fee the amount required in this division to be so added to the sales price or admission fee and collected from the purchaser, and it shall likewise be unlawful for any person subject to such taxes to refund or offer to refund all or any part of the amount so collected or to absorb or advertise directly or indirectly the absorption or refund of such taxes or any portion of such taxes. 
(Ord. No. 85-02, § 6, 1-28-1985) 
Sec. 66-87. - Enforcement of this division; civil suit; taxes a lien. 
    The taxes imposed by this division shall constitute a debt due the city and may be collected by civil suit, in addition to all other methods provided by law and in this division. The taxes, together with interest and penalties with respect thereto, shall constitute and be secured by a lien upon the property of any person from whom the taxes are due or who is required to collect the taxes. All the provisions of the revenue laws of the state which apply to the enforcement of liens for license taxes due the state shall apply fully to the collection of the taxes levied in this division, and the state department of revenue, for the use and benefit of the city, shall collect such taxes and enforce this division and shall have and exercise for such collection and enforcement all rights and remedies that the state department of revenue has for collection of the state sales tax and the state use tax. The state department of revenue shall have full authority to employ such special counsel as it deems necessary from time to time to enforce collection of the taxes levied hereby and otherwise to enforce the provisions of this division, including the institution, prosecution and defense of any litigation involving this division; and the department shall pay such special counsel such fees as it deems necessary and proper from the proceeds of the taxes collected by it under this division. 
(Ord. No. 85-02, § 7, 1-28-1985) 
Sec. 66-88. - Applicability of state sales and use tax statutes. 
    All exceptions, proceedings, requirements, provisions, penalties, fines, punishments and deductions provided by the state sales tax statutes or the state use tax statutes shall apply to the sales taxes levied in section 66-83 and the use taxes levied in section 66-84, respectively, except where inapplicable or where otherwise provided in this division. The commissioner and the state department of revenue shall have and exercise the same powers, duties and obligations, with respect to the taxes levied in this division, that are imposed on the commissioner and the department by the state sales tax statutes and the state use tax statutes. All provisions of the state sales tax statutes and the state use tax statutes that are made applicable by this division to the taxes levied in this division and to the administration of this division are incorporated in this section by reference and made a part of this division as if fully set forth in this section. 
(Ord. No. 85-02, § 8, 1-28-1985) 
Sec. 66-89. - Division cumulative to general license code or ordinance. 
    This division is cumulative to, and shall not be construed to repeal any of the provisions of, the general license code or ordinance of the city, and the taxes levied and imposed in this division shall be deemed to be in addition to, and not in lieu of, all other taxes levied and imposed by the city under and pursuant to the general license code or ordinance. 
(Ord. No. 85-02, § 9, 1-28-1985) 
Secs. 66-90-66-120. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - GASOLINE, MOTOR FUEL TAX[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Gasoline and other motor fuels, Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-17-1 et seq. 

Sec. 66-121. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Distributor or seller means every person who shall engage in selling or delivering gasoline or motor fuel, or both, within the corporate limits of the city or without the corporate limits of the city but within its police jurisdiction. 
    Gasoline means as provided in Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-17-30. 
    Motor fuel means as provided in Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-17-1. 
(Ord. No. 81-17, § 1, 9-24-1981) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 66-122. - License tax imposed. 
    Every distributor or seller shall pay a license tax to the city, and a license tax is hereby fixed and levied, which license tax shall be an amount equal to $.02 on each and every gallon of gasoline or motor fuel, or both, sold or delivered in the corporate limits of the city, and a sum equal to $.01 on each and every gallon of gasoline or motor fuel, or both, sold or delivered in the police jurisdiction of the city. 
(Ord. No. 81-17, § 2, 9-24-1981; Ord. No. 2010-08, § 2, 3-31-2010 ) 
Sec. 66-123. - Exemption on purchases from other distributors or sellers. 
    Any person engaged as such seller or distributor in selling or distributing gasoline or motor fuel purchased from other sellers or distributors, who have paid the license tax imposed in this article with respect to the sale or delivery of such gasoline or motor fuel, shall not be required to pay any license tax with respect to the sale or delivery of such gasoline or motor fuel so purchased; provided, however, that in order to obtain the exemption in this section contained, such seller or distributor must, on or before the 20th day of each month, file with the city clerk a sworn, written statement showing each and every purchase by such person of gasoline and motor fuel during the calendar month next preceding, as well as the name of the person from whom, the amount, and the date on which purchased. 
(Ord. No. 81-17, § 3, 9-24-1981) 
State Law reference- Single taxing of fuel, Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-17-51. 
Sec. 66-124. - Written statement of sales must be filed. 
    Each distributor and seller, except such as are exempt from license tax under the provisions of section 66-123, shall, on or before the 20th day of each month, file with the city clerk a sworn, written statement which shall be a full, true, accurate and correct statement of the following: 
(1)  The amount and quantity of all gasoline and of all motor fuel sold or delivered by such distributor or seller within the corporate limits or police jurisdiction of the city; and 
(2)  The amount and quantity of all gasoline sold and delivered to any other distributor within the corporate limits or police jurisdiction of the city. 
(Ord. No. 81-17, § 4, 9-24-1981) 
Sec. 66-125. - Permit and license tax where no place of business in the city. 
    It shall be unlawful for any seller of distributor, having no place of business within the corporate limits or police jurisdiction of the city, to make any sales or deliveries of gasoline therein, without first having obtained a permit from the city clerk to do so. Such seller or distributor shall be liable for and pay the same license as that fixed and levied in section 66-122. Any seller or distributor who shall violate any provisions of this article shall be punished as provided in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 81-17, § 5, 9-24-1981) 
Sec. 66-126. - Failure to file or making false statement continuing offense. 
    It shall be unlawful for any seller or distributor to fail or omit to make or file any statement required in this article within the time specified or to make any false statement. Such an offense shall be a continuing offense against the city. Each day during which such business or occupation is engaged in during such default shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 81-17, § 6, 9-24-1981) 
Sec. 66-127. - Payments; when due; penalties for failure to make. 
    The license tax fixed in this article shall be due by each person against whom the tax is levied on the first day of each calendar month. The license tax fixed in this article shall be paid by each person against whom the tax is levied on or before the 20th day of each month, being the time fixed for filing the statement based on the sales and deliveries made during the preceding month. Any person failing or omitting to pay the license within such time shall be guilty of an offense against the city, and such offense shall be a continuing offense. Each day during which such business or occupation is engaged in during such default shall constitute a separate offense. In addition, such license tax shall be increased by the addition of a penalty of 20 percent thereon. 
(Ord. No. 81-17, § 7, 9-24-1981) 
Sec. 66-128. - Duty to furnish information. 
    Upon demand of the city clerk, or his authorized deputy or representative, all such information as may be required for determination of the correct amount of license tax, to which any person is subject, shall be furnished to the city. To that end, it shall be the duty of such person, upon such demand, to submit to the city clerk, or his authorized deputy, auditor, or representative, for inspection and examination all books of account, invoices, papers, reports and memoranda containing entries showing the amount of purchases, sales, receipts, inventory and other information from which the correct amount of license tax to which he is subject may be determined, including exhibition of bank deposit books and bank statements. It shall be unlawful for any person to fail or refuse to submit such records for such examinations and inspections upon such demand. 
(Ord. No. 81-17, § 8, 9-24-1981) 
Sec. 66-129. - Pumps must be metered. 
    It shall be the duty of every person selling or distributing gasoline within the corporate limits or police jurisdiction of the city to have a meter in good working order on each and every pump from which gasoline is dispensed, and to keep an accurate record of the readings of the meter. 
(Ord. No. 81-17, § 9, 9-24-1981) 
Sec. 66-130. - Penalties for violation of article. 
    Whoever shall violate any provision of this article shall, for each offense, be subject to punishment as provided in section 1-11 and to such further penalties as are provided by law. 
(Ord. No. 81-17, § 10, 9-24-1981) 
Secs. 66-131-66-160. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - DELINQUENT TAXES 

Sec. 66-161. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    City means the City of Valley, Alabama, a municipal corporation in Chambers County, Alabama, as well as its police jurisdiction when taxes are levied therein. 
    Responsible party means the person upon whom a particular tax is levied or from whom payment of any particular tax is required by law or ordinance. 
    Revenue agent means that person designated, authorized and empowered, whether by appointment, employment, contract or otherwise, by the city council, to assess, ascertain and collect privilege, license, sales, use, excise, rental, gasoline or tobacco taxes on commerce, whether such agent has been designated and appointed prior to the adoption of this article or thereafter. 
    Taxing ordinance means any ordinance levying and providing for the collection of privilege, license, sales, use, excise, rental, gasoline or tobacco or other taxes on commerce, whether in the city of its police jurisdiction. 
(Ord. No. 94-09, § 1(a), (c)-(e), 3-28-1994) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 66-162. - Initial procedure. 
(a)  If the revenue agent discovers a discrepancy in any tax report filed by or on behalf of any responsible party, determines or suspects that there is a delinquency in the payment of taxes due on account of any responsible party, discovers or suspects that some required report or other act of compliance from a responsible party according to any taxing ordinance has or may not have been made or done by a responsible party, or otherwise has a question as to the status of the account or obligations of any responsible party, the revenue agent may, in his discretion, attempt to contact the responsible party either by telephone or in person, in order to discuss the discrepancy, delinquency or other problem, and attempt to resolve the problem in an informal manner. If no such resolution can be reached without undue delay, the revenue agent shall proceed to the step outlined in subsection (b) of this section, or, in his discretion, he may make the first contact in such manner without first attempting telephone or personal contact. 
(b)  If the discrepancy, delinquency or other problem cannot be resolved informally when the informal method is first attempted, or when no such informal method has been attempted, the revenue agent shall send a written notice of the discrepancy, delinquency or other problem to the responsible party, which notice shall demand the problem be resolved within 30 days of the date of the sending of the notice. 
(c)  If the procedures outlined in subsections (a) and (b) of this section do not bring about a resolution of the discrepancy, delinquency or other problem within the specified time, the revenue agent shall report this fact to the city treasurer, who shall in turn, report the same to the mayor of the city. The mayor shall take such steps as are necessary to resolve the matter as expeditiously as possible, including if necessary, initiation of legal proceedings. 
(d)  The revenue agent is authorized to enter into informal agreements for resolution of the discrepancy, delinquency or other problem, provided that in no event shall the revenue agent enter into any agreement which will allow payment of any delinquent account over a period of time exceeding 90 days without the express written permission of the mayor. 
(Ord. No. 94-09, § 2, 3-28-1994) 
Sec. 66-163. - Legal proceedings. 
(a)  If directed by the mayor to do so, the revenue agent shall initiate legal proceedings pursuant to the provisions of the ordinance levying and providing for the collection of the tax in question or as otherwise authorized by law. 
(b)  If the ordinance, statute or law in question clearly makes the conduct or omission of the responsible party a misdemeanor, the revenue agent shall, after consultation and with the concurrence of the municipal prosecutor, cause the commencement of appropriate criminal proceedings in the district court, which, if permitted by the procedures thereof, shall be initiated by seeking the issuance of a summons requiring the responsible party or its appropriate representative to appear before the court to answer these charges. The case shall thereafter be pursued and shall proceed as any case before the court for which a summons is the initial procedure. Otherwise, the case shall be initiated by warrant. In the event of an appeal to the circuit court for a trial de novo, the municipal prosecutor shall prosecute the case therein and in the prosecutions both in the district court as well as the circuit court, the revenue agent shall fully assist the municipal prosecutor with the development and prosecution of the case. 
(c)  If there is any delinquency in taxes owed by the responsible party according to the calculations of the revenue agent, whether before or after commencement of any criminal proceedings, which such delinquency cannot be resolved in accordance with the procedures outlined elsewhere in this article, the revenue agent shall, through the assistance of the municipal attorney, initiate and assist fully in the development and prosecution of civil proceedings in accordance with Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-51-96, 11-51-150-11-51-161, or any other lawfully authorized procedure, for the collection of such delinquent taxes. The municipal attorney is authorized to first attempt collection through informal contact with the responsible party before initiating civil process and is further authorized to enter into settlement agreements on behalf of the city, with the advice of the revenue officer and consent of the mayor, prior to or after the initiation of any such civil proceedings. 
(Ord. No. 94-09, § 3, 3-28-1994) 
Sec. 66-164. - Article cumulative and not exclusive. 
    This article and the procedures set forth in this article shall be cumulative with and in addition to all other ordinances of the city and the procedures set forth therein, and shall not be construed to repeal any provisions of any other ordinances of the city. Likewise, the procedures set forth in this article shall not be exclusive, but are cumulative with those otherwise allowed by law or ordinance. 
(Ord. No. 94-09, § 4, 3-28-1994) 
Secs. 66-165-66-200. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - ADMINISTRATIVE REVIEW AND APPEAL PROCEDURES[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2. 

Sec. 66-201. - Taxpayers' bill of rights. 
(a)  Adoption. The city council does adopt in whole the Alabama Taxpayers Bill of Rights and Uniform Revenue Procedures Act (Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-2A-1 et seq.), as enacted by the State Legislature, except where inapplicable. These rights are as enumerated in this section. 
(b)  Enumeration of rights. The following rights are guaranteed to taxpayers under the Taxpayers Bill of Rights and Uniform Revenue Procedures Act (Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-2A-1 et seq.): 
(1)  The taxpayer has the right to receive a clear and simple written description of his role and the examiner's role during an audit or examination before the audit or examination proceedings begin. 
(2)  The taxpayer has the right to a written description of the basis for any preliminary assessment, the basis for any penalty imposed by the taxing jurisdiction regarding any preliminary assessment, and a method describing how the taxpayer can request an administrative review of any preliminary assessment. 
(3)  The taxpayer has the right to receive a written description of how to exercise his right of appeal to the taxing jurisdiction's administrative law division or to circuit court at or before the issuance of a final assessment. 
(4)  The taxpayer has the right to have examinations conducted during regular business hours or to arrange for a more convenient time. 
(5)  The taxpayer has the right to be assisted or represented by his authorized representative during the dealings with the examiner. 
(6)  The taxpayer has the right to make an audio recording of any in-person interview with an examiner. 
(7)  The taxpayer has the right to obtain assistance from a taxpayer assistance officer on matters that have been pending for an unreasonable length of time. 
(8)  The taxpayer has the right to apply the abatement of any penalties attributable to erroneous written advice if furnished to him by an employee of the taxing jurisdiction. 
(c)  Roles of the examiner and taxpayer during an audit. In most cases, a taxing jurisdiction has three years from the date a tax return is due or filed, whichever is later, to audit the taxpayer's tax return and send the taxpayer a notice of any change in the amount of the tax, penalty, and interest the taxpayer may owe, or notify the taxpayer of any refund owed to him. Under certain circumstances, the time limitations to audit tax returns may be extended. These are if: 
(1)  The taxpayer signed an agreement with the taxing jurisdiction to extend the time period to adjust his tax return. 
(2)  The taxpayer omitted more than 25 percent of the taxes that he should have reported on his tax return. 
(3)  The taxpayer intentionally misstated or fraudulently filed his tax return. 
(d)  Audit contact. 
(1)  The audit process will begin with the examiner giving the taxpayer reasonable notice of his audit and scheduling an appointment to meet with him during normal business hours. When the appointment is made, the examiner will notify him in writing as to the necessary books and records required for the audit. 
(2)  Throughout any examination process, the taxpayer may represent himself, or, with proper written authorization, he may elect to have an authorized representative act on his behalf. When he meets with the examiner the taxpayer has the right to have an authorized representative present, or the authorized representative may represent him in his absence. In order for this representative to act on his behalf, the taxpayer must, prior to his audit appointment, sign a power of attorney and declaration of representative form, or such other form such as a federal power of attorney form, which designates the taxpayer as the "taxpayer," identifies the type of tax or assessment, identifies the taxpayer's authorized representative, and states the effective date of representation. To obtain a power of attorney form, the taxpayer may call Local Governments Revenue Enhancement Consultants, Inc. at 256/751-0692, or write to LGREC, P.O. Box 1324, Hartselle, Alabama 35640. 
(3)  If the taxpayer wishes, he may audio record any in-person interview with the examiner, provided that the taxpayer notifies the examiner at least 24 hours prior to the interview. Likewise, the examiner may audio record an in-person interview with the taxpayer, provided the examiner notifies the taxpayer at least 24 hours prior to the interview or if the taxpayer has arranged to audio record the interview. In order to obtain a copy of any transcript or audio recording made by the examiner, the taxpayer must make a written request and pay the established fee. 
(e)  After the audit. 
(1)  After a taxpayer's audit, one of the following three actions will be taken: 
a.  Accept the tax return as filed; 
b.  Issue a preliminary assessment which will state any additional tax, penalty, and interest the city believes the taxpayer owes; or 
c.  Issue a refund of tax and any applicable interest to the taxpayer. 
(2)  If any charges are proposed to the taxpayer's tax return, the examiner will explain the reason. The taxpayer should inquire about anything that is unclear to him. 
(3)  If the taxpayer does not agree with the decision in his case, he may appeal the decision by filing a written petition for review to request a conference on his case. The petition for review must be filed within 30 days of the issuance date of the preliminary assessment. To request a petition for review form, the taxpayer may call Local Governments Revenue Enhancement Consultants, Inc. at 256/751-0692 or write to LGREC, P.O. Box 1324, Hartselle, Alabama 35640. 
(4)  The taxing jurisdiction will review the taxpayer's petition and schedule a conference if requested or otherwise necessary. 
(5)  During this conference the taxpayer will have the opportunity to discuss his case with a designated hearing officer from the taxing jurisdiction. This conference will allow both the taxpayer and the examiner to present each side of the issue and to review any additional information being presented. 
(6)  Based on the outcome of this conference, the taxing jurisdiction will either cancel, change, or affirm the action. If the taxpayer does not timely file his petition for review or the taxing jurisdiction determines from the conference that the preliminary assessment is due to be upheld in whole or in part, the taxing jurisdiction will enter a final assessment. 
(7)  If a final assessment is entered, the taxpayer will be notified in writing and advised that he may appeal either to the taxing jurisdiction's administrative law judge or to the circuit court. 
(Ord. No. 99-02, § 1, 4-1-1999) 
Sec. 66-202. - Adoption of state department of revenue rules and regulations. 
    Pursuant to Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-51-204, the city council adopts in whole the rules and regulations promulgated by the state department of revenue. 
(Ord. No. 99-02, § 2, 4-1-1999) 
Secs. 66-203-66-220. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - TAX ON RENTERS OR LESSORS OF TANGIBLE PERSONAL PROPERTY 
DIVISION 1. - IN CITY LIMITS 

Sec. 66-221. - Definitions. 
    For the purpose of this division, the following terms shall have the following respective meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Business means all activities engaged in, or caused to be engaged in, with the object of gain, profit, benefit or advantage, either direct or indirect, and not excepting sub-activities producing marketable commodities used or consumed in the main business activity, each of which sub-activities shall be considered business engaged in, taxable in the classification in which it falls. 
    City clerk means the duly appointed city clerk of the city, or in his or her absence, the person performing the duties of the city clerk. 
    Gross proceeds means the value proceeding or accruing from the leasing or rental of tangible personal property, without any deduction on account of the cost of the property so leaded or rented, the cost of the materials used, labor or service cost, interest paid or any other expense whatsoever, and without any deduction on account of loss, and shall also include on the part of any person claiming exemption under the Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-12-223, as amended, an amount equal to the rental paid on any tangible personal property acquired under such exemption and thereafter diverted to the use of the person. 
    Leasing or rental means a transaction under which the person who owns or controls the possession of tangible personal property permits another person to have possession or use thereof for a consideration and for the duration of a definite or indefinite period of time without transfer of the title to such property. 
    Person means any natural person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, receiver, trust, estate or other entity, or any other group or combinations of any thereof acting as a unit. 
    Tangible personal property means the personal property which may be seen, weighed, measured, felt or touched, or is in any manner perceptible to the senses. The term "tangible personal property" shall not include stocks, bonds, notes, insurance or other contracts or securities. 
( Ord. No. 2009-18, § 1, 7-13-2009 ) 
Sec. 66-222. - Rental fee levy and amount. 
    There is hereby levied and imposed in addition to all other taxes not imposed by law, a privilege or license fee upon each person engaging or continuing in this city in the business of leasing or renting tangible personal property at the rate of two percent of the gross proceeds derived by the lessor from the lease or rental of tangible personal property, provided, that the said fee on each person engaging or continuing in this city in the business of leasing or renting any automotive vehicle or truck trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer for a period of 12 months or longer shall be at the rate of one percent of the gross proceeds derived by the lessor from the lease or rental of such automotive vehicle or truck trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer; provided further, that the fee levied in this division shall not apply to any leasing or rental, as lessor, by the State of Alabama, or any municipality or county in the State of Alabama, including without limiting the generality of the foregoing, any corporation organized under the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-54-80 through 11-54-101, as amended. 
(Ord. No. 2009-18, § 2, 7-13-2009) 
Sec. 66-223. - Monthly report and payment. 
    The fee levied under provision of this division shall be due and payable in monthly installments on or before the twentieth day of the month next succeeding the month in which the fee accrues. On or before the twentieth day of each month, every person on whom the amounts levied by this division are imposed shall render to the city, on a form prescribed by the city, a true and correct statement showing the gross proceeds of such person's business, for the next preceding month the amount of gross receipts which are not subject to the fee or are not to be used as a measurement of the amounts due by such person, and the nature thereof, together with such other information as the city may require; and at the time of making such monthly report such person shall compute the fee due and shall pay to the city the amount shown to be due. 
(Ord. No. 2009-18, § 3, 7-13-2009) 
Sec. 66-224. - Reports of cash and credit card rentals. 
    Any person taxable under this division, making cash and credit leases or rentals, may if he desires, report such cash leases or rentals only, and he shall thereafter include in each monthly report all cash and credit collections made during the month preceding, and shall pay the privilege license tax due thereon at the time of filing such report. 
(Ord. No. 2009-18, § 4, 7-13-2009) 
Sec. 66-225. - Records. 
(a)  It shall be the duty of every person engaging in or continuing in any business for which a privilege is imposed by this division to keep and preserve suitable records of the gross proceeds of any such business and such other books or accounts as may be necessary to determine the amount of tax for which he is liable under the provisions of this division. It shall be the duty of every person to keep and preserve for a period of three years, all invoices of gross proceeds proceeding or accruing from the leasing or rental herein taxed; and all such books, invoices, and other records shall be open for examination at any time by the city clerk or his or her authorized representative. Any person leasing who in addition leases for re-leasing shall keep his books so as to show separately the gross proceeds of leasing and the gross proceeds of leasing for re-leasing. 
(b)  The books, records and accounts mentioned above shall at all times be open to examination by the city clerk or his or her authorized representative, upon request by the city clerk. Upon demand by the city clerk or his or her representative, it shall be the duty of any person subject to this license tax to submit to the city clerk or his or her authorized representative, for inspection and examination, during reasonable business hours, in the city, all books of account. Each occurrence of a failure to keep records, or allow examination thereof shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 2009-18, § 5, 7-13-2009) 
Sec. 66-226. - Penalty. 
    Any person subject to this division failing to pay the fee imposed herein, failing to render any report required hereby, willfully making a false statement of fact in the statement or return, failing to keep records required herein, refusing to permit examination of such records or violating any other provision of this division shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be punishable as provided in the Code of Ordinances of the City of Valley, Alabama. 
(Ord. No. 2009-18, § 6, 7-13-2009) 
Secs. 66-227-66-230. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - IN POLICE JURISDICTION 

Sec. 66-231. - Definitions. 
    For the purpose of this division, the following terms shall have the following respective meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning. 
    Business means all activities engaged in, or caused to be engaged in, with the object of gain, profit, benefit or advantage, either direct or indirect, and not excepting sub-activities producing marketable commodities used or consumed in the main business activity, each of which sub-activities shall be considered business engaged in, taxable in the classification in which it falls. 
    City clerk means the duly appointed city clerk of the city, or in his or her absence, the person performing the duties of the city clerk. 
    Gross proceeds means the value proceeding or accruing from the leasing or rental of tangible personal property, without any deduction on account of the cost of the property so leaded or rented, the cost of the materials used, labor or service cost, interest paid or any other expense whatsoever, and without any deduction on account of loss, and shall also include on the part of any person claiming exemption under the Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-12-223, as amended, an amount equal to the rental paid on any tangible personal property acquired under such exemption and thereafter diverted to the use of the person. 
    Leasing or rental means a transaction under which the person who owns or controls the possession of tangible personal property permits another person to have possession or use thereof for a consideration and for the duration of a definite or indefinite period of time without transfer of the title to such property. 
    Person means any natural person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, receiver, trust, estate or other entity, or any other group or combinations of any thereof acting as a unit. 
    Tangible personal property means the personal property which may be seen, weighed, measured, felt or touched, or is in any manner perceptible to the senses. The term "tangible personal property" shall not include stocks, bonds, notes, insurance or other contracts or securities. 
( Ord. No. 2009-19, § 1, 7-13-2009 ) 
Sec. 66-232. - Rental fee levy and amount. 
    There is hereby levied and imposed in addition to all other taxes not imposed by law, a privilege or license fee upon each person engaging or continuing in the police jurisdiction of the City of Valley, Alabama in the business of leasing or renting tangible personal property at the rate of one percent of the gross proceeds derived by the lessor from the lease or rental of tangible personal property, provided, that the said fee on each person engaging or continuing in the police jurisdiction in the business of leasing or renting any automotive vehicle or truck trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer for a period of 12 months or longer shall be at the rate of one-half percent of the gross proceeds derived by the lessor from the lease or rental of such automotive vehicle or truck trailer, semi-trailer or house trailer; provided further, that the fee levied in this division shall not apply to any leasing or rental, as lessor, by the State of Alabama, or any municipality or county in the State of Alabama, including without limiting the generality of the foregoing, any corporation organized under the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-54-80 through 11-54-101, as amended. 
( Ord. No. 2009-19, § 2, 7-13-2009 ) 
Sec. 66-233. - Monthly report and payment. 
    The fee levied under provision of this division shall be due and payable in monthly installments on or before the 20th day of the month next succeeding the month in which the fee accrues. On or before the twentieth day of each month, every person on whom the amounts levied by this division are imposed shall render to the city, on a form prescribed by the city, a true and correct statement showing the gross proceeds of such person's business, for the next preceding month the amount of gross receipts which are not subject to the fee or are not to be used as a measurement of the amounts due by such person, and the nature thereof, together with such other information as the city may require; and at the time of making such monthly report such person shall compute the fee due and shall pay to the city the amount shown to be due. 
( Ord. No. 2009-19, § 3, 7-13-2009 ) 
Sec. 66-234. - Reports of cash and credit card rentals. 
    Any person taxable under this division, making cash and credit leases or rentals, may if he desires, report such cash leases or rentals only, and he shall thereafter include in each monthly report all cash and credit collections made during the month preceding, and shall pay the privilege license tax due thereon at the time of filing such report. 
( Ord. No. 2009-19, § 4, 7-13-2009 ) 
Sec. 66-235. - Records. 
(a)  It shall be the duty of every person engaging in or continuing in any business for which a privilege is imposed by this division to keep and preserve suitable records of the gross proceeds of any such business and such other books or accounts as may be necessary to determine the amount of tax for which he is liable under the provisions of this division. It shall be the duty of every person to keep and preserve for a period of three years, all invoices of gross proceeds proceeding or accruing from the leasing or rental herein taxed; and all such books, invoices, and other records shall be open for examination at any time by the city clerk or his or her authorized representative. Any person leasing who in addition leases for re-leasing shall keep his books so as to show separately the gross proceeds of leasing and the gross proceeds of leasing for re-leasing. 
(b)  The books, records and accounts mentioned above shall at all times be open to examination by the city clerk or his or her authorized representative, upon request by the city clerk. Upon demand by the city clerk or his or her representative, it shall be the duty of any person subject to this license tax to submit to the city clerk or his or her authorized representative, for inspection and examination, during reasonable business hours, in the city, all books of account. Each occurrence of a failure to keep records, or allow examination thereof shall constitute a separate offense. 
( Ord. No. 2009-19, § 5, 7-13-2009 ) 
Sec. 66-236. - Penalty. 
    Any person subject to this division failing to pay the fee imposed herein, failing to render any report required hereby, willfully making a false statement of fact in the statement or return, failing to keep records required herein, refusing to permit examination of such records or violating any other provision of this division shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be punishable as provided in the Code of Ordinances of the City of Valley, Alabama. 
( Ord. No. 2009-19, § 6, 7-13-2009 ) 
Chapter 70 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Any ordinance or resolution not in conflict with such Code regulating traffic on specific streets or portions thereof or in areas of the city saved from repeal, § 1-15(10); junkyards, junked vehicles, § 30-31 et seq.; law enforcement, ch. 46; offenses and miscellaneous provisions, ch. 50; litter thrown by persons in vehicles, § 58-65; truck loads causing litter, § 58-66; placing handbills on vehicles, § 58-93; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 62. 
State Law reference- Ordinances to provide for public safety, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-1; power of city to regulate the standing and running of trains, automobiles, etc., Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-47-114, 32-5-1; local traffic control devices, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5-31; Alabama Rules of the Road Act, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-1 et seq.; uniform system of traffic control devices, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-30; magistrates, uniform traffic infractions, Alabama Rules of Judicial Administration, rules 18-20, Code of Ala. 1975, vol. 23A. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 70-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Authorized emergency vehicle means as provided in Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-1-1.1. 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 70-2. - Equipment used in investigations of case of driving under the influence. 
    The city police department shall utilize the Intoxilyzer 5000-564 unit, or any lawful acceptable replacement, in the investigation and prosecution of cases involving suspected driving under the influence as outlined in Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 32-5-190 et seq., 32-5A-194 et seq., 36-18-50 et seq. and any other applicable law, all under methods approved by the state department of forensic sciences currently in effect, or as may from time to time be amended. 
(Ord. No. 95-05, 2-27-1995) 
Cross reference- Alcoholic beverages, ch. 6. 
Sec. 70-3. - Tire protuberances prohibited; exceptions; penalty. 
(a)  No tire on a vehicle moved on the highways or roads within the city shall have on its periphery any block, stud, flange, cleat or spike or any other protuberances of any material other than rubber which project beyond the tread of the traction surface of the tire, except that it shall be permissible to use farm machinery with tires having protuberances which will not injure the highway and, except also, that it shall be permissible to use tire chains or metal studded or safety spike tires of reasonable proportions upon any vehicle when required for safety because of snow, rain or other conditions tending to cause a vehicle to slide or skid. Also, no vehicles with tires that are tracked or covered will be allowed on the streets of the city. 
(b)  Any violation of this section shall be punished as provided in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 82-08, §§ 1, 2, 5-24-1982) 
Sec. 70-4. - Unlawful vehicular use of private property; penalty. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person in the city or its police jurisdiction, to drive a motor vehicle across, through or over any private property for the purpose of avoiding any traffic control device lawfully in place, or for the purpose of using the private property solely as a means or way of travel from one public street or highway to another public street or highway. 
(b)  Any person violating this section shall be punished as provided in section 1-11, and shall be citable by the issuance of a uniform nontraffic violation. 
(Ord. No. 00-14, §§ 1, 2, 9-11-2000) 
Sec. 70-5. - Emergency vehicles. 
(a)  The driver of an authorized emergency vehicle, when responding to an emergency call or when in the pursuit of an actual or suspected violator of the law or when responding to but not upon returning from a fire alarm, may exercise the privileges set forth in this section, but subject to the conditions stated in this section. 
(b)  The driver of an authorized emergency vehicle may: 
(1)  Park or stand, irrespective of the provisions of this chapter; 
(2)  Proceed past a red or stop signal or stop sign, but only after slowing down as may be necessary for safe operation; 
(3)  Exceed the maximum speed limits so long as he does not endanger life or property; 
(4)  Disregard regulations governing direction of movement or turning in specified directions. 
(c)  The exemptions granted in this section to an authorized emergency vehicle shall apply only when such vehicle is making use of an audible signal meeting the requirements of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5-213 and visual requirements of any laws of this state requiring visual signals on emergency vehicles. 
(d)  Subsections (a)-(c) of this section shall not relieve the driver of an authorized emergency vehicle from the duty to drive with due regard for the safety of all persons, nor shall such provisions protect the driver from the consequences of his reckless disregard for the safety of others. 
(Ord. No. 87-01, § 3, 1-12-1987) 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-7. 
Sec. 70-6. - Disposition of repossessed property. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Motor vehicle means any automobile, truck, or motorcycle. 
(b)  Application of section. This section shall apply only to a motor vehicle that is collateral pursuant to a chattel mortgage or security agreement. 
(c)  Notification of police department. It shall be the duty of every person, firm, or corporation who intends to repossess a motor vehicle within the corporate limits of the city and police jurisdiction thereof, to notify the police department in person prior to the repossession of the vehicle and to further provide the police department with any information required including the make, model, color, vehicle identification and tag registration number of the vehicle, the name and address of the registered owner of the vehicle, the location of the vehicle where repossession is intended to take place, the name of the person presently in possession of the vehicle if different than the owner, and the name and address of the chattel mortgage holder on the vehicle. This information shall be provided upon a form which may be obtained from the police department. Once repossession or attempted repossession has taken place, it shall be the further duty of every person, firm or corporation who repossesses or attempts to repossess a motor vehicle within the city limits or police jurisdiction, to notify the police department in person within 30 minutes of repossession or attempted repossession that the repossession has been effected or that the repossession was not made. 
(d)  Penalty for violation of section. The failure or refusal to give the notification required in this section shall be a misdemeanor, and any person convicted thereof shall be punished as provided in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 91-02, 3-11-1991) 
Sec. 70-7. - Seizure and forfeiture of automobiles. 
(a)  The city council finds and declares all of the following: 
(1)  Driving a motor vehicle on the public streets and highways is a privilege, not a right. 
(2)  Of all drivers involved in fatal accidents, a driver with a suspended license is more likely to be involved in a fatal accident than a properly licensed driver. 
(3)  Alabamians who comply with the law are frequently victims of traffic accidents caused by unlicensed drivers. These innocent victims suffer considerable pain and property loss at the hands of people who flaunt the law. 
(4)  It is necessary and appropriate to take additional steps to prevent unlicensed drivers from driving. The city has a critical interest in enforcing its traffic laws and in keeping unlicensed drivers from illegally driving. Seizing the motor vehicles used by unlicensed drivers serves a significant governmental and public interest, namely the protection of the health, safety, and welfare of the citizens of the city from the harm of unlicensed drivers who are involved in a disproportionate number of traffic incidents, and the avoidance of the associated destruction and damage to lives and property. 
(5)  This section is consistent with the due process requirements of the United States Constitution and the holding of the Supreme Court of the United States in Calero-Toledo v. Pearson Yacht Leasing Co., 416 U.S. 663, 94 S. Ct. 2080, 40 L.Ed.2d 452 (1974). 
(b)  (1)  a. If a driver is unable to produce a valid driver's license on the demand of a law-enforcement officer, the motor vehicle is subject to impoundment regardless of ownership, unless the law-enforcement officer is reasonably able, by other means, to verify that the driver is properly licensed. Prior to impounding the motor vehicle, a law-enforcement officer shall make a reasonable attempt to verify the license status of a driver who claims to be properly licensed, but who is unable to produce the license on demand of the law-enforcement officer. A notation of the officer's attempt to verify that the driver is properly licensed shall be noted on the departmental report. The driver and occupants of the motor vehicle will be transported to a place of safety by the impounding officer or arrangements made for transportation, and a vehicle-impound report made with a full inventory of items in the motor vehicle. 
b.  A law-enforcement officer shall not impound a motor vehicle pursuant to this section if the license of the driver expired within the preceding 60 days and the driver would otherwise have been properly licensed. 
c.  If the owner of the motor vehicle or another family member of the owner is present in the motor vehicle and has a valid license, the motor vehicle shall not be impounded and towed. 
d.  If there is a medical necessity jeopardizing life or limb, the law-enforcement officer may elect not to impound the motor vehicle. 
e.  A law-enforcement officer who requests that a motor vehicle be towed onto the property of another pursuant to this section shall do so by using a vehicle impound report. 
(2)  A motor vehicle impounded pursuant to this section shall be released if the person redeeming the motor vehicle satisfies in full the fees provided for by subsection (d) and: 
a.  The registered owner appears at the Valley Police Department or a representative of the owner with written notarized authorization from the registered owner appears, and presents a valid driver's license and a copy of the written authorization, if applicable, to be copied by the Valley Police Department; 
b.  If the registered owner does not have a valid driver's license, he or she may bring someone with them who has a verified valid license and the motor vehicle may be released without written notarized permission; or 
c.  Upon order of a court of competent jurisdiction. 
(c)  Any owner of a motor vehicle (including a lien holder, person with a security interest in the motor vehicle, a lessor of the motor vehicle, assignee of the lessor, or the person who is the registered owner of the motor vehicle) who suffers any loss due to the impoundment of any motor vehicle pursuant to this section may recover the amount of the loss from the driver who was unable to produce a valid driver's license at the request of the law-enforcement officer. 
(d)  The person redeeming the motor vehicle from the automobile dealer, wrecker service owner, repair service owner, or person, firm, or governmental entity on whose property the motor vehicle was lawfully towed at the written request of a law-enforcement officer pursuant to this section will be responsible for paying the fees for the removal and any storage of the motor vehicle. 
(e)  If a motor vehicle impounded pursuant to this section is not redeemed or claimed pursuant to this section within 60 days of the date that it is impounded, then the automobile dealer, wrecker service or repair service owner, or any person, firm, or governmental entity on whose property the motor vehicle was lawfully towed at the written request of a law-enforcement officer pursuant to this section may sell the motor vehicle at public auction according to the state law governing abandoned motor vehicles in Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 32-13-1 through 32-13-8, as now exist or are hereafter amended. 
(f)  Information about any motor vehicle impounded pursuant to this section by a law-enforcement officer of the city, including the date of impoundment and the vehicle identification number, will be made publicly available on the city's web site by the Valley Police Department within five days after impoundment. This information will be made available to assist those with a legal interest in the motor vehicle, but the failure to post such notice will not make the impoundment unlawful. 
( Ord. No. 2007-40, 9-10-2007 ) 
Secs. 70-8-70-40. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - SPEED 

Sec. 70-41. - Limit in absence of signs or markers. 
    In the absence of signs or markers indicating a different speed limit, it shall be unlawful to operate any vehicle in the city at a rate of speed exceeding 25 miles per hour. 
(Ord. No. 87-01, § 1, 1-12-1987) 
Sec. 70-42. - Maximum or minimum limits; signs, signals or markings. 
    The city council may from time to time impose maximum or minimum speed limits applicable at specific locations or on specific streets or parts of streets, different from that set out in section 70-41. Signs, signals or markings shall be installed giving notice, and it shall be unlawful to exceed or violate the posted maximum or minimum speed, or fail to comply with such sign, signal or marking. 
(Ord. No. 87-01, § 2, 1-12-1987) 
Sec. 70-43. - Applicability of article provisions. 
    Limitation of speed imposed by this article shall not be applicable on highways or roads designated as U.S. highways, state highways or extensions, or county roads and for which the applicable authority has installed and maintains a sign or marker authorizing a different speed limit on such federal, state, or county highway or road. A violation of such posted speed limit shall be a violation of this article to the same extent as violation of the 25 mile speed limit imposed on all streets other than as excepted in this section. 
(Ord. No. 87-01, § 4, 1-12-1987) 
Sec. 70-44. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    A violation of this article shall be punished as provided for in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 87-01, § 5, 1-12-1987) 
Secs. 70-45-70-70. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PARKING LOTS 

Sec. 70-71. - Speed limit established. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to drive a vehicle in willful or wanton disregard for the safety of persons or property upon or within a parking lot, or to drive thereon or therein at a speed in excess of ten miles per hour. The chief of police is authorized to cause such signs as he may deem necessary to be erected on public rights-of-way, at or near one or more entrances to such lots stating the speed limit of ten miles per hour upon or in such lot. 
(Ord. No. 89-02, § 1, 6-12-1989) 
Sec. 70-72. - Unlawful vehicle operation. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to stop, park, drive or operate a vehicle upon any parking lot in any manner which unreasonably obstructs or hinders the free flow of pedestrian or vehicular traffic. 
(Ord. No. 89-02, § 2, 6-12-1989) 
Sec. 70-73. - Prohibited assembly or loitering. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person: 
(1)  Without permission from the owner of the property, to assemble with one or more other persons upon any public parking lot without having a legitimate reason for being there, after having been requested to leave the parking area by any law enforcement officer; or 
(2)  Without permission from the owner of the property, to loiter or remain in a public parking area for the purpose of socializing with one or more other persons, after having been requested to leave the parking area by any law enforcement officer. 
(Ord. No. 89-02, § 3, 6-12-1989) 
Sec. 70-74. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    A violation of this article shall be punished as provided in section 1-11. Any charge may be citable by the issuance of a uniform nontraffic citation. 
(Ord. No. 89-02, § 4, 6-12-1989; Ord. No. 99-10, 8-30-1999) 
Secs. 70-75-70-110. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - PARKING 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 70-111-70-130. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - RESIDENTIAL AREAS 

Sec. 70-131. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Residential area means any area designated as residential under the city's existing zoning ordinance as may from time to time be amended. 
(Ord. No. 00-01, § 1, 2-14-2000) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 70-132. - Prohibited parking. 
(a)  Parking of motor vehicles in residential areas is limited to passenger vehicles, and not more than one class B vehicle as defined by the U.S. Department of Transportation, per dwelling unit. Parking of all motor vehicles must conform to article 7, section 3.0 of the city's zoning ordinance, as may from time to time be amended. 
(b)  Parking of any class A type vehicle as defined by the U.S. Department of Transportation, as well as attachments, in any residential area, or on any city right-of-way or other public property is prohibited except for purposes of making a delivery or pickup. 
(Ord. No. 00-01, § 2, 2-14-2000) 
Sec. 70-133. - Penalty for violation of division. 
    Any person who violates any provision of this division shall be punished as provided in section 1-11, in addition to the cost of court, as may be assessed by a court of competent jurisdiction. 
(Ord. No. 00-01, § 3, 2-14-2000) 
Secs. 70-134-70-150. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - NO PARKING ZONES 

Sec. 70-151. - Enumerated. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to park a vehicle along designated portions of: 
(1)  Frazier Street and Pine Street; 
(2)  South 54th Street between 20th Avenue and 21st Avenue. 
The chief of police is authorized to establish the areas of restricted parking and to erect such signs as he may deem necessary along the restricted portions of these public rights-of-way upon which parking is prohibited. 
(Ord. No. 94-17, § 1, 8-22-1994; Ord. No. 94-22, § 1, 10-24-1994) 
Sec. 70-152. - Fire lanes. 
(a)  Prohibited acts. It shall be unlawful for any person to stop a vehicle or park a vehicle in a designated fire lane. The chief of police is authorized to designate fire lanes upon which parking shall be prohibited and shall supervise the designation of such restrictions or the erection of signs by property owners adjoining the restricted areas. 
(b)  Applicability of section provisions. This section shall not apply to any authorized emergency vehicle or the personnel of any such vehicle. 
(c)  Towing. Any vehicle found to be in violation of the provisions of this section shall be subject to being towed away by law enforcement officials, with the owner and/or driver of the vehicle being liable for the reasonable cost of towing. In order to obtain possession of any towed vehicle the owner shall be required to pay the outstanding costs for towing. 
(Ord. No. 94-17, §§ 2, 3, 8-22-1994; Ord. No. 94-18, §§ 1-3, 8-22-1994; Ord. No. 94-22, §§ 2, 3, 10-24-1994) 
Cross reference- Fire prevention and protection, ch. 34. 
Sec. 70-153. - Charging of violations. 
    The traffic citation of the form known as the uniform traffic ticket and complaint shall not be used to charge violations of this division. Such violations shall be charged as provided in Alabama Rules of Judicial Administration, rule 19(B), Code of Ala. 1975, vol. 23A. 
(Ord. No. 94-17, § 4, 8-22-1994; Ord. No. 94-18, § 4, 8-22-1994; Ord. No. 94-22, § 4, 10-24-1994; Ord. No. 99-122, 8-30-1999; Ord. No. 99-13, 8-30-1999) 
Sec. 70-154. - Penalty for violation of division. 
    Violations of this division shall be punished as provided in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 94-17, § 4, 8-22-1994; Ord. No. 94-18, § 4, 8-22-1994; Ord. No. 94-22, § 4, 10-24-1994; Ord. No. 99-12, § 4, 8-30-1999) 
Secs. 70-155-70-170. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - TRUCK ROUTES 

Sec. 70-171. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Implement of husbandry. Every vehicle designed and adapted exclusively for agricultural, horticultural, or livestock operations or for lifting or carrying an implement of husbandry and in either case not subject to registration if used upon the highways. 
    Person. Every natural person, firm co partnership, association or corporation. 
    Roadway. That portion of a highway improved, designed or ordinarily used for vehicular travel, exclusive of the berm or the shoulder. In the event a highway includes two or more separate roadways the term "roadway" as used herein shall refer to any roadway separately but not to all such roadways collectively. 
    Semitrailer. Every vehicle with or without motive power, other than a pole trailer, designed for carrying persons or property and for being drawn by a motor vehicle and so constructed that some part of its weight and that of its load rests upon or is carried by another vehicle. 
    Trailer. Every vehicle with or without motive power, other than a pole trailer, designed for carrying persons or property and for being drawn by a motor vehicle and so constructed that no part of its weight and that of its load rests upon the towing vehicle. 
    Truck. Every motor vehicle designed, used or maintained primarily fro the transportation of property. 
    Truck tractor. Every motor vehicle designed and used primarily for drawing other vehicles and not so constructed as to carry a load other than a part of the weight of the vehicle and load so drawn. 
( Ord. No. 2007-23, § 1, 6-11-2007 ) 
Sec. 70-172. - Rule of construction. 
    Any word or term not defined herein shall be considered to be defined in accordance with its common or standard definition. 
(Ord. No. 2007-23, § 2, 6-11-2007 ) 
Sec. 70-173. - Truck routes. 
    The following roadways in the City of Valley, Alabama, are hereby designated as truck routes and classified for truck traffic: 
(1)  Fob James Drive. 
(2)  Fairfax Bypass. 
( Ord. No. 2007-23, § 3, 6-11-2007 ) 
Sec. 70-174. - Prohibition against travel on other than truck routes. 
    Except as expressly permitted under this ordinance, no person shall operate a truck or truck-tractor and trailer combination in the City of Valley, Alabama, on any roadway other than a designated truck route. 
( Ord. No. 2007-23, § 4, 6-11-2007 ) 
Sec. 70-175. - Exemptions. 
    The truck route limitations prescribed in this article shall not apply to: 
(1)  Fire trucks or other emergency vehicles or vehicle on emergency business involved in the saving of life or property; or 
(2)  Implements of husbandry incidentally moved upon a roadway; or 
(3)  Road repair, construction or maintenance vehicles while involved in the repair, construction or maintenance of roadways within the city; or 
(4)  Garbage service vehicles while involved in the provision of services to residents of the city. 
( Ord. No. 2007-23, § 5, 6-11-2007 ) 
Sec. 70-176. - Pick-ups, deliveries, service calls. 
    A vehicle that would otherwise be restricted to truck routes and which is being used to make pick-ups, deliveries or service calls in the city on roadways other than designated truck routes shall restrict its travel to a minimum and shall not be driven or moved on other than truck routes except when being used to make pick-ups, deliveries or service calls within the city. Said vehicle shall be driven in such a manner as to leave a permitted truck route and proceed to its destination or destinations in the city by the most direct route. Upon completion of the pick-ups, deliveries or service calls, the vehicle shall return to the nearest permitted truck route or leave the city by the most direct route. This section shall not be interpreted as permitting a vehicle otherwise restricted to a truck route from entering or leaving the city by other than a truck route. 
( Ord. No. 2007-23, § 6, 6-11-2007 ) 
Sec. 70-177. - Leaving or returning to home or place of business. 
    Nothing herein contained shall prevent a truck or truck-tractor and semi-trailer, or truck tractor and trailer combination, or truck and trailer combination from leaving or returning to its customary lawful storage location at the owner or operator's personal residence, or a commercial or industrial location within the city, provided the most direct route to and from a designated truck route is utilized. 
( Ord. No. 2007-23, § 7, 6-11-2007 ) 
Sec. 70-178. - Special permits. 
    The Valley City Council shall have authority to grant a written permit in special cases that would otherwise be in violation of the provisions of this ordinance. Such permits, however, shall not be valid for a longer period than ten days from the date of issue. Said permit shall describe the vehicle, the time and dates of travel, and the route to be taken by the vehicle. The city shall, by resolution, set the fee for special permits at $100.00 per application. Non-refundable. 
( Ord. No. 2007-23, § 8, 6-11-2007 ) 
Sec. 70-179. - Signs. 
    The Valley City Council shall procure and have posted appropriate signs along the designated truck routes as required by the laws of the State of Alabama. 
( Ord. No. 2007-23, § 9, 6-11-2007 ) 
Sec. 70-180. - Penalties. 
    Any person who violates any provision of this article shall be guilty of an offense against the city and such penalty upon conviction shall be in accordance with section 1-11 of the Code of Ordinances, at the discretion of the court. 
( Ord. No. 2007-23, § 10, 6-11-2007 ) 
Sec. 70-181. - Administrative liability. 
    No officer, agent, or employee of the City of Valley, or member of the Valley City Council shall render him/herself personally liable for any damage that may accrue to any person as a result of any act, decision, or other consequence or occurrence arising out of the discharge of his/her duties and responsibilities pursuant to this article. 
( Ord. No. 2007-23, § 12, 6-11-2007 ) 
Sec. 70-182. - Designation and marking of truck routes. 
    The chief of police may designate streets as truck routes through the city and shall cause suitable signs to be erected indicating such designated routes, which signs may also warn the operators of trucks to remain on marked truck routes through the city. 
    These marked routes shall apply to and govern the movement through the city of all trucks or motor vehicles set forth in Code of Ala., 1975, § 32-9-20, reference to which is hereby made. 
( Ord. No. 2014-08, § 1, 4-14-2014 ) 
Chapter 74 - UTILITIES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2; buildings and building regulations, ch. 14; businesses, ch. 18; environment, ch. 30; floods, ch. 38; historic preservation, ch. 42; planning, ch. 54; solid waste, ch. 58; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 62; tree management over utilities, § 78-38. 
State Law reference- Contracts and indebtedness for waterworks systems, consolidation with lighting systems, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-3; public improvements and assessments generally, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-48-1 et seq.; public utilities in municipalities, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-50-1 et seq.; boards for operation of water, sewer, gas and electric systems, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-50-310 et seq.; boards of water and sewer commissioners, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-5-340 et seq.; revenue bonds for waterworks, gas, sewer or electric systems, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-81-160 et seq.; water pollution control, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-22-1 et seq.; environmental management, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-22A-1 et seq.; waterworks and water supplies generally, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-23-20 et seq.; public utilities generally, Code of Ala. 1975, tit. 37. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 74-1-74-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - CONNECTIONS; INITIATION OF SERVICE 

Sec. 74-31. - Definitions.
